Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Mu'tazilite Classification of Voluntary Acts and the Five Hukm Categories
Explains Mu'tazilite division of acts and derivation of five shari rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Mu'tazilite division of voluntary acts into five rational rulings and identify the logical proof for the limitation.

Core Idea
Reason alone, for Mu'tazila, determines five moral categories for voluntary acts before revelation.

This passage from Sharh Muslim al-Thubut explains the Mu'tazilite approach to ethics: they held that the moral quality of certain acts can be known by reason. They classified voluntary acts into those whose good or evil can be rationally perceived and those that cannot. For the first type, reason assigns one of five rulings: wajib, haram, makruh, mandub, and mubah. The author then provides a logical proof that these five categories are exhaustive. Understanding this rationalist framework is essential for comparing with the Ash'ari-Hanafi position that rulings come only from revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main divisions of acts
The passage first divides all acts into voluntary (اختيارية) and involuntary. Then voluntary acts are divided into those whose moral quality reason can perceive and those it cannot.
The focus of the lesson is on the first type, where reason can perceive good and evil.
2
List the five categories derived by reason
Reason perceives strong good (wajib), strong evil (haram), weak evil (makruh), weak good (mandub), and equal not calling for reward/punishment (mubah). Each is defined by whether acting or leaving entails reward/punishment.
Note that the categories are based on the strength of the perceived good or evil and the consequence of leaving or doing.
3
Trace the logical proof (دليل حصر) for the limitation to five
The proof considers two properties: evil and good. For act and leave, either both contain evil, only one contains good, or none. Each combination yields one of the five rulings, showing that no other category exists.
This is a classical Mantiq-style exhaustive division, ensuring completeness of the categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اما المعتزلة فقسموا الافعال الاختيارية وهى الخ خیال رہے کہ معتزلہ کے نزدیک قبل ورود شرع بندہ کے افعال دو طرح کے کہلاتے ہیں، افعال اختیاریه، افعال غیر اختیاریه، افعال اختیار یہ وہ فعل کہلاتا ہے جس کے بغیر تعیش و بقا ممکن ہو جیسے اکل فواکہہ ان علاقوں میں جہاں بطور تفریح طبع فواکہ واثمار کا استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ اور افعال اختیار یہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں ایک وہ افعال اختیار یہ جس کے حسن و فتح کے طرق کو عقل اور اک کر لیتی ہے دوسری قسم وہ افعال اختیار یہ جس کے حسن و فتح کے طرق کو عقل ادراک نہیں کر سکتی ہے پھر قسم اول (یعنی جس میں جہت حسن و فتح کو بذریعہ عقل اور اک کیا جاسکتا ہے ) تو اس کی مشہور پانچ قسمیں ہیں، واجب، حرام، مکروہ ، مندوب اور مباح پس عقل نے فعل میں اگر جہت محسنہ قویہ کا ادراک کیا ایسا حسن قوی کہ اس کا ترک فتح اور ذم و عقاب کا باعث ہے تو وہ فعل واجب ہے اس کے برخلاف اگر جہت مقبحہ قویہ کا ادراک کیا ایسا فتح شدید کہ اسکا ارتکاب باعث عقاب اور ترک باعث اجر و ثواب ہے تو وہ حرام ہے۔ البتہ اگر عقل نے فتح ضعیف کا ادراک کیا ایسا ضعف کہ فعل باعث عقاب نہیں ہے لیکن اس کا ترک فعل کے بہ نسبت اولی ہے تو وہ مکروہ ہے اور اگر عقل نے جہت محسنہ ضعیفہ کا ادراک کیا ایسا حسن ضعیف کہ اسکا کرنا باعث ثواب ہے لیکن ترک سبب عقاب نہیں تو وہ مندوب ہے اور اگر فعل و ترک دونوں جہتیں ثواب و عقاب کی طرف مستدعی نہ ہونے میں مساوی ہیں تو وہ مباح ہے۔
دليل حصر: اقسام خمسہ مشہورہ کے پانچ قسموں میں محصور ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ وہ افعال نہیں خالی ہیں کہ ان کے دونوں طرف یعنی فعل و ترک یا تو قبح پر مشتمل ہونگے یا نہیں ، شق اول پر (یعنی فعل و ترک دونوں فتح پر مشتمل ہے ) اگر فعل فتح پر مشتمل ہے تو محرمہ ہے اور اگر ترک فتح پر مشتمل ہے تو واجبہ ہے اور شق ثانی ( یعنی فعل و ترک فتح پر مشتمل نہیں ہے) کی تقدیر پر یا تو دونوں میں سے کوئی ایک حسن پر مشتمل ہوگا یا نہیں اگر حسن پر مشتمل ہے تو یہ مندوب ہے اور اگر ترک حسن پر مشتمل ہے تو یہ مکروہ ہے اور اگر فعل و ترک میں سے کوئی حسن پر مشتمل نہیں ہے تو یہ مباح ہے۔
As for the Mu'tazila, they divided voluntary acts... and there are two types: one whose ways of good and evil reason can grasp, and another whose ways reason cannot grasp. Then the first type has five well-known categories: wajib, haram, makruh, mandub, mubah. So if reason perceives a strong good aspect such that leaving it necessitates evil and blame and punishment, that act is wajib. Conversely, if it perceives a strong evil aspect such that committing it causes punishment and leaving it causes reward, that is haram. If it perceives a weak evil such that the act is not punishable but leaving it is preferable, that is makruh. If it perceives a weak good such that doing it is rewardable but leaving it is not punishable, that is mandub. If both acting and leaving are equal in not calling for reward or punishment, that is mubah. Proof of limitation: The five categories are limited to five because acts are not free from having both sides (act and leave) either containing evil or not. If both contain evil, then if act contains evil it is haram, if leave contains evil it is wajib. If neither contains evil, then either one contains good or not. If act contains good it is mandub, if leave contains good it is makruh. If neither contains good it is mubah.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite classification of acts before revelation. It divides acts into voluntary (اختيارية) and involuntary. Voluntary acts are further divided into two types: those whose moral quality (good/evil) can be rationally perceived, and those that cannot. For the first type, reason alone can determine the ruling, leading to five categories: wajib (strong good with punishment for leaving), haram (strong evil with punishment for committing), makruh (weak evil with preference to leave), mandub (weak good with reward for doing), and mubah (no reward or punishment for either). The author then provides a logical proof (دليل حصر) that these five are exhaustive, based on considering the presence or absence of evil/good in acting and leaving. This is a rationalist approach to ethics, typical of Mu'tazila, but the Hanafi position differs by requiring divine revelation for rulings. However, this passage is explaining the Mu'tazilite view as part of a broader discussion.

Key Terms
فعل اختياري (fi'l ikhtiyari): An act whose performance or omission is within human free will, distinct from involuntary acts.
حسن وقبح عقلي (husn wa qubh 'aqli): Rational perception of good and evil in an act independently of revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilite classification, what ruling applies to an act whose performance contains a strong good aspect and leaving it brings punishment?
A) Wajib
B) Haram
C) Mandub
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite rational classification of acts into five categories based on perceived good and evil is a foundational alternative to the revelatory approach of Hanafi usul.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Logical Defense of Ibaḥah and Ḥaẓr against the Objection of Contradictory Rulings
Rebuttal of the objection that Ibahah/Hazr leads to contradictory rulings on the same act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the objection of contradictory rulings against the positions of Ibaḥah and Ḥaẓr, and articulate the two Hanafi uṣūlī responses: the distinction of perspectives (nafs al-amr vs. za‘m) and the analogy between the summary ruling (ḥukm ijmālī) and ijtihādī rulings.

Core Idea
An act can be assigned contradictory rulings from different perspectives without logical contradiction.

This lesson examines a sophisticated logical objection raised against the two foundational uṣūlī views on original permissibility (ibāḥah) and original prohibition (ḥaẓr). The objection claims that if one holds either view, a single act could bear two contradictory rulings in actual reality, which is impossible. You will see how the Hanafi commentators defend both positions by distinguishing between actual reality and human estimation, and by comparing the summary ruling to an ijtihādī ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Read the objection as presented: if we accept original ibāḥah or ḥaẓr, then for an act whose specific ruling is unknown, we might assign it a ruling while in actual reality it may have a different ruling, leading to two contradictory rulings on the same act.
The objection is logical, not textual.
2
Recognize the Failed Defense
Note why the initial attempt to deflect by distinguishing between summary (ijmālī) and detailed (tafṣīlī) rulings is insufficient: the contradiction lies in the locus (the act itself), not in the cause of knowledge.
This shows the need for a more nuanced defense.
3
Understand the First Response (fa-ta’ammal)
The commentator indicates that the two rulings apply from different aspects: one in actual reality (nafs al-amr) and the other in the estimation (za‘m) of the proponents. From one aspect alone, there is no conjunction. Additionally, ibāḥah as 'absence of restriction' does not truly contradict wujūb.
This response focuses on the perspective of description.
4
Understand the Second Response (Analogous to Ijtihād)
The second response compares the summary ruling (ḥukm ijmālī) to an ijtihādī ruling. Just as a mujtahid's ruling is binding even if it differs from the actual divine ruling, so too the summary ruling of ibāḥah or ḥaẓr is temporarily binding until specific evidence arrives, allowing the act to be described with both rulings without impossibility.
This response justifies the practical validity of the summary ruling.
5
Synthesize the Outcome
Conclude that the objection does not refute the positions of ibāḥah and ḥaẓr; rather, it highlights the need to carefully distinguish between perspectives and the temporary nature of summary rulings.
The objection is based on a misunderstanding of how rulings relate to acts.

Source Text

اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم التبوت
۲۸۷
کبری کی طرف اجمالاً معلوم ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ نتیجہ کبری میں کلیہ ہو نے کی وجہ سے شامل ہے چنانچہ العالم متغير وكل متغیر حادث، کی ہیئت قیاسیہ سے جو نتیجہ العالم حادث حاصل ہوتا ہے وہ پہلے ہی ہمارے قول کل متغیر حادث سے اجمالا معلوم ہو چکا ہے اس لئے کہ العالم حادث کل متغیر حادث کا ایک فرد ہے۔
قوله اقول يرد عليهما انه يلزم جواز اتصاف
اس عبارت سے ماتن کہنا چاہتے ہیں کہ قول اباحت وقول حظر پر اعتراض مذکور تو وارد نہ ہوگا البته قائلین اباحت و نظر پر دوسری جہت سے اعتراض اجتماع نقیضین لازم آئیگا اور اس کے جواب میں اجمال و تفصیل کا فرق نفع بخش نہ ہوگا۔
اعتراض: اجتماع متنافسین اس طرح لازم آئیگا کہ اصل اباحت واصل حظر کے قول کو ماننے کی تقدیر پر فعل واحد کا دو حکم متضاد کے ساتھ انصاف کا جواز لازم آتا ہے یعنی نفس الامر میں فعل واحد کا دو حکم مثلا و جوب و حرمت یا وجوب واباحت کے ساتھ متصف ہونا جائز ہو جائے گا۔ بایں طور کہ یہ فرض کیا گیا ہے کہ کسی خاص فعل میں اس کی جہت خاص کے عدم علم کے سبب اس فعل کا حکم معلوم نہیں ہے پس اس صورت میں ایسا ممکن ہے کہ اس فعل کے لئے نفس الامر اور خارج میں مثلاً ایک حکم وجوب ثابت ہو پھر اہل اباحت واہل نظر اس میں مزید حکم اباحت یا حکم حرمت مثلا ثابت کریں ۔ تو اس طرح نفس الامر میں فعل واحد کے ساتھ دو حکم حکم وجوب و حکم اباحت یا حکم وجوب و حکم حرمت دونوں مجتمع ہو جائیں گے یہی اجتماع نقیضین ہے کہ وجوب واباحت یا وجوب و حرمت متناقض ہیں اور اجتماع نقیضین محال لہذا حکم اباحت و حرمت محال ٹھہرا۔
رہا اس اعتراض کے دفع کے لئے اجمال و تفصیل کا فرق دکھانا تو یہ نافع نہیں کیونکہ علت کا اختلاف تناقض کو ختم نہیں کرے گا اس لئے کہ اجمال و تفصیل کا فرق معرفت حکم کی علت میں ہے نہ کہ محل حکم (فعل) میں ۔ چونکہ یہاں نفس فعل جو کل حکم ہے میں حکم متضاد ین یعنی وجوب و حرمت یا وجوب وا باحت کا اجتماع لازم آ رہا ہے، حکم کی علت میں نہیں کہ اجمال و تفصیل کا فرق دکھا کر اجتماع متنا فین ختم کیا جائے۔

اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
۲۸۸
قوله فتأمل : سے غالبا جواب کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ یہاں نفس الامر میں دو متضاد حکم کے ساتھ فعل واحد کا انصاف لازم نہیں آرہا ہے ہاں زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ لازم آئے گا کر فعل میں دو حکم ہے ایک حکم نفس الامر میں دوسرا حکم اہل اباحت اہل نظر کے زعم میں نہ کہ نفس الامر میں غرض محل واحد (فعل) میں دو حکم متضاد کا اتصاف دوحیثیت سے ہے ایک جہت نفس الامری دوسری حیثیت زعم اہل اباحت واہل نظر ۔ ایک جہت سے اجتماع نہیں کہ اجتماع متنافین لازم آئے علاوہ ازیں اباحت عدم حرج کے معنی میں ہے اور عدم الحرج اور وجوب کے مابین منافات نہیں ہے اور یہ ظاہر ہے چنانچہ اس مقام پر مصنف نے حاشیہ میں کہا ہے۔
اشارة الى أن مبنى الاعتراض على زعم اهل المذهبين وهو العلم بالحكم وعدم العلم بالحكم المخصوص في نظر الشارع نظرا الى خصوصية الفعل، ويمكن أن يجاب بأن الحكم الاجمالي موقت الى ورود الشرع بالخصوص فكان كالاجتهاد فهناك يجب العمل به الى ظهور الصواب مع اتصاف الفعل بالحكمين - انتهت - ال ماليات .
قوله فى الحاشيه اشارة إلى أن... الى خصوصية الفعل
اس کے قول فنامل کے ذیل میں شرح ہو چکی ہے
قوله فى الحاشيه ويمكن أن يجاب.
یعنی اجتماع متنافین کا یہ بھی جواب ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہ حکم اجمالی ( یعنی حکم اباحت یا حکم حظر قول کرنا کسی فعل میں اجتھاد سے حکم کرنے کی طرح ہے یعنی جس طرح کسی فعل میں ایک حکم اجتھادی ہوتا ہے حالانکہ ایسا ممکن ہے کہ اس فعل میں عند اللہ کوئی دوسرا حکم ہو لیکن پھر بھی اس حکم اجتھادی پر عمل کرنا واجب ہے پس اسی طرح حکم اجمالی اباحت یا خطر ہے پھر بھی عمل کرنا واجب ہے اگر چہ نفس الامر میں اسکا کوئی دوسرا حکم ہوں۔ الحاصل فعل دو حکم متضاد کے ساتھ متصف ہونے کے باوجود ممنوع نہیں ہے جیسے کسی مسئلہ کا حکم اجتھادی و حکم نفس الامری ممنوع نہیں ۔
Ashraf al-Nu‘ut Sharḥ Musallam al-Thubūt 287. The major premise is known in summary because the result is included in the major due to its universality. For example, from the syllogistic form 'The world is changing and everything changing is created', the result 'the world is created' was already known in summary from our statement 'everything changing is created' because 'the world is created' is an individual of 'everything changing is created'. His saying: 'I say, it is objected to them that it necessitates the possibility of being described...' By this expression the author means that the mentioned objection does not apply to the statement of Ibaḥah and the statement of Ḥaẓr; however, upon the proponents of Ibaḥah and Ḥaẓr from another direction the objection of the conjunction of two contradictories becomes necessary, and in its answer the distinction between summary and detail will not be beneficial. The objection: The conjunction of contradictories becomes necessary in this manner: upon the assumption of accepting the statement of original Ibaḥah and original Ḥaẓr, the permissibility of attributing two contradictory rulings to a single act becomes necessary — that is, in actual reality, it would be permissible for a single act to be described with two rulings, for example obligation and prohibition, or obligation and permissibility. In this way, it is assumed that in some specific act, due to lack of knowledge of its specific aspect, the ruling of that act is not known. So in such a case, it is possible that in actual reality and externally, for example, one ruling of obligation is established for that act, then the proponents of Ibaḥah and the proponents of Ḥaẓr establish an additional ruling of permissibility or prohibition for it. Thus, in actual reality, two rulings — ruling of obligation and ruling of permissibility, or ruling of obligation and ruling of prohibition — will both be combined for a single act. This is the conjunction of two contradictories, because obligation and permissibility or obligation and prohibition are contradictory, and the conjunction of contradictories is impossible. Therefore, the rulings of permissibility and prohibition are impossible. As for showing the distinction between summary and detail to repel this objection, it is not beneficial because the difference in cause does not eliminate contradiction. This is because the distinction between summary and detail is in the cause of knowledge of the ruling, not in the locus of the ruling (the act). Since here the conjunction of contradictory rulings — i.e., obligation and prohibition or obligation and permissibility — becomes necessary in the very act, which is the locus of the ruling, not in the cause of the ruling, so that by showing the distinction between summary and detail the conjunction of contradictories could be ended. Scanned by CamScanner. Ashraf al-Nu‘ut Sharḥ Musallam al-Thubūt 288. His saying: 'Then consider' (fa-ta’ammal) generally indicates the answer: that here in actual reality, the description of a single act with two contradictory rulings is not necessary. At most, what becomes necessary is that the act has two rulings: one ruling in actual reality, and the second ruling in the estimation of the proponents of Ibaḥah and the proponents of Ḥaẓr, not in actual reality. That is, the description of a single locus (the act) with two contradictory rulings is from two aspects: one aspect of actual reality, the second aspect of the estimation of the proponents of Ibaḥah and Ḥaẓr. From one aspect there is no conjunction such that the conjunction of contradictories becomes necessary. Moreover, Ibaḥah is in the meaning of absence of restriction (adam al-ḥaraj), and between absence of restriction and obligation there is no opposition, and this is clear. Accordingly, at this point the author said in the margin: 'An indication that the basis of the objection is upon the estimation of the adherents of the two schools, which is knowledge of the ruling and lack of knowledge of the specific ruling in the view of the Lawgiver with regard to the specificity of the act. And it can be answered that the summary ruling is temporary until the specific Law comes, so it is like ijtihad; thus, it is obligatory to act upon it until the correct appears, despite the act being described with two rulings — end.' His saying in the margin: 'Indication that... to the specificity of the act' — its explanation has already come under his saying 'fa-ta’ammal'. His saying in the margin: 'And it can be answered' – i.e., this also can be an answer to the conjunction of contradictories: that this summary ruling (i.e., the statement of the ruling of Ibaḥah or Ḥaẓr regarding an act) is like ruling by ijtihad. Just as an act has an ijtihadi ruling, although it is possible that there is another ruling for that act with Allah, yet acting upon that ijtihadi ruling is obligatory; similarly, the summary ruling of Ibaḥah or Ḥaẓr is such that acting upon it is obligatory, even if there is another ruling for it in actual reality. In conclusion, an act being described with two contradictory rulings is not prohibited, just as the ijtihadi ruling and the actual reality ruling of a matter are not prohibited.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on an objection and rebuttal concerning the views of Ibaḥah (original permissibility) and Ḥaẓr (original prohibition) in uṣūl al-fiqh. The objection claims that if one adopts either view, a single act could have two contradictory rulings (e.g., wajib and mubah, or wajib and haram) simultaneously in actual reality, which is logically impossible. The commentator explains that this objection does not directly attack the positions themselves but raises a logical problem. The first attempted defense—distinguishing between summary (ijmālī) and detailed (tafṣīlī) rulings—fails because the contradiction lies in the act itself, not in the cause of knowledge. The author then provides two responses, hinted at by the phrase 'fa-ta’ammal' (then consider). First, the two contradictory rulings apply from different perspectives: one in actual reality, the other in the estimation of the claimants. Moreover, Ibaḥah as 'absence of restriction' does not truly contradict obligation. Second, from the marginal note, the summary ruling is temporary like an ijtihadi ruling; it is binding until the specific divine ruling is revealed, even if it differs from the actual reality. Hence, the conjunction of two rulings is not inherently impossible. The commentary stays within the text, explaining each step of the argument without introducing external sources.

Key Terms
اباحت (ibāḥah): The ruling of permissibility; in this context, the view that acts are originally permissible (al-ibāḥah al-aṣliyyah).
حظر (ḥaẓr): The ruling of prohibition; in this context, the view that acts are originally prohibited (al-ḥaẓr al-aṣlī).
اجمال (ijmāl): Summary; a general or undetailed ruling, as opposed to tafṣīl.
تفصيل (tafṣīl): Detail; a specific or elaborated ruling.
نفس الامر (nafs al-amr): Actual reality; the true ruling in the sight of Allah, as opposed to human estimation.
حكم اجمالي (ḥukm ijmālī): A summary ruling, which is temporary and based on general evidence until a specific evidence arrives.
حكم اجتهادي (ḥukm ijtihādī): A ruling derived through ijtihad, which is binding for the mujtahid even if it differs from the actual reality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the objection of contradictory rulings not refute the views of Ibaḥah and Ḥaẓr?
A) Because the two rulings apply from different perspectives (actual reality and estimation).
B) Because the rulings are only hypothetical and never actual.
C) Because the objection is based on a misunderstanding of Ijtihad.
D) Because the original permissibility and prohibition have no rulings.

Key Takeaway
The positions of original permissibility and prohibition are not invalidated by the logical objection of contradictory rulings because the two rulings apply from different perspectives and the summary ruling is analogous to an ijtihādī ruling.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Tawaqquf and the Possibility of Summary Ruling
Third Mu'tazili view on pre-revelation acts and a critique

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Mu'tazili position of tawaqquf on pre-revelation acts and explain why the Hanafi objection refutes it by distinguishing between specific and summary rulings.

Core Idea
Summary knowledge of a ruling is possible even if the specific ruling is unknown, so suspension is unnecessary.

Before revelation, what is the ruling on voluntary acts? The Mu'tazila debated three views; the third is tawaqquf (suspension). Some Hanafis and others also adopted this view, but the text presents a key objection: while the specific ruling may be unknown, a summary ruling (like permissibility) can be derived from general principles. This lesson unpacks the dispute and its implications for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the position of tawaqquf
Understand what tawaqquf means: either no ruling exists or the specific ruling is unknown. The proponents argue that since revelation has not come and reason cannot determine the specific ruling, we must suspend judgment.
Proponents include some Mu'tazila, al-Maturidi, al-Ash'ari, and even some Companions.
2
Examine the rationale for tawaqquf
The proponents' reason: one of the five rulings must apply, but we do not know which, so suspension is the safe course (al-tawaqquf asl al-taqwa).
This is a rational (aqli) argument based on ignorance of the specific.
3
Analyze the objection to tawaqquf
The matn objects that not knowing the specific ruling does not negate all knowledge. A summary ruling (hukm ijmali) can be known from a general principle (qā'ida kulliyya).
The objection distinguishes between hukm mu'ayyan and hukm ijmali.
4
Apply the distinction
If a summary ruling (e.g., permissibility) is possible, absolute suspension is unwarranted. The act may be governed by a general rule even if its specific category is unknown.
This is the Hanafi usul view: we can have practical guidance before revelation.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in fiqh, when facing a novel issue not addressed by revelation, Hanafi usul allows presuming permissibility (ibaha asliyya) rather than suspending judgment.
This affects ijtihad in new matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله " الثالث التوقف لان ثمه حكما معينا من الخ اس عبارت سے افعال اختیاریہ کی دوسری قسم میں معتزلہ کے تین اقوال میں سے تیسرے اور آخری قول کا ذکر ہے۔ اور وہ ہے تو قف۔ اور توقف کا معنی یہ ہے کہ یہاں حکم معدوم ہے یا حکم معین معلوم نہیں ہے چنانچہ قاضی بیضاوی اور علامہ ابن حاجب وغیرھما علمائے اصول نے یہی معنی بیان کئے ہیں ۔ البتہ بعض علماء نے فرمایا ہے کہ " قبل ورود شرع کسی فعل کے کرنے پر ثواب و عقاب کا مستحق نہ ہونا توقف کا معنی ہے یہ معنی حضرت شیخ ابو منصور ماتریدی کی طرف منسوب ہے بلکہ معتزلہ کے علاوہ بہت سے علماء حق بھی اس طرف گئے ہیں۔ جیسے ابو منصور ماتریدی صاحب ہدایہ برهان الدین مرغینانی اہل حدیث وغیرہ ابن امیر حاج نے تقریر میں کہا ہے کہ یہی مذہب شیخ ابوالحسن اشعری ابوبکر صیر فی شافعی کا ہے بلکہ اکثر شافعیہ کا یہی رجحان ہے جیسا کہ عبد العزیز بن احمد بن محمد بخاری نے کشف البز دوی میں کہا ہے یہاں تک کہا گیا ہے کہ یہی مذہب اہلسنت ہے حتی کہ صحابہ میں حضرت ابوبکر ، حضرت عمر، اور حضرت عثمان غنی رضی اللہ مسلم و غیر ھم کا بھی یہی مذہب تھا۔
وجہ تو قف : - اصحاب توقف نے اس کی وجہ بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے کہ اس جگہ احکام خمسہ مشہورہ میں سے کوئی حکم بالضرور ہے مگر چونکہ شریعت وارد نہیں ہوئی نہ ہی اس کی معرفت میں عقل کو دخل ہے اس لئے ہم نہیں جانتے کہ ان احکام میں سے کونسا حکم یہاں پر واقع ہے لہذا ہم نے توقف کا قول کیا کہ امر مسکوت عنہ میں تو قف ہی اصل تقویٰ ہے۔
قوله اقول هذا يقتضى الوقف فى الخصوصية ولاينا في الخ اس عبارت سے ماتن نے اہل توقف کے قول پر اعتراض کیا ہے کہ اس جگہ احکام خمسہ میں سے ایک حکم معین کا ہونا اور اس حکم معین کے وقوع کا علم نہ ہونا زیادہ سے زیادہ اسبات کو متقاضی ہے کہ کسی خاص فعل کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے حکم کا علم نہیں ہو سکا ہے یہ اسبات کا مقتضی نہیں ہے کہ قاعدہ کلیہ سے حکم کا مطلقا علم ہی نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ کسی خاص فعل کے حکم کا عدم علم، اس فعل کے حکم اجمالی کے علم کے منافی نہیں ہے چنانچہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ قاعدہ کلیہ مجملہ سے اس فعل کے حکم اجمالی کا علم حاصل ہو جائے مگر اسی فعل خاص کا حکم خاص نہ معلوم ہو سکے الغرض حکم اجمالی یہاں ممکن ہے لہذا توقف نہیں ہو سکے گا۔
His saying: "Third: suspension (al-tawaqquf), because there is a specific ruling..." From this expression, mention is made of the third and last of three opinions of the Mu'tazila regarding the second category of voluntary acts. And that is tawaqquf. The meaning of tawaqquf is that here there is no ruling, or the specific ruling is not known. Thus Qadi Baydawi and Allama Ibn Hajib and other usul scholars have stated this meaning. However, some scholars have said that "before revelation, not deserving reward or punishment for doing an act" is the meaning of tawaqquf. This meaning is attributed to Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. Indeed, many scholars of truth besides the Mu'tazila also adopted this view, such as Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, the author of al-Hidaya Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani, the Ahl al-Hadith, etc. Ibn Amir Hajj said in al-Taqrir that this is the school of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, Abu Bakr al-Sayrafi (al-Shafi'i), rather the majority of Shafi'is lean towards it, as Abd al-Aziz ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Bukhari said in Kashf al-Bazdawi. It has even been said that this is the school of Ahl al-Sunnah, to the extent that among the Companions, Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman (may Allah be pleased with them) and others also held this view.
The reason for tawaqquf: The proponents of suspension said: This place necessarily has one of the five well-known rulings, but since the Law has not been revealed, nor does reason have access to its knowledge, we do not know which ruling actually applies here. Therefore we adopt suspension, as in a matter not spoken about, suspension is the essence of piety.
His saying: "I say: This necessitates suspension in particularity, not at all." From this expression, the author (matn) objects to the statement of the proponents of suspension. That here there is a specific ruling among the five rulings and the lack of knowledge of that specific ruling's occurrence necessitates at most that the ruling of a particular act is not known. This does not necessitate that from a general principle the ruling cannot be known at all, because lack of knowledge of the ruling of a particular act does not negate knowledge of the summary ruling of that act. Thus it is possible that from a general summary principle, knowledge of the summary ruling of that act can be obtained, but the specific ruling of that particular act cannot be known. In short, a summary ruling is possible here, so suspension cannot occur.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage presents the third Mu'tazili position on acts before revelation: tawaqquf (suspension). The commentator explains that tawaqquf means either that there is no ruling or that the specific ruling is unknown. He notes that many non-Mu'tazili scholars, including al-Maturidi, al-Marghinani, al-Ash'ari, and even some Companions, held this view. The rationale is that while one of the five rulings definitely applies, reason cannot determine which, so the safest course is to suspend judgment. However, the author of the matn objects: not knowing the specific ruling does not entail complete ignorance; a summary ruling (e.g., permissibility in general) can still be known through a general principle. Thus, pure suspension is unnecessary because a summary ruling provides guidance. The commentator concludes that summary knowledge is possible, negating the need for absolute tawaqquf.

Key Terms
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment regarding the ruling of an act before revelation, either due to absence of ruling or ignorance of the specific ruling.
حكم إجمالي (hukm ijmali): A general or summary ruling derived from broad principles, as opposed to a specific detailed ruling.
حكم معين (hukm mu'ayyan): A specific, detailed ruling from the five categories (wajib, haram, etc.) applicable to a particular act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main objection to the Mu'tazili position of tawaqquf (suspension) before revelation?
A) That a specific ruling is always known through revelation.
B) That a summary ruling can be known from general principles, making absolute suspension unnecessary.
C) That reason alone can determine the ruling.
D) That the act is definitely permissible.

Key Takeaway
Before revelation, a summary ruling (hukm ijmali) can be known from general principles, so absolute suspension (tawaqquf) is not warranted.

Hanafi Classification of Actions: Good in Itself vs. Good for Something Else
Introducing the Hanafi categorization of actions into those good in themselves and those good due to something else.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'hasan li nafsihi' and 'hasan li ghayrihi', and classify an action like prayer or zakat according to this Hanafi usul taxonomy.

Core Idea
The Hanafi legal classification divides actions into those good by essence and those good by command—a foundational lens for understanding obligation and abrogation.

In this lesson, we begin the matn of Muslim al-Thubut, where the Hanafi usul framework introduces a primary classification of actions. This classification is not merely semantic; it shapes how we understand the nature of obligation, the possibility of abrogation, and the basis of reward. The passage distinguishes actions that are good in themselves from those that are good due to an external command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
From the passage, note that the Hanafis divided actions into 'what is good in itself' (hasan li nafsihi) and 'what is good due to something else' (hasan li ghayrihi).
2
Examine the subdivision within 'good in itself'
The first category is further split: some actions are good in themselves and 'do not admit of removal' (e.g., iman), while others 'admit of removal' (e.g., salat, which can be prohibited at disliked times).
The term 'removal' here refers to temporary abrogation or prohibition, not permanent nullification.
3
Understand the second category: 'good due to something else'
These actions (e.g., zakat, fasting) are good not inherently but because they are commanded. The servant has no choice in their intrinsic goodness; their value derives entirely from the divine command.
This category is attached to the first, meaning it shares the characteristic of being good, but the basis differs.
4
Relate the classification to legal implications
Reflect on how this taxonomy affects issues like abrogation: actions that are good in themselves but admit removal can be temporarily suspended, whereas those that do not admit removal are eternally valid.
This is a key usul principle when assessing apparent contradictions in revealed texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن المسلم : تنبيه الحنفية قسموا الفعل الى ماهو حسن لنفسه لا يقبل السقوط كالايمان او يقبل كالصلوة منعت في الاوقات المكروهة والى مالغيره ملحق بالاول وهو فيما لا اختيار للعبد فيه كالزكوة والصوم والجح شرعت نظراً
The Muslim text: A caution: The Hanafis divided the action into what is good in itself, which either does not admit of removal like faith, or admits of removal like prayer, prohibited in disliked times, and into what is due to something else, attached to the first, and that is where the servant has no choice, like zakat and fasting... [according to] the view that it is prescribed.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This is the beginning of a matn passage that presents the Hanafi classification of actions according to their moral and legal assessment. The first category is 'good in itself' (hasan li nafsihi), which is further subdivided: some actions are good in themselves and cannot be abrogated or removed, such as faith (iman), and others are good in themselves but can be abrogated in certain circumstances, such as prayer (salat) which is prohibited in dislike times (like sunrise, zenith, sunset). The second category is 'good due to something else' (hasan li ghayrihi), which is attached to the first category, and applies to actions where the servant has no choice, such as zakat and fasting. The text is incomplete here; it likely continues to explain the ruling and the basis for the classification.

Key Terms
حسن لنفسه (hasan li nafsihi): An action that is good in itself, irrespective of external factors.
حسن لغيره (hasan li ghayrihi): An action that gains goodness due to an external factor or command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Good due to something else.
B) Good in itself and subject to removal (i.e., can be prohibited at certain times).
C) Good in itself and not subject to removal.
D) Neither good nor evil in itself.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of actions into hasan li nafsihi and hasan li ghayrihi is foundational for understanding which actions can be abrogated or temporarily suspended and which are eternally good.

Hanafi Classification of Actions: Hasan li-Dhatihi and Hasan li-Ghayrihi
Classifying actions by intrinsic and extrinsic goodness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hasan li-dhatihi and hasan li-ghayrihi, identify their subdivisions, and explain the Hanafi debate on whether an absolute command indicates intrinsic or acquired goodness.

Core Idea
Good actions are either intrinsically good (hasan li-dhatihi) or become good due to an external factor (hasan li-ghayrihi).

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, actions are not all equal in moral and legal quality. Scholars have classified actions based on the source of their goodness: some are good in themselves, while others derive goodness from external factors. This classification has direct implications for how commands are interpreted and how obligations may be repealed. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi taxonomy of hasan actions and the internal debate on the absolute command.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the overall division
The Hanafis first divide actions into hasan (good) and qabih (bad). This lesson focuses on hasan. Identify the two main categories: hasan li-dhatihi and hasan li-ghayrihi.
The same division applies to qabih by analogy.
2
Define hasan li-dhatihi and its subtypes
Hasan li-dhatihi is an action good in itself. It has two subtypes: non-repealable (e.g., iman) and repealable (e.g., salat). Understand what makes each subtype distinct.
The goodness of iman never falls; salat’s obligation can be lifted in certain circumstances.
3
Define hasan li-ghayrihi and its subtypes
Hasan li-ghayrihi is an action good due to an external factor. It also has two subtypes: attached to hasan li-dhatihi (e.g., zakat, fasting) and not attached (e.g., jihad, hudud). Note the external factor that confers goodness.
Attached type: the action has some intrinsic goodness but requires an external need (e.g., poverty for zakat).
4
Analyze the debate on al-amr al-mutlaq
The absolute command (amr mutlaq) devoid of context raises the question: does it indicate hasan li-dhatihi (Shams al-A'imma's view) or hasan li-ghayrihi (al-Badi's view)? Examine the basis of each position.
The thamarah al-khilaf concerns whether the commanded act’s goodness is intrinsic or derived from the command.
5
Apply the classification to examples
Practice by classifying given actions (e.g., iman, salat, zakat, jihad) into the correct category and subtype, justifying your answer with reference to the criteria.

Source Text

الحنفية قسموا الفعل الى ماهو الحسن لنفسه لا يقبل السقوط كما اختاره شمس الائمة او لغيره كما في البديع لثبوت الحسن في المامور به اقتضاء فيثبت الادنى :ترجمہ : - حنفیہ نے تقسیم کی ہے فعل کی حسن لعینہ ، کی طرف جو سقوط کو قبول نہیں کرتا جیسے ایمان ، یا سقوط کو قبول کرے جیسے نماز چنانچہ وہ اوقات مکروہ میں ممنوع ہے۔ (اور تقسیم کی ہے ) حسن لغیرہ کی طرف جو حسن لعینہ کے ساتھ ملحق ہو اور وہ وہ ہے جس میں بندہ کو اختیار نہ ہو جیسے زکوۃ، روزہ، حج، نظر کرتے ہوئے حاجت فقیر نفس اور بیت اللہ کی طرف مشروع ہوا ہے، یا حسن لعینہ کے ساتھ ملحق نہ ہو جیسے جہاد و حدود اور نماز جنازہ ، بیشک وہ کفر، معصیت اور میت کے مسلمان ہونے کے واسطے سے مشروع ہوا ہے اور اسی طرح قبیح کے بھی اقسام ہونگے ، امر مطلق جو قرینہ سے خالی ہوتو کیا ایسا امرحسن لنفسہ غیر قابل سقوط کے لئے آتا ہے جیسا کہ شمس الائمہ سرخسی کا مختار ہے یا حسن لغیرہ، کے لئے آتا ہے جیسا کہ بدیع میں ہے مامور بہ میں اقتضاء حسن ثابت ہونے کی وجہ سے پس اس سے ادنی ثابت ہوگا۔

تشريح - قوله الحنفية قسموا الفعل الى ماهو الخ افعال کے حسن و فتح کو ذاتی و عقلی ثابت کرنے کے بعد فعل حسن اور فعل قبیح کے اقسام کو بر بنائے مذہب حنفیہ، درج بالا عبارت میں بیان کیا ہے ان قسموں کو اجمالاً و تفصیلاً ذیل کے سطور میں ملاحظہ کرو۔
اجمال: فعل کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) فعل حسن، (۲) فعل قبیح ،
(1) فعل حسن کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) حسن لنفہ، (۲) حسن لغیرہ، (۱) حسن لنفسہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں، وہ حسن جو غیر قابل سقوط ہو (۲) وہ حسن جو قابل سقوط ہو۔ (۲) حسن لغیرہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) حسن لغیر و احق بحسن لنفسہ (۲) حسن لغیرہ غیر ملحق بحسن لنفسه ، اسی طرح فعل قبیح کی دو قسمیں ہیں ۔ (۱) قبيح لعينہ (۲) قبیح لغیرہ (۱) قبيح لعينیہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) قبيح غیر محتمل سقوط ہو (۲) قبيح محتمل السقوط ہو۔ (۲) قبيح لغیرہ کی بھی دو قسمیں ہیں۔
(1) قبيح لغیر الحق بتصیح لعینه - (۲) قبيح لغیره غیر ماحق بنتیج بعينه
تفصیل :۔ حنفیہ نے بطور استقر الفعل حسن کی اولا دو قسمیں کی ہیں قسم اول - حسن النصہ ہے اور وہ فعل ہے کہ حسن ذات فعل میں ہو ثبوت حسن میں واسطہ فی العروض، بلکہ واسطہ فی الثبوت کو بھی دخل نہ ہو۔ پھر اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں ایک وہ حسن ہے جس کا حسن مامور بہ سے کبھی ساقط نہ ہو بلکہ ہمیشہ حسن ہی رہے اور وہ مامور به مکلف پر واجب رہے جیسے ایمان یعنی حضور نبی کریم نے کی تصدیق قلبی ان تمام باتوں میں جو من عند اللہ لیکر آئے ہیں۔ پس یہ تصدیق کبھی بھی حتی کہ حالت اکراہ میں بھی بندہ مکلف سے ساقط نہیں ہوتی ارشادربانی ہے الا من اكره و قلبه مطمئن بالایمان ماتن نے اس جگہ حاشیہ میں کہا ہے ۔ اى التصديق القلبى فانه لا يسقط بالاكراه فانه كمال النفس بذاته. انتهت - یعنی ایمان سے تصدیق مراد ہے اس لئے کہ اقرار باللسان حالت اکراہ میں کبھی ساقط ہو جاتا ہے لیکن تصدیق قلبی قطعا کسی حالت میں ساقط نہیں ہوتی ۔ اس حاشیہ کی عبارت سے سمجھ میں آتا ہے کہ ماتن نے مسئلہ ایمان میں ان لوگوں کا مذہب اختیار کیا ہے جن کے نزدیک اقرار باللسان ایمان کا جز ہے نہ شرط ہے بلکہ دنیا میں محض اجراء احکام کے لئے اقرار شرط ہے اس لئے منافق عند اللہ مومن نہ ہو گا بعد عہد نبوت صرف اجراء احکام نبویہ کے اعتبار سے مسلمان کہا جاتا ہے۔
قوله او يقبل كالصلوة فى الأوقات المكروهة.
اس عبارت میں حسن لنفسہ کی دوسری قسم کا بیان ہے۔ اور وہ وہ ہے جسکا حسن اوقات میں سے کسی وقت یا اعزار میں سے کسی عذر کیوجہ سے سقوط کو قبول کرتا ہے جیسے نماز چنانچہ وہ اوقات مکروہہ میں ممنوع ہے ، یونہی حالت حیض و نفاس میں اجماعاً ساقط ہو جاتی ہے جیسے اقرار حالت اکراہ میں حالانکہ نماز فی نفسہا حسن ہے کہ اس میں ابتداء سے انتہا ء تک اقوال وافعال کے ذریعہ رب کی تعظیم ہے اور اسکی ثناء ہے، اس کے لئے خشوع ہے اور اس کے لئے قیام کرنا اور اسکی بارگاہ میں جلسہ کرنا ہے وغیرہ۔ اس جگہ مصنف نے حاشیہ آرائی کرتے ہوئے کہا۔
" ويسقط بالحيض والنفاس اجماعاً في التحرير ان كان لذواتها لا يتخلف فحرمتها لعروض قبح خارج اقول المراد من السقوط عدم اعتباره في الاحكام.
The Hanafis divided the action into what is good in itself, not accepting repeal, as chosen by Shams al-A'imma, or due to something else, as in al-Badi', because goodness is established in the commanded action by implication, so the lower is established. Translation: The Hanafis have divided action into hasan li-dhatihi, which does not accept repeal, like iman, or accepts repeal, like salat, thus it is prohibited in disliked times. And they divided into hasan li-ghayrihi that is attached to hasan li-dhatihi, and that is that which the servant has no choice over, like zakat, fasting, hajj, being prescribed with regard to the need of the poor, the soul, and the House of Allah, or not attached to hasan li-dhatihi, like jihad, hudud, and salat al-janazah, indeed they are prescribed due to kufr, sin, and the deceased's Islam. And similarly the divisions of qabih. The absolute command devoid of context: does it come for hasan li-dhatihi non-repealable, as Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose, or for hasan li-ghayrihi, as in al-Badi'? Because of the establishment of goodness in the commanded act by implication, so the lower is established.

Elucidation: His saying 'The Hanafis divided the action into what is...' etc. After establishing the intrinsic and rational goodness and ugliness of actions, the divisions of good and bad actions according to the Hanafi school are stated in the above passage. Observe these divisions briefly and in detail in the following lines.
Summary: Action has two types: (1) good action, (2) bad action.
(1) Good action has two types: (1) good in itself, (2) good due to something else. (1) Good in itself has two types: (a) that good which is non-repealable, (b) that good which is repealable. (2) Good due to something else has two types: (a) good due to something else attached to good in itself, (b) good due to something else not attached to good in itself. Similarly, bad action has two types: (1) bad in itself, (2) bad due to something else. (1) Bad in itself has two types: (a) bad non-repealable, (b) bad repealable. (2) Bad due to something else also has two types: (a) bad due to something else attached to bad in itself, (b) bad due to something else not attached to bad in itself.
Detail: The Hanafis, by induction, first divided good action into two types. The first type is good in itself, and that is an action whose goodness is in the essence of the action, with no intermediary in its occurrence of goodness, nor even an intermediary in its establishment. Then it has two types: one is that good whose goodness is never repealed from the commanded act, but remains always good and obligatory upon the mukallaf, like iman, i.e., heartfelt affirmation of the Prophet's message in all matters brought from Allah. Thus this affirmation is never repealed from the servant, even under coercion. Allah says: "Except him who is forced and his heart is at rest with iman." The author said in a marginal note: i.e., heartfelt affirmation, for it is not repealed by coercion, as it is the perfection of the soul by itself. End. That is, by iman is meant affirmation, because verbal confession sometimes falls under coercion, but heartfelt affirmation never falls in any circumstance. From this marginal note it is understood that the author has adopted the school of those who consider verbal confession not a part of iman but a condition, rather it is a condition for the application of rulings in this world. Therefore, the hypocrite is not a believer in the sight of Allah, but after the prophetic era, he is called a Muslim only for the application of prophetic rulings.
His saying: 'or accepts, like salat in disliked times.' In this phrase the second type of good in itself is explained. And that is that whose goodness accepts repeal due to a particular time or a particular excuse, like salat: thus it is prohibited in disliked times, similarly it is repealed during menstruation and post-childbirth by consensus, just as confession falls under coercion, while salat is in itself good, from beginning to end containing glorification of the Lord through words and actions, praise, humility, standing, sitting in His court, etc. Here the author commented in the margin: "And it is repealed by menstruation and post-childbirth by consensus in al-Tahrir. If it were good for its own essence, it would not be repealed. So its prohibition is due to an external ugliness. I say: the meaning of repeal is its non-consideration in rulings."
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi classification of actions (af'al) into hasan (good) and qabih (bad) from the perspective of usul al-fiqh. The focus is on hasan actions. The Hanafis divide hasan into two main categories: hasan li-dhatihi (good in itself) and hasan li-ghayrihi (good due to something else). Each is further subdivided. Hasan li-dhatihi includes actions whose goodness is intrinsic and independent; these may be non-repealable (e.g., iman, the inner affirmation of faith, which never falls even under coercion) or repealable (e.g., salat, which can be prohibited in disliked times or dropped during menstruation). Hasan li-ghayrihi includes actions that become good only because of an external factor, such as a command or need; these may be attached to hasan li-dhatihi (e.g., zakat, fasting, hajj, which are prescribed due to other's need) or not attached (e.g., jihad, hudud, salat al-janazah, prescribed due to kufr, sin, or the deceased's Islam). The passage also discusses the absolute command (amr mutlaq) and whether it indicates hasan li-dhatihi (as per Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi) or hasan li-ghayrihi (as per al-Badi'). The tashrih (commentary) then elaborates on these divisions with examples, including a note on iman and the status of verbal confession. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi inductive method and internal ikhtilaf on the nature of commanding.

Key Terms
حسن لنفسه (hasan li-dhatihi): An action that is good in itself, without needing an external factor for its goodness.
حسن لغيره (hasan li-ghayrihi): An action that becomes good due to an external factor, such as a command, need, or context.
الأمر المطلق (al-amr al-mutlaq): An absolute command that is not qualified by any context (qarina).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, which type of goodness does iman (faith) belong to?
A) Hasan li-ghayrihi
B) Hasan li-dhatihi that is non-repealable
C) Hasan li-dhatihi that is repealable
D) Qabih li-dhatihi

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, actions are classified into intrinsic and acquired goodness, with the absolute command's implication debated as indicating either intrinsic or acquired goodness.

Hasan li-Dhatihi: The Never-Ceasing Goodness of Iman
Defines first subdivision of hasan li-dhatihi with iman example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definition of the first subtype of hasan li-dhatihi and apply the Quranic proof (16:106) to argue that iman (tasdiq qalbi) remains wajib even under coercion.

Core Idea
The first subtype of hasan li-dhatihi is never removed; iman, as heartfelt belief, remains wajib eternally even under coercion.

This lesson explores the Hanafi classification of acts based on intrinsic goodness. The first category, hasan li-dhatihi, is subdivided into two types; the first type is an act whose goodness never ceases and remains obligatory forever. The paradigmatic example is iman—specifically heartfelt belief (tasdiq qalbi). The Quranic verse on coercion serves as the proof, and the associated gloss clarifies that verbal confession (iqrar) is not part of iman but a condition for worldly rulings. By understanding this, you will grasp how Hanafi usul establishes permanent obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi classification of hasan
The Hanafis divided good acts (hasan) into two primary categories: hasan li-dhatihi (good by essence) and hasan li-ghairihi (good due to something else). The passage focuses on the first category.
This division is based on induction (istiqra).
2
Define the first subtype of hasan li-dhatihi
Within hasan li-dhatihi, there is a subtype whose goodness is never removed from the commanded act; it always remains good and wajib on the mukallaf. No external circumstance can strip it of its goodness.
3
Examine the example: iman as tasdiq qalbi
The exemplar is iman, defined as heartfelt belief (tasdiq qalbi) in everything the Prophet brought. The passage asserts that this belief is never dropped from the mukallaf, even in a state of coercion (ikrah).
The Arabic phrase 'تصدیق قلبی' (tasdiq qalbi) is key.
4
Analyze the dalil: Quran 16:106
The proof is the verse 'except he who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith'. The verse explicitly shows that coercion does not affect inner certainty; the heart remains firm. Thus, tasdiq is not nullified.
The dalil is qat'i in thubut and dalala.
5
Understand the gloss on iqrar vs tasdiq
The author's gloss explains that 'iman' here means tasdiq, because iqrar bil-lisan may be removed under coercion. Tasdiq is the perfection of the soul and cannot be coerced. This implies that iqrar is a condition for worldly rulings, not a part of iman.
This reflects a Hanafi ikhtilaf: iqrar is not part of iman but a condition for hukum in this world.

Source Text

(1) قبیح لغیر الحق بتصیح لعینه - (۲) فتیح لغیره غیر ماحق بنتیج بعينه
تفصیل :۔ حنفیہ نے بطور استقر الفعل حسن کی اولا دو قسمیں کی ہیں قسم اول - حسن النصہ ہے اور وہ فعل ہے کہ حسن ذات فعل میں ہو ثبوت حسن میں واسطہ فی العروض، بلکہ واسطہ فی الثبوت کو بھی دخل نہ ہو۔ پھر اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں ایک وہ حسن ہے جس کا حسن مامور بہ سے کبھی ساقط نہ ہو بلکہ ہمیشہ حسن ہی رہے اور وہ مامور به مکلف پر واجب رہے جیسے ایمان یعنی حضور نبی کریم نے کی تصدیق قلبی ان تمام باتوں میں جو من عند اللہ لیکر آئے ہیں۔ پس یہ تصدیق کبھی بھی حتی کہ حالت اکراہ میں بھی بندہ مکلف سے ساقط نہیں ہوتی ارشادربانی ہے الا من اكره و قلبه مطمئن بالایمان ماتن نے اس جگہ حاشیہ میں کہا ہے ۔ اى التصديق القلبى فانه لا يسقط بالاكراه فانه كمال النفس بذاته. انتهت - یعنی ایمان سے تصدیق مراد ہے اس لئے کہ اقرار باللسان حالت اکراہ میں کبھی ساقط ہو جاتا ہے لیکن تصدیق قلبی قطعا کسی حالت میں ساقط نہیں ہوتی ۔ اس حاشیہ کی عبارت سے سمجھ میں آتا ہے کہ ماتن نے مسئلہ ایمان میں ان لوگوں کا مذہب اختیار کیا ہے جن کے نزدیک اقرار باللسان ایمان کا جز ہے نہ شرط ہے بلکہ دنیا میں محض اجراء احکام کے لئے اقرار شرط ہے اس لئے منافق عند اللہ مومن نہ ہو گا بعد عہد نبوت صرف اجراء احکام نبویہ کے اعتبار سے مسلمان کہا جاتا ہے۔
The Hanafis, through induction, first divided the good act into two categories. First category: hasan li-dhatihi, and it is an act whose goodness is in the essence of the act, with no intermediary in the occurrence of the goodness, nor even an intermediary in the affirmation. Then it has two subdivisions: one is that goodness which is never removed from the commanded act, rather it always remains good, and the commanded act remains obligatory upon the mukallaf, like iman, i.e., heartfelt belief in the Prophet (PBUH) in all that he brought from Allah. Thus this belief is never removed from the mukallaf even in a state of coercion. The divine command is: {except he who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith} (Quran 16:106). The author (matn) said in a gloss: 'i.e., the heartfelt belief, for it is not removed by coercion, for it is the perfection of the soul by itself.' End. That is, by iman is meant heartfelt belief, because verbal confession may be removed in coercion, but heartfelt belief is absolutely never removed. From this gloss it is understood that the author adopted the position of those who hold that verbal confession is not a part of iman but a condition, rather it is a condition for the execution of rulings in this world, so a hypocrite is not a believer in the sight of Allah, but after the prophetic era he is called a Muslim only with regard to the execution of the prophetic rulings.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage opens the discussion on the classification of acts according to their inherent goodness (husn). The Hanafi position, based on induction, first divides good acts into two: hasan li-dhatihi (good by essence) and hasan li-ghairihi (good due to something else). The author focuses on the first category, hasan li-dhatihi, which is an act whose goodness resides in its very essence without any external cause. This category is further subdivided into two types. The first type is an act whose goodness is never removed; it remains wajib on the mukallaf forever. The example given is iman (belief), specifically heartfelt belief (tasdiq qalbi). The proof is the Quranic verse: 'except he who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith' (16:106). The author's gloss clarifies that this heartfelt belief is the perfection of the soul and cannot be negated by coercion. The text then explains that verbal confession (iqrar bil-lisan) may fall away under coercion, but the inner conviction never does. The author adopts the position that verbal confession is not a part of iman but a condition for worldly rulings, distinguishing between a true believer and a hypocrite. This is a standard Hanafi position: iman is primarily tasdiq, and iqrar is for the application of legal rules in this world.

Key Terms
حسن لنفسہ (hasan li-dhatihi): An act whose goodness is intrinsic to its essence, without external cause.
تصدیق قلبی (tasdiq qalbi): Heartfelt belief and affirmation in the teachings brought by the Prophet (PBUH).
استثنا (istithna): An exception in a text that excludes a subset from a general ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does iman (heartfelt belief) never cease to be wajib even under coercion?
A) Because verbal confession is always maintained
B) Because the Quranic verse says the heart remains firm
C) Because the act of iman is hasan li-ghairihi
D) Because the mukallaf cannot control coercion

Key Takeaway
The first subtype of hasan li-dhatihi is an act whose goodness is never removed; iman, as heartfelt belief, remains wajib forever, even under coercion, as proven by Quran 16:106.

Hasan li-Dhatihi Second Subtype: Act Whose Goodness Can Cease Temporarily
Explains the second subtype of hasan li-dhatihi using salah and the dispute with Ibn al-Humam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the second subtype of hasan li-dhatihi and evaluate Ibn al-Humam's objection using the concept of 'squqt' as non-consideration in rulings.

Core Idea
Essential goodness can be overridden in legal rulings without being eliminated — the accidental may overpower the essential.

This lesson explores a critical refinement in the Hanafi classification of hasan li-dhatihi. While an act may be intrinsically good, its legal consideration can be suspended by external factors such as time or excuse. The case of salah during menstruation and disliked times illustrates how the Hanafi school navigates the interaction between essential goodness and accidental properties, addressing a challenge from Imam Ibn al-Humam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Second Subtype
Define the second subtype of hasan li-dhatihi: an act whose essential goodness accepts removal due to time or excuse. The example is salah, which is prohibited during disliked times and falls away during menstruation and postpartum bleeding.
The first subtype was one whose goodness is never removed.
2
Understand the Example of Salah
Salah is essentially good—contains glorification, praise, humility—yet it is legally suspended during menstruation by consensus. Discuss why this does not negate essential goodness.
Essential goodness remains, but legal consideration (i'tibar) is removed.
3
Examine Ibn al-Humam's Objection
Ibn al-Humam argued that if goodness is essential, it cannot be removed from the essence; rather an accidental evil must attach, making the act evil temporarily. Understand his reasoning.
He denied the possibility of 'squqt' of essential goodness.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The matn clarifies that 'squqt' means not considering the essential goodness in rulings, not its removal. The accidental can overpower the essential, as with carrion becoming permissible due to necessity.
Analogy: carrion is essentially haram but permissible in dire need.
5
Derive Practical Implication
For menstruating women: no salah and no makeup. This shows that accidental factors can suspend even the most essential acts. Reflect on the thamarah al-khilaf.
The Hanafi view is mufta bihi.

Source Text

قوله او يقبل كالصلوة فى الاوقات المكروهة.
اس عبارت میں حسن لنفسہ کی دوسری قسم کا بیان ہے۔ اور وہ وہ ہے جسکا حسن اوقات میں سے کسی وقت یا اعزار میں سے کسی عذر کیوجہ سے سقوط کو قبول کرتا ہے جیسے نماز چنانچہ وہ اوقات مکروہہ میں ممنوع ہے ، یونہی حالت حیض و نفاس میں اجماعاً ساقط ہو جاتی ہے جیسے اقرار حالت اکراہ میں حالانکہ نماز فی نفسہا حسن ہے کہ اس میں ابتداء سے انتہا ء تک اقوال وافعال کے ذریعہ رب کی تعظیم ہے اور اسکی ثناء ہے، اس کے لئے خشوع ہے اور اس کے لئے قیام کرنا اور اسکی بارگاہ میں جلسہ کرنا ہے وغیرہ۔ اس جگہ مصنف نے حاشیہ آرائی کرتے ہوئے کہا۔ " ويسقط بالحيض والنفاس اجماعاً في التحرير ان كان لذواتها لا يتخلف فحرمتها لعروض قبح خارج اقول المراد من السقوط عدم اعتباره في الاحكام. والعارض قد يزيد اعتباره على الذاتى فى الحكم كالضررة في اباحة الميتة فتدبر " انتهت۔
یعنی حالت حیض و نفاس میں نماز اجماعاً ساقط ہو جاتی ہے کہ ان دونوں حالتوں میں نماز فتیح لذاتہ ہے، اور اسوقت میں حسن ذاتی وحسن خارجی باقی نہیں رہتا۔ مگر امام ابن ہمام نے تحریر میں اس پر اعتراض کیا ہے کہ افعال کا حسن اگر ذاتی ہو تو اسکا ذات سے تخلف نہیں ہوتا اسلئے کہ مقتضی ذات کا ذات سے تخلف ممتنع ہے لہذا اوقات مکروہ میں نماز کا حسن ذاتی زائل نہیں ہوگا البتہ نماز کو عرض عارض کی وجہ سے فتح عارض ہوا ہے اور یہاں عارض ہے نماز کا اوقات مکروہہ میں واقع ہونا۔ یونہی حالت حیض ونفاس میں نماز کا حسن ذاتی متخلف نہیں ہوتا البتہ اس پر عرض عارض کی وجہ سے فتح عارض ہے اور یہاں عارض ہے نماز کا نا پاک حالت میں وقوع۔
صاحب تحریر کا جواب دیتے ہوئے ماتن کہتے ہیں کہ حسن کے سقوط سے مراد اسکا احکام میں معتبر نہ ہونا ہے چنانچہ اس لئے کہ سقوط حسن سے مراد احکام میں حسن ذاتی کا معتبر نہ ہونا ہے حائضہ ونفساء سے حالت حیض و نفاس میں نماز ساقط ہے کہ نماز کا حسن ذاتی ان دونوں کے حق میں غیر معتبر ہے۔ جبھی ان پر نماز واجب نہیں رہتی نہ ہی قضا واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اور رہا عارض تو اسکا اعتبار حکم میں کبھی ذاتی سے بھی بڑھ جاتا ہے جیسے ضرورت ، اباحت میتہ میں ، دیکھو میتہ کی حرمت ذاتی ہے مگر ضرورت کے عارض ہونے کی وجہ سے میتہ مباح ہو گیا کہ اباحت میتہ کے حکم میں ضرورت عارضہ، حرمت ذاتی سے بڑھ گئی ہے۔ لہذا یہ کہنا کہ اس کا حسن ذاتی ساقط نہیں ہوا بلکہ فتح عارض غالب ہو گیا ہے صحیح نہیں کیونکہ اس تقدیر پر حائضہ و نفساء کے حق میں نماز ذاتی کے بالمقابل مزید تیج ہو جائے گی کہ عارض کبھی ذاتی سے بڑھ جاتی ہے۔
His saying: 'or accepts removal, like salah in disliked times.' In this phrase, the second type of hasan li-dhatihi is explained. It is that whose goodness accepts removal due to a particular time or a certain excuse, such as salah; indeed it is prohibited in disliked times, and similarly, by consensus, it falls away during menstruation and postpartum bleeding, like confession under coercion, even though salah in itself is good, for from beginning to end it involves glorification of the Lord through words and actions, praising Him, humility, standing, sitting in His presence, etc. At this point the author wrote a gloss: 'It falls away during menstruation and postpartum bleeding by consensus in al-Tahrir. If it were due to its essence, it would not be removed; rather its prohibition is due to the occurrence of an external evil. I say: the meaning of falling away is that it is not considered in the rulings. And the accidental sometimes increases in consideration over the essential in rulings, like necessity in permitting carrion, so ponder.' End. That is, salah falls away by consensus during menstruation and postpartum bleeding, because in these states salah is good in essence, but at that time the essential and external goodness do not remain. However, Imam Ibn al-Humam objected in al-Tahrir: if the goodness of acts is essential, it cannot be removed from that essence, because the essence's requirement cannot be removed from the essence; therefore, in disliked times the essential goodness of salah is not removed; rather, due to an accidental evil, the act becomes evil accidentally. Similarly, during menstruation and postpartum bleeding, the essential goodness of salah is not removed; rather, due to an accidental evil, it becomes evil accidentally. Responding to the author of al-Tahrir, the matn says: by 'falling away' of goodness is meant that it is not considered in the rulings; hence, for a menstruating or postpartum woman, salah is fallen away because the essential goodness of salah is not considered for them. Therefore, salah is not obligatory on them, nor must it be made up later. As for the accidental, its consideration in rulings sometimes overpowers the essential, like necessity in permitting carrion; note that carrion's prohibition is essential, but due to the accidental necessity, carrion becomes permissible, as the accidental necessity overpowers the essential prohibition. So saying that the essential goodness is not removed but rather the accidental evil dominates is incorrect, because on that assumption, for the menstruating and postpartum woman, salah would have a stronger effect, since the accidental sometimes overpowers the essential.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on hasan li-dhatihi and presents its second subtype: an act whose essential goodness can be overridden by external factors like time or excuse. The example is salah (prayer). Although salah is inherently good—consisting of glorification, praise, humility, etc.—it is prohibited during disliked times (awqat makruha) and falls away entirely during menstruation and postpartum bleeding by consensus. The author's gloss argues that 'falling away' means the essential goodness is not legally considered; it does not mean the essential goodness disappears. This leads to a dispute with Imam Ibn al-Humam (in al-Tahrir) who reasoned that if goodness is essential, it cannot be removed from the act's essence; rather, an accidental evil (qubh 'arid') attaches, making the act evil temporarily. The matn responds by clarifying that 'squqt' (falling away) in legal context means the act is not considered, not that its essential nature changes. The author supports this by citing the example of carrion: its prohibition is essential (haram li-dhatihi), but in cases of necessity, it becomes permissible because the accidental necessity takes precedence. This shows that an accidental factor can override an essential one in legal rulings. Thus, for menstruating and postpartum women, the essential goodness of salah is overridden by the accidental impurity, so they are not required to pray or make up those prayers. The lesson highlights the Hanafi principle that essential (dhati) and accidental ('arid) properties interact in legal rulings, and accidental factors sometimes dominate.

Key Terms
حسن ذاتی (hasan dhati): Essential goodness intrinsic to the act, e.g., the essence of salah.
عارض ('arid): An accidental property that comes to an act externally, affecting its rulings (e.g., time, excuse).
سقوط (squqt): Falling away; in this context, means the essential goodness is not considered in legal rulings, not that it disappears.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the matn reject Ibn al-Humam's objection that essential goodness cannot be removed?
A) Because essential goodness is indeed removed during menstruation
B) Because 'squqt' means the essential goodness is not considered in rulings, not that it disappears
C) Because Ibn al-Humam did not understand the consensus
D) Because the Quran explicitly states salah is not required during menstruation

Key Takeaway
Essential goodness can be overridden by accidental factors in legal rulings without being negated — this is the hallmark of the second subtype of hasan li-dhatihi.

Hasan li-Ghairihi: Acts Good Due to External Factor
Introduces the second main category of good acts: hasan li-ghairihi and its two subdivisions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hasan li-ghairihi and distinguish it from hasan li-dhatihi by identifying the source of goodness.

Core Idea
Goodness can be borrowed: an act becomes good because of an external factor, not its own nature.

In Usul al-Fiqh, we classify acts based on their moral value. Some acts are good in themselves; others become good because of something outside them. This lesson defines hasan li-ghairihi, the second main category, and explains its structure.

Guided Path
1
Recall the broader classification
Remember that acts are divided into hasan li-dhatihi (intrinsically good) and hasan li-ghairihi. This lesson focuses on the latter.
This is a foundational memorization anchor – fix the two-category framework.
2
Analyze the definition
Read the definition: hasan li-ghairihi is an act that has no intrinsic goodness; its goodness is acquired from an external source. Break down each element: 'no intrinsic goodness', 'goodness from external source'.
External source can be a divine command, intention, or circumstance.
3
Distinguish from hasan li-dhatihi
Contrast with hasan li-dhatihi: the latter’s goodness is inherent and does not depend on anything else. For hasan li-ghairihi, if the external factor is removed, the act becomes neutral or bad.
Example: Fasting is good because commanded (external), not because the act of abstaining is good in itself.
4
Note the two subdivisions
The text mentions hasan li-ghairihi has two subdivisions. Even though the passage cuts off, note this for further study: one subdivision relates to goodness affirmed via an intermediary, the other to goodness arising from an intermediary.
These are often detailed in later texts as hasan li-ghairihi bi-al-'arad and hasan li-ghairihi bi-al-ghayr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله والى مالغيره ملحق بالاول وهو فيما الخ درج بالا عبارت میں مصنف نے فعل کی دوسری قسم یعنی حسن لغیرہ اور اس کی قسموں کو ذکر کیا ہے۔ حسن لغیرہ اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ اس فعل میں ذاتی طور پر کوئی حسن نہ ہو نہ حسن میں اس کو دخل ہو بلکہ اس میں حسن غیر کی وجہ سے آیا ہو وہ غیر خواہ واسطہ فی الثبوت ہو یا واسطہ فی العروض ہو ۔ حسن لغیرہ کی بھی دو قسمیں ہیں
His saying: 'And to what is other than it, annexed to the first, and it is in what...' In the above phrase, the author mentioned the second type of act, i.e., hasan li-ghairihi and its divisions. Hasan li-ghairihi is called that which in the act has no intrinsic goodness, nor does it enter into goodness, rather goodness comes to it due to something else, whether that something is an intermediary in affirmation or an intermediary in occurrence. Hasan li-ghairihi also has two divisions.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage transitions to the second major category of good acts: hasan li-ghairihi (good due to something else). Unlike hasan li-dhatihi, acts in this category do not possess intrinsic goodness; their goodness is derived from an external factor, such as a divine command or a good intention. The author defines hasan li-ghairihi as an act that, by itself, has no goodness, nor does it contribute to goodness; rather, goodness attaches to it from an external source. This external source may be an intermediary in the affirmation of goodness (i.e., a reason why goodness is attributed) or an intermediary in its occurrence (i.e., a cause that brings about goodness). The passage then states that hasan li-ghairihi also has two subdivisions, but the text cuts off, so the specific subdivisions are not provided here. This classification is fundamental in Hanafi usul for understanding the moral and legal value of actions: some acts are inherently good (like faith), while others become good only through external factors (like ritual acts that are good because commanded, not because they are intrinsically so).

Key Terms
حسن لغیرہ (hasan li-ghairihi): An act whose goodness derives from an external source, not from its own essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the defining characteristic of hasan li-ghairihi?
A) Its goodness is intrinsic and never ceases
B) Its goodness comes from an external factor, not from the act itself
C) It is always prohibited during certain times
D) It is only found in acts of worship

Key Takeaway
Hasan li-ghairihi: goodness is borrowed from an external factor, not inherent in the act.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

The Virtue of Zakat, Fasting, and Hajj: Intrinsic or Through Means?
Dispute on whether three acts derive virtue from themselves or their means

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies zakat, fasting, and Hajj as hasan li-ghayrihi and evaluate the objection that they are hasan li-aynihi.

Core Idea
Zakat, fasting, and Hajj are virtuous not in themselves but through the means of repelling need, subduing the self, and visiting the House.

This passage from Sharh Muslim al-Thubut delves into a foundational usul dispute: are the three major acts of worship—zakat, fasting, and Hajj—virtuous in their own right (hasan li-aynihi) or do they acquire virtue through external means (hasan li-ghayrihi)? Sadr al-Shari'ah and al-Taftazani defend the latter view, arguing that in themselves these acts involve harm or diminishment, and their virtue stems from the noble purposes they serve.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objector's Claim
The objector argues that if the means (repelling need, subduing self, visiting House) are identical to the acts themselves, then the acts are hasan li-aynihi. Also, voluntary acts cannot serve as means.
The objector is unnamed but represents a view that the acts are intrinsically virtuous.
2
Examine the Hanafi Response
Sadr al-Shari'ah and al-Taftazani assert the means are more general than the acts: repelling need is broader than zakat, subduing self broader than fasting, visiting House broader than Hajj. Thus identity is false.
The means are not identical; they are overarching categories.
3
Analyze the Nature of the Means
The means themselves are not entirely virtuous. The poor deserve favor from Allah, not simply due to need; the House is just a building; the self is inclined to evil. Hence virtue is not intrinsic to the means either.
This shows the virtue is derived, not self-sufficient.
4
Conclude the Classification
Therefore, the three acts are hasan li-ghayrihi. Their virtue depends on the presence of the means with proper intention and circumstances.
This is the mukhtar (preferred) position of Sadr al-Shari'ah and al-Taftazani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زکوة ، قہر نفس عین صوم اور زیارت بیت عین حج ہیں تو پھر حسن افعال کے لئے واسطہ کیسے ہو سکتے ہیں کہ واسطہ وذ والواسطہ میں تغایر ضروری ہے علاوہ ازیں دفع حاجت، قہر نفس، اور زیارت بیت افعال اختیار یہ میں سے ہیں تو پھر وسائط کیونکر بن سکتے ہیں حالانکہ مصنف نے کہا ہے کہ انما يكون فيما لا اختيار للعبد فیه یعنی یہ واسط فعل اختیاری نہیں ہو گا۔
صدر الشریعہ صاحب توضیح اور علامہ تفتازانی صاحب تلویح کا مختار یہ ہے کہ ان عبادات ثلثہ کے لئے وسائط دفع حاجت قہر نفس اور زیارت بیت ہیں وجہ یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ فی نفسہ تنقیص مال ہے، صوم فی نفسہ اضرار نفس ہے اور صوم سے نفس کو خالق نفس کی طرف سے مباح کر دہ چیزوں سے روکنا ہے اور حج امکنہ مخصوصہ کی طرف مسافت کو طے کرنا اس کی زیارت کرنا ، سفر تجارت اور اماکن و بلدان کی زیارت اور سیر و تفریح کے منزلہ میں ہے غرض ان تینوں عبادتوں میں فی ذاتہا کوئی حسن نہیں ہے اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ اس کے وسائط میں حسن ہوتا کہ وسائط کے حسن سے ان عبادات میں حسن آسکے۔ رہے محض حاجت فقیر ، نفس اور بیت تو انہیں مطلقا کوئی حسن نہیں ہے لہذا یہ حاجت نفس اور بیت ان عبادات کے لئے وساطت کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتے بلکہ وسائط دفع حاجت ، قہر نفس اور زیارت بیت ہی ہو سکتے ہیں کہ وہ سب فی انفسہا حسن ہیں ۔ رہا یہ کہنا کہ دفع حاجت عین زکوۃ ، قہر نفس عین صوم اور زیارت بیت عین حج ہیں تو عینیت تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ دفع حاجت زکوۃ سے عام ہے۔ قہر نفس صوم سے عام ہے اور زیارت بیت حج سے عام ہے۔
اس تقدیر پر عبادات ثلثہ ( زکوۃ ، صوم ، حج ، ) کے اول یعنی حسن لعینہ کے ساتھ ملحق ہونے کی تقریر اس طرح ہوگی کہ وسائط گرچہ فی نفسہا حسن ہیں اور ان کے واسطے سے عبادات ثالثہ حسن ہو گئے ہیں لیکن یہ وسائط بھی من کل الوجوه حسن فی نفسہ نہیں ہیں بلکہ وہ وسائط من وجہ حسن ہیں اور من وجہ حسن نہیں ہیں اس لئے کہ فقیر محض اپنی حاجت کی وجہ سے مستحق احسان نہیں ہوا ہے بلکہ وہ احسان کا مستحق اپنے مولی عز وجل کی طرف سے ہوا ہے بندوں کی جہت سے نہیں۔ اور بیت فی نفسہ تو وہ بھی زیارت و تعظیم کا مستحق نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی دنیا کے جملہ بیوت میں سے ایک بیت ہے۔ اسی طرح نفس بحسب فطرت اگر چہ خیر وشر دونوں کا عمل ہے تا ہم نفس معاصی کو زیادہ قبول کرنے والا اور شہوات کی طرف زیادہ میلان رکھنے والا ہے گویا معاصی وشہوات نفس کا فطری تقاضا ہے بلکہ ایسا محسوس ہوتا ہے کہ نفس معاصی وشہوات پر پیدا کیا گیا ہے پس نفس کے فطری تقاضے اور خلقی جبلت کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے اس کو مجبور و مقہور کرنا حسن نہیں ہوگا۔
Zakat, subduing the self is fasting itself, and visiting the House is Hajj itself — so how can they be means for virtuous acts, because difference between the means and the object is necessary. Besides, repelling need, subduing the self, and visiting the House are among voluntary acts, so how can they be means while the author said: 'It only occurs in that which the slave has no choice,' i.e., the means will not be a voluntary act.

Sadr al-Shari'ah, the author of al-Tawdih, and 'Allamah al-Taftazani, the author of al-Talwih, have chosen that for these three acts the means are repelling need, subduing the self, and visiting the House. The reason is that zakat in itself is diminishment of wealth, fasting in itself is harm to the self, and fasting restrains the self from things permitted by the Creator of the self, and Hajj is traversing distance to specific places, visiting them, and it is similar to a trade journey and visiting places and cities and recreation. In summary, in themselves these three acts have no virtue, so it is necessary that the means have virtue so that virtue can come to these acts through the virtue of the means. As for mere need of the poor, the self, and the House, they have absolutely no virtue, so these (needs, self, house) do not have the capacity for intermediacy for these acts; rather, the means can only be repelling need, subduing the self, and visiting the House, because all of them are virtuous in themselves. As for the statement that repelling need is the same as zakat, subduing the self is the same as fasting, and visiting the House is the same as Hajj — this identity is not accepted, because repelling need is more general than zakat, subduing the self is more general than fasting, and visiting the House is more general than Hajj.

On this basis, the explanation for the three acts (zakat, fasting, Hajj) being annexed to the first category (virtue in themselves) is as follows: although the means are virtuous in themselves and through them the three acts become virtuous, these means are not entirely virtuous in themselves; rather, they are virtuous in one respect and not virtuous in another respect. This is because the poor person is not entitled to favor merely due to his need; rather, he is entitled to favor from his Lord, may He be exalted, not from the side of servants. And the House in itself is not entitled to visitation and veneration, because it is also one of all the houses in the world. Similarly, the self by nature, although it is the instrument of both good and evil, yet the self is more accepting of sins and more inclined towards desires; it is as if sins and desires are the natural demand of the self. Rather, it is felt that the self was created upon sins and desires. Therefore, looking at the natural demand and innate disposition of the self, subduing and overpowering it is not virtuous.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the classification of zakat, fasting, and Hajj as virtuous acts (hasan). The objector claims that if zakat itself is repelling need, fasting itself is subduing the self, and Hajj itself is visiting the House, then how can these be virtuous through means? Moreover, these means are voluntary acts, contradicting the rule that means are for involuntary acts. Sadr al-Shari'ah and al-Taftazani respond by asserting that the means are repelling need, subduing the self, and visiting the House, which are different and more general than the acts themselves. The acts in themselves lack virtue; virtue comes from these means, which are virtuous in themselves. They further clarify that these means are not entirely virtuous: the poor deserves favor from Allah, not merely due to need; the House is just a building; the self is inclined to evil. Thus, subduing the self is virtuous, but the self per se is not. This shows that the virtue of these acts derives from their means, making them hasan li-ghayrihi.

Key Terms
حسن لعینہ (hasan li-aynihi): An act that is virtuous in itself, intrinsically good.
حسن لغیرہ (hasan li-ghayrihi): An act that becomes virtuous due to an external factor (the means).
وساطت (wasatiyyah): Intermediation or means by which an act acquires virtue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sadr al-Shari'ah and al-Taftazani, what are the means through which zakat becomes virtuous?
A) Mere need of the poor
B) Repelling need
C) The act of giving money
D) The poor person's gratitude

Key Takeaway
The virtue of zakat, fasting, and Hajj is not intrinsic; it is derived from the means of repelling need, subduing the self, and visiting the House, making them hasan li-ghayrihi.
