The Second Type of Hasan Li-Ghayrihi: Ghayr Mulhaq
Defining hasan li-ghayrihi ghayr mulhaq with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hasan li-ghayrihi ghayr mulhaq and identify its two subtypes with examples from Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Acts like jihad and funeral prayer are virtuous not intrinsically but through their objectives.

In the previous lesson, we learned about hasan li-ghayrihi that is annexed to hasan li-aynihi. Now we turn to the second type: that which is not annexed. Here, the act itself may be blameworthy in appearance, but it becomes virtuous because of a noble intention or goal. The author provides examples from the Shari'ah: jihad, hudud, and funeral prayer. Although these acts involve unpleasant elements, they are commanded because of their beneficial ends.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that the author is defining the second type of hasan li-ghayrihi: ghayr mulhaq bi hasan li-aynihi, meaning the act is not intrinsically virtuous but becomes virtuous through an external means.
This type contrasts with the first type where the act has some intrinsic virtue.
2
Analyze the means (wasita)
The means must be a voluntary, intrinsically virtuous act. The object (the act in question) may or may not be intrinsically virtuous; the virtue is attributed to the object because of the means.
Two sub-types: wasita fi al-thubut (the means establishes virtue) and wasita fi al-urud (the virtue is accidental).
3
Examine the examples
Jihad, hudud, and funeral prayer are cited. Jihad involves killing and destruction but is virtuous because it repels disbelief. Hudud involve punishment but prevent sin. Funeral prayer resembles idol worship outwardly but honors the deceased Muslim.
These acts are legislated because of their higher objectives.
4
Understand the ruling implication
Because the virtue is from the means, the act itself is not considered hasan li-aynihi. However, it is still commanded and rewarded. The intention is crucial; if the means is not genuine, the act loses its virtue.
This distinction affects how we derive rulings for similar acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله اوغير ملحق كالجهاد والحدوصلوة الجنازة الخ
اس عبارت میں مائن نے حسن لغیرہ کی دوسری قسم کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ اس کی دوسری قسم حسن لغیرہ غیر ملحق بالا ول یعنی حسن لغیر و غیر ملحق بالسن لعینہ ہے اور وہ یہ ہے جس میں غیر اور واسطہ صفت حسن کے ساتھ متصف ہو بایں طور کہ وہ واسطہ فعل اختیاری ہو اور صفت حسن کے ساتھ بالذات متصف ہو خواہ ذوواسطہ بھی حسن کے ساتھ حقیقۂ متصف ہو خواہ ذوالواسطہ حسن کے ساتھ حقیقتا متصف نہ ہو بلکہ واسطہ کے واسطہ سے متصف ہو بہر دو تقدیر یہ قسم حسن لعینہ کے ساتھ ملحق نہیں ہوگی۔ واسطہ فی الثبوت کی دوسری صورت جس میں ذوالواسطه مثلا فعل ، صفت حسن کے ساتھ واسطہ کی تبعیت سے متصف ہوتا ہے، اسکا حسن لنفسہ سے غیر ملحق ہونا ظاہر ہے اور واسطہ فی الثبوت کی پہلی قسم جسمیں واسطہ و ذ والواسطہ دونوں صفت (حسن) کے ساتھ متصف ہوتے ہیں کا حسن لنفسہ سے غیر ملحق ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ واسطہ کی اس قسم میں ذوالواسطہ کی صفت غیر معتبر رہتی ہے اور واسطہ کی صفت حسن کے اعتبار سے ذوالواسطہ میں صفت کا لحاظ ملحوظ ہوتا ہے غرض واسطہ فی الثبوت کی یہ قسم واسطہ فی العروض سے زیادہ قریب ہے اور واسطہ فی العروض کا حسن لنفسہ سے غیر ملحق ہونا امین من الظہو ر ہے۔ حسن لغیرہ غیر ملحق بالسن لعینہ کی دوقسمیں ہیں ۔ ایک یہ کہ واسطہ اور غیر ذ والواسطہ اور فعل کے وجود سے موجود ہو جاتا ہے اور ذوالواسطہ کے ادا کر لینے سے واسطہ ادا ہو جاتا ہے جیسے جہاد، حدود اور نماز جنازہ۔ چنانچہ جہاد دفع کفر کے واسطہ سے، حدود دفع معاصی کے واسطے سے ، اور صلوٰۃ الجنازہ اسلام میت کے واسطہ سے حسن ہے۔ جہاد و حدود ان دونوں میں گرچہ عباداللہ کی تعذیب، اور بلاد کی تخریب ہے۔ ایسے ہی صلوٰۃ الجنازہ بظاہر عبادت اصنام و جہاد کے مشابہ ہے لیکن جہاد دفع کفر،
His statement: 'Or not annexed, like jihad, hudud, and funeral prayer, etc.'

In this expression, the author (mayn) has pointed to the second category of hasan li-ghayrihi. Its second category is hasan li-ghayrihi ghayr mulhaq bi al-awwal, i.e., hasan li-ghayrihi not annexed to hasan li-aynihi. And it is that in which the other (the means) is described with the attribute of virtue in such a way that the means is a voluntary act and is intrinsically described with the attribute of virtue, whether the object (the act) is also described with virtue in reality or the object is not described with virtue in reality but is described through the mediation of the means. In both cases, this category will not be annexed to hasan li-aynihi. As for the second form of waasita fi al-thubut (means in establishing virtue), in which the object (e.g., the act) is described with the attribute of virtue through following the means, its not being annexed to hasan li-aynihi is obvious. And as for the first type of waasita fi al-thubut, in which both the means and the object are described with the attribute (of virtue), the reason for its not being annexed to hasan li-aynihi is that in this type the attribute of the object remains unregarded, and the consideration of the attribute in the object is based on the attribute of the means. In short, this type of waasita fi al-thubut is closer to waasita fi al-urud, and the fact that waasita fi al-urud is not annexed to hasan li-aynihi is most evident.

Hasan li-ghayrihi ghayr mulhaq bi hasan li-aynihi has two types. First: the means comes into existence through the existence of the object (the act), and once the object is performed, the means is also performed. Examples: jihad, hudud, and funeral prayer. Thus, jihad is virtuous through the means of repelling disbelief, hudud through the means of repelling sins, and funeral prayer through the means of Islam of the deceased. Although in jihad and hudud there is punishment of Allah's servants and destruction of lands, similarly funeral prayer outwardly resembles worship of idols and jihad, but jihad repels disbelief...
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage defines the second major category of hasan li-ghayrihi: that which is not annexed to hasan li-aynihi. The author explains that in this category, the means (wasita) is a voluntary act that is intrinsically virtuous. The object (the act) may or may not be intrinsically virtuous; if it is not, the virtue comes entirely from the means. The means can be of two types: one where the means is realized through the act itself (e.g., jihad, hudud, funeral prayer). In these acts, although the acts themselves involve undesirable elements (killing, punishment, or resemblance to idol worship), they become virtuous through their objectives: jihad defends against disbelief, hudud punish crimes, and funeral prayer honors the Muslim deceased. The text from the OCR ends mid-sentence, but the explanation is clear: this type of virtue derives entirely from the external goal, not from the act's intrinsic nature.

Key Terms
حسن لغیرہ غیر ملحق (hasan li-ghayrihi ghayr mulhaq): Virtuous through means, not annexed to intrinsic virtue; the means is voluntary and intrinsically virtuous, and the act becomes virtuous through it without the act itself being intrinsically virtuous.
واسطہ فی الثبوت (wasita fi al-thubut): A means that establishes virtue in another; the virtue of the object is proven through this means.
واسطہ فی العروض (wasita fi al-urud): A means that is only accidental; the virtue appears in the object but is not inherent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason for funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) being considered virtuous?
A) Because it involves standing and supplication
B) Because it is performed for the deceased
C) Because the means is the Islam of the deceased
D) Because it resembles the prayer of the prophets

Key Takeaway
Hasan li-ghayrihi ghayr mulhaq applies to acts whose virtue derives entirely from a praiseworthy objective, not from the act itself.

Two Types of Ḥusn li-Ghayrihi Not Annexed to Ḥusn li-Dhātihi
Explaining the two types of حسن لغیرہ غیر ملحق بالحسن لعینہ with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the two types of ḥusn li-ghayrihi not annexed to ḥusn li-dhātihi, distinguishing cases where the beneficial purpose is directly achieved by the act from those requiring additional intention.

Core Idea
Acts can be good because of a purpose; the purpose may be directly fulfilled or require separate intention.

In Hanafi usul, acts are classified as good in themselves (ḥusn li-dhātihi) or good due to an external factor (ḥusn li-ghayrihi). This commentary from Ashraf al-Nuʿūt explains a critical subdivision: ḥusn li-ghayrihi that is not annexed to intrinsic goodness. It presents two patterns: Type 1, where the beneficial purpose is realized immediately upon performing the act, and Type 2, where the purpose requires an additional intention or act beyond the immediate action. Understanding this distinction helps jurists determine when an act becomes praiseworthy and whether separate intent is needed for reward.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish ḥusn li-dhātihi from ḥusn li-ghayrihi
Recall the basic classification: an act is ḥasan li-dhātihi if its goodness is intrinsic (e.g., justice, truthfulness); it is ḥasan li-ghayrihi if goodness depends on an external purpose (e.g., a painful injection that cures illness). This lesson focuses on the latter.
If the act is intrinsically good, it is annexed to the first kind; the passage deals only with those not annexed.
2
Identify the two types in the passage
From the text, note that the first non-annexed type has an intermediary (the purpose) that is achieved directly by the act. The second type requires an additional step beyond the act to realize the purpose.
Type 1 examples: jihad, hudud, salat al-janazah. Type 2 examples: wudu, sa'y to Jumu'ah.
3
Apply the definition to each example
For Type 1, verify that the beneficial purpose (e.g., repelling disbelief) is accomplished by the act itself without needing further intention or act. For Type 2, confirm that the purpose (e.g., prayer after wudu) requires a separate intention or performance.
Jihad directly elevates Allah's word; wudu only becomes good when intended for prayer which is a separate act.
4
Understand the author's note on the intermediary
The author emphasizes that in both types, the intermediary (wasilah) itself does not need to be good. It is merely a means. This refines the classification: the goodness of the act depends only on its connection to a good outcome, not on the quality of the intermediary.
For example, the punishment in hudud is not good in itself but deters sin; the act becomes good because of that deterrent effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله اوغير ملحق كالجهاد والحدوصلوة الجنازة الخ

بہر دو تقدیر یہ قسم حسن لعینہ کے ساتھ ملحق نہیں ہوگی۔ واسطہ فی الثبوت کی دوسری صورت جس میں ذوالواسطه مثلا فعل ، صفت حسن کے ساتھ واسطہ کی تبعیت سے متصف ہوتا ہے، اسکا حسن لنفسہ سے غیر ملحق ہونا ظاہر ہے حسن لغیرہ غیر ملحق بالسن لعینہ کی دوقسمیں ہیں ۔ ایک یہ کہ واسطہ اور غیر ذ والواسطہ اور فعل کے وجود سے موجود ہو جاتا ہے اور ذوالواسطہ کے ادا کر لینے سے واسطہ ادا ہو جاتا ہے جیسے جہاد، حدود اور نماز صلوٰۃ الجنازہ بظاہر عبادت اصنام و جہاد کے مشابہ ہے لیکن جہاد دفع کفر، اور اعلاء کلمتہ اللہ کے واسطہ سے حسن ہو گیا، اور اعلاء کلمۃ الحق جو جہاد کے لئے واسطہ ہے محض فعل جہاد ہے حاصل ہو جاتا ہے، جہاد کے بعد اعلاء کلمتہ اللہ کے لئے اب کسی امر آخر کی ضرورت نہیں رہتی ، اسی طرح اقامت حدود ، عباداللہ کو معصیت کے ارتکاب سے روکنے کے واسطے سے حسن ہو گیا اور زجر عباد ( دفع معصیت) جو اقامت حدود کا واسطہ ہے محض اقامت حدود سے حاصل ہو جاتا ہے، یونہی صلوۃ الجنازہ ، اسلام میت کی تعظیم اور اس کے حق کی ادائیگی کے واسطہ سے حسن ہے کیونکہ مسلمان کی تعظیم و تو قیر فی نفسہ حسن ہے پس تعظیم مسلم کے حسن کے واسطہ سے میت کی طرف استقبال کر کے اسکی مغفرت کی دعاء کرنا فعل حسن بن گیا اور یہ تعظیم مسلم جو صلوۃ الجنازہ کا واسطہ ہے محض صلوۃ الجنازہ سے حاصل ہو جاتا ہے اب اس کے بعد کسی امر آخر کی ضرورت نہیں رہتی ۔
دوسری قسم : حسن لغیرہ غیر ملحق بالحسن لعینہ کی دوسری قسم یہ ہے کہ ذوالواسطہ کے موجود ہو جانے سے واسطہ موجود نہیں ہوتا نہ ہی اس کے ادا کر لینے سے واسطہ ادا ہوتا ہے بلکہ واسطہ کے وجود و تحقق اور اسکی ادائیگی کے لئے کسی امر آخر کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے جیسے وضو جو کہ فی نفسہ تبرید، تنظیف اعضاء اور اللہ کی عظیم نعمت پانی کی اضاعت ہے تاہم وضو اللہ عز شانہ کی خاص عبادت نماز کے واسطہ سے حسن ہو گیا مگر نماز جو وضو کے حسن کا واسطہ ہے محض فعل وضوء سے ادا نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اس کے لئے ایک فعل آخر کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے اور وہ ہے ایجاد صلوٰۃ کا قصد اور اسکا ایقاع ہے چنانچہ اس لئے اگر وضوء میں قصد کیا تو وہ قربت مقصودہ ہو جاتا ہے جس پر متوضی کو ثواب ملتا ہے۔ اسی طرح سعی الی الجمعہ فی نفسہ جسم و جان اور نفس و روح کو تعب و مشقت میں ڈالنا اور اضاعت وقت ہے مگر ادائیگی جمعہ کے واسطہ سے سعی فعل حسن ہو گیا تا ہم نماز جمعہ جو سعی کے حسن ہونے کا واسطہ ہے صرف سعی سے ادا نہیں ہوتی بلکہ ایک امر آخر کی ضرورت ہوتی ہے اور وہ مسجد جمعہ میں نماز کا قصد اور اس کا ایقاع ہے۔ تنبيه : حسن لغیر ملحق بالاول، و غیر ملحق بالاول کی تفصیل سے آپ کو معلوم ہوا ہوگا کہ مصنف کا مختاران دونوں قسموں میں یہ ہے کہ واسطہ کا صفت حسن سے متصف ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے چنانچہ واسطہ قسم اول میں سفیر محض ہے حسن کے ساتھ متصف نہیں ہے جیسے حاجت فقیر نفس اور بیت اسی طرح غیر ملحق بالاول یعنی قسم دوم میں بھی واسطہ صفت حسن کے ساتھ متصف نہیں ہے اس لئے کہا انھ
Even though it is an act of both good and evil, nonetheless the soul is more receptive to sins and more inclined towards desires, as if sins and desires are the natural demand of the soul; rather it seems that the soul was created upon sins and desires. So, considering the natural demand and inherent disposition of the soul, compelling and subduing it is not good. His statement: 'or not annexed, like jihad, hudud, and salat al-janazah, etc.' In this phrase, the author indicates the second type of husn li-ghayrihi. Its second type is husn li-ghayrihi not annexed to the first, i.e., husn li-ghayrihi not annexed to husn li-dhatihi. It is that in which the intermediary (wasitah) is qualified by the attribute of goodness in such a way that the intermediary is an optional act and is qualified by goodness by itself, whether the thing-in-itself (dhu al-wasitah) is also qualified by goodness in reality or not; rather it is qualified by goodness through the intermediary. In both cases, this type is not annexed to husn li-dhatihi. The second form of 'intermediary in existence' (wasitah fi al-thubut) in which the thing-in-itself, e.g., an act, is qualified by goodness by following the intermediary – its not being annexed to husn li-dhatihi is obvious. And the first form of 'intermediary in existence' in which both the intermediary and the thing-in-itself are qualified by goodness – the reason for not being annexed to husn li-dhatihi is that in this type of intermediary, the attribute of the thing-in-itself is not considered; rather the attribute is considered in the thing-in-itself based on the attribute of goodness of the intermediary. In short, this type of 'intermediary in existence' is closer to 'intermediary in occurrence' (wasitah fi al-urud), and that 'intermediary in occurrence' is not annexed to husn li-dhatihi is clear. Husn li-ghayrihi not annexed to husn li-dhatihi has two types. One: the intermediary and the thing-in-itself both come into existence with the existence of the act, and by performing the thing-in-itself, the intermediary is performed, like jihad, hudud, and salat al-janazah. So jihad is good through the intermediary of repelling disbelief; hudud through the intermediary of preventing sins; and salat al-janazah through the intermediary of honoring the Muslim deceased. Although in jihad and hudud there is punishment of slaves of Allah and destruction of lands, and similarly salat al-janazah is apparently similar to worship of idols and jihad, but jihad becomes good through repelling disbelief and raising the word of Allah; and raising the word of truth, which is the intermediary for jihad, is achieved by the mere act of jihad; after jihad, no other thing is needed for raising the word of Allah. Similarly, establishing hudud becomes good through the intermediary of preventing the slaves of Allah from committing sins; and deterring the slaves (preventing sins), which is the intermediary of establishing hudud, is achieved by the mere establishment of hudud. Likewise, salat al-janazah is good through the intermediary of honoring the Muslim deceased and fulfilling his right, because honoring and venerating a Muslim is good in itself. So by the goodness of honoring a Muslim, facing the deceased and praying for his forgiveness becomes a good act. And this honoring of a Muslim, which is the intermediary for salat al-janazah, is achieved by the mere salat al-janazah; after it, no other thing is needed. Second type: The second type of husn li-ghayrihi not annexed to husn li-dhatihi is that by the existence of the thing-in-itself the intermediary does not exist, nor is the intermediary performed by performing the thing-in-itself; rather, for the existence and realization of the intermediary and its performance, another thing is needed. For example, wudu, which in itself is cooling, cleaning of limbs, and wasting the great blessing of water, yet wudu becomes good through the intermediary of the special worship of Allah – prayer. But prayer, which is the intermediary for the goodness of wudu, is not performed by the mere act of wudu; rather, another act is needed for it, and that is the intention and performance of prayer. So if one intends in wudu, then it becomes an intended act of worship for which the person performing wudu receives reward. Similarly, sa'y (going) to Jumu'ah in itself is putting body, soul, and spirit into difficulty and wasting time, but sa'y becomes a good act through the intermediary of performing Jumu'ah. However, the Jumu'ah prayer, which is the intermediary for the goodness of sa'y, is not performed by mere sa'y; rather, another thing is needed, and that is the intention and performance of prayer in the Jumu'ah mosque. Note: From the detail of husn li-ghayrihi annexed to the first and not annexed to the first, you may have understood that the author's chosen view in both types is that it is not necessary for the intermediary to be qualified by the attribute of goodness. Thus in the first type, the intermediary is merely a means (safir) not qualified by goodness, like the need of a poor person and a house. Similarly in the not-annexed-to-the-first type, i.e., the second type, the intermediary is also not qualified by the attribute of goodness; therefore he said...
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on a line from the matn of Musallam al-Thubut, clarifying the subdivision of husn li-ghayrihi (goodness derived from another). The author defines two broad categories: (1) husn li-ghayrihi annexed to husn li-dhatihi (which is not discussed here), and (2) husn li-ghayrihi not annexed to husn li-dhatihi. The latter is further divided into two types. In the first type, the intermediary (wasitah) that confers goodness is achieved directly by the act itself; once the act is performed, the purpose is fulfilled without needing any further action. Examples given are jihad (whose purpose is to repel disbelief and elevate Allah's word), hudud (deterrence from sin), and salat al-janazah (honoring the deceased Muslim). Although these acts may involve apparent harms (punishment, destruction, or resemblance to unlawful acts), they become good because the beneficial purpose is attained immediately upon performing the act. In the second type, the intermediary is not achieved by the act alone; an additional intention or act is required. The examples are wudu and sa'y to Jumu'ah. Wudu in itself is merely cleaning and cooling, but it becomes good when intended for prayer. However, the prayer itself is not performed by wudu; one must separately intend and perform the prayer. Similarly, going to Jumu'ah in itself is burdensome, but it becomes good when one intends and performs the Jumu'ah prayer. The note (tanbih) emphasizes that in both types of non-annexed husn li-ghayrihi, the intermediary itself does not need to be intrinsically good; it is merely a means. This is the author's chosen position.

Key Terms
حسن لغیره (ḥusn li-ghayrihi): An act that is good not in itself but because it leads to something good or is a means to a good end.
واسطة فی الثبوت (wāsiṭa fī al-thubūt): An intermediary that is an essential part of the act's existence—the goodness of the act depends on this intermediary being present.
ملحق بالاول (mulḥaq bi-l-awwal): Annexed to the first kind of husn li-ghayrihi (which is directly linked to husn li-dhātihi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is wudu considered ḥusn li-ghayrihi not annexed to ḥusn li-dhātihi?
A) Because wudu is painful and thus not good in itself.
B) Because the purpose (prayer) is not achieved by wudu alone; additional intention is needed.
C) Because wudu is not an act of worship.
D) Because the intermediary (prayer) is not good.

Key Takeaway
The two types of ḥusn li-ghayrihi not annexed to ḥusn li-dhātihi differ in whether the beneficial purpose is achieved directly by the act (Type 1) or requires additional intention or act (Type 2); the intermediary itself need not be good.

Evil Actions in Usul al-Fiqh: Intrinsic vs. Extrinsic
Classification of evil actions into intrinsic and extrinsic categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any evil action into its subtype (qabih li-aynihi or li-ghayrihi) and identify whether it can be removed by necessity.

Core Idea
An action's evil can be inherent or acquired due to context; only some intrinsic evils can be temporarily permitted.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi taxonomy of evil actions (qabih). Just as good actions have levels, evil actions are divided into intrinsic evil (qabih li-aynihi) and extrinsic evil (qabih li-ghayrihi). This classification is crucial for understanding when an act can become permissible under necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
Recognize that evil actions are first divided into qabih li-aynihi (evil in itself) and qabih li-ghayrihi (evil due to another). This distinction is based on whether the evil resides in the essence of the act or arises from external factors.
The source states: 'فعل قبیح کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) قبیح لعینه (۲) قبیح لغیره'.
2
Subclassify qabih li-aynihi
Determine whether the intrinsic evil can be removed under necessity (qabil al-suqut) or not (ghayr qabil al-suqut). Examples: eating carrion can be permitted in dire necessity (removable), while kufr and zina are never permissible (non-removable).
The source divides qabih li-aynihi into 'قبیح لعینہ غیر قابل سقوط' and 'قبیح لعینہ قابل سقوط'.
3
Subclassify qabih li-ghayrihi
Check if the external factor makes the act annexed (mulhaq) to intrinsic evil (like ghasb, because it involves violating another's right) or not annexed (like fasting on Eid, which is good in itself but becomes evil due to neglecting God's hospitality).
The source: 'قبیح لغیرہ ملحق بالتصیح لعینہ' and 'قبیح لغیرہ غیر ملحق'.
4
Apply to new cases
For any given act, first assess its essence: is it inherently blameworthy (like consuming carrion) or neutral/positive (like selling)? Then examine external circumstances: does a necessity exist? Does the context impose prohibition?
Use the example of selling during Friday call: selling is permissible in essence, but the call makes it qabih li-ghayrihi.
5
Derive the ruling
Based on the classification, determine the hukm: acts qabih li-aynihi non-removable are always haram; removable ones become haram unless necessity lifts the prohibition; acts qabih li-ghayrihi are normally permissible but become makruh or haram due to the external factor (e.g., selling during Friday call is makruh tahrimi).
The ruling depends on the strength of the external prohibition and the presence of necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله. وهكذا اقسام القبح. یعنی فعل حسن کی طرح فعل قبیح کی بھی قسمیں ہیں ۔ جن کا اجمالا تذکرہ ہو چکا ہے یہاں ذیل میں اس کی مثالیں ذکر کی جاتی ہیں بقیہ وسائط کی تفصیل کو حسن کے وسائط پر قیاس کرنا چاہئے ۔ فعل قبیح کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) قبیح لعینه (۲) قبیح لغیره فتیح لعینہ : یہ ہے کہ قطع نظر اوصاف لازمہ اور عوارض مجاورہ کے جس کی ذات قبیح ہو پھر اس کی دوقسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) قبیح لعینہ غیر قابل سقوط جیسے کفر وشرک، زنا وغیرہ (۲) قبیح لعینہ قابل سقوط ۔ جیسے اکل میتہ کی حرمت و فتح کا سقوط حالت مخمصہ میں ۔ (۲) قبیح لغیرہ ۔ جس کی ذات قبیح نہ ہو بلکہ وصف خارج کی وجہ سے اس میں قبح آیا ہو۔ پھر اس کی بھی دو قسمیں ہیں ۔ (۱) قبیح لغیرہ ملحق بالتصیح لعینہ ، جسے غصب جو کہ حرام ہے کہ اس میں غیر کا حق وابستہ ہے لیکن یہ واسطہ مصدرہ ہے اس لئے غصب قبیح لعینہ کے ساتھ ملحق ہے۔ (۲) قبیح لغیرہ غیر ملحق بالتصیح لعینہ :۔ جیسے صوم یوم عید ۔ کہ صوم فی نفسہ حسن ہے مگر ضیافتہ اللہ سے اعراض کی وجہ سے یوم عید میں صوم قبیح ہے اور جیسے بیج بوقت ندا قبیح ہے کہ فوات جمعہ کی طرف مفضی ہے ورنہ فی نفسہ بیع مباح ہے ارشاد ہے اصل اللہ البیع وحرم الرباء ۔
His statement: 'And thus are the divisions of evil.' That is, just as good actions have divisions, evil actions also have divisions. Their summary has already been mentioned; here examples are given. The remaining details of intermediaries should be analogized to the intermediaries of good. Evil actions are of two types: (1) Evil in itself (qabih li-aynihi) and (2) Evil due to another (qabih li-ghayrihi). Evil in itself: it is that whose essence is evil regardless of necessary attributes and adjacent accidents. Then it has two types: (1) Evil in itself that cannot be removed, such as disbelief, polytheism, adultery, etc. (2) Evil in itself that can be removed, such as the prohibition of eating carrion and its permissibility in dire necessity. (2) Evil due to another: that whose essence is not evil, but evil enters it due to an external attribute. This also has two types: (1) Evil due to another annexed to evil in itself, such as usurpation (ghasb), which is prohibited because it involves the right of another, but this (the right) is a source intermediary, so usurpation is annexed to evil in itself. (2) Evil due to another not annexed to evil in itself: such as fasting on the day of Eid. Fasting is good in itself, but it becomes evil on Eid due to turning away from God's hospitality. Similarly, selling during the call to prayer is evil because it leads to missing Friday prayer; otherwise, selling is permissible in itself. The command is: 'God has permitted selling and prohibited usury.'
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a classification of evil actions (qabih) in Usul al-Fiqh. It begins by analogizing that just as good actions have divisions, so do evil actions. The division is binary: evil in itself (qabih li-aynihi) and evil due to another (qabih li-ghayrihi). Evil in itself is further divided into that which can be removed (like eating carrion becoming permissible in necessity) and that which cannot be removed (like disbelief and adultery). Evil due to another is also subdivided: some cases are annexed to evil in itself (like usurpation, because it involves violating someone's right, which is akin to intrinsic evil) and others are not annexed (like fasting on Eid or selling during the Friday call to prayer). The examples illustrate how the same act can be praiseworthy in one context and blameworthy in another, depending on external factors.

Key Terms
قبيح لعينه (qabīḥ li-ʿaynihi): Evil in itself due to its essence, regardless of context.
قبيح لغيره (qabīḥ li-ghayrihi): Evil due to an external factor, not from its own essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of qabih li-aynihi qabil al-suqut (removable intrinsic evil)?
A) Eating carrion without necessity
B) Disbelief (kufr)
C) Eating carrion in dire necessity
D) Fasting on Eid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of evil actions into intrinsic and extrinsic types allows for temporary permission under necessity for some intrinsically evil acts, while others remain absolutely prohibited.

Divisions of Qabih: Intrinsic and Extrinsic Evil
Explaining the two categories of evil acts in Hanafi usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the two main categories of qabih and DISTINGUISH their subtypes with examples from the Hanafi usul tradition.

Core Idea
An act's evil may be intrinsic to its essence or derived from external circumstances; knowing this determines if it can be overridden by necessity.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not all evil acts are treated the same. This passage from a classical commentary clarifies that acts like kufr and zina are evil in themselves, while others become evil only due to external factors like violating another's right or missing a time-bound obligation. Understanding this classification is key to grasping how rulings can change under necessity or special circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
Start by recognizing that qabih is divided into qabih li-aynihi (intrinsically evil) and qabih li-ghayrihi (extrinsically evil). The defining feature is whether the evil is part of the act's essence or arises from an external attribute.
2
Analyze the subtypes of intrinsic evil
Within intrinsic evil, note two subtypes: those that cannot be removed under any circumstance (e.g., kufr, shirk, zina) and those that can be removed due to dire necessity (e.g., eating carrion when starving). This distinction shows that even intrinsic prohibitions can be lifted for preservation of life.
3
Analyze the subtypes of extrinsic evil
Extrinsic evil also has two types: those that are annexed to intrinsically evil acts because they involve another's right (e.g., ghasb, which violates ownership) and those that are not so annexed (e.g., fasting on Eid, which turns from good to evil due to the occasion, or selling during the Friday call to prayer, which leads to missing the obligatory prayer).
4
Apply to examples from the text
Work through the examples given: carrion in desperation (intrinsic, removable), ghasb (extrinsic, annexed), fasting on Eid (extrinsic, not annexed). This solidifies the conceptual framework.
5
Relate to Hanafi usul methodology
Recognize that this classification impacts istinbat (derivation of rulings). For instance, the prohibition of ghasb is treated as severe because it is annexed to intrinsic evil, while selling during the call to prayer is considered makruh haram but not as severe because the evil is external and can be removed by performing the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله. وهكذا اقسام القبح. یعنی فعل حسن کی طرح فعل قبیح کی بھی قسمیں ہیں۔ جن کا اجمالا تذکرہ ہو چکا ہے یہاں ذیل میں اس کی مثالیں ذکر کی جاتی ہیں بقیہ وسائط کی تفصیل کو حسن کے وسائط پر قیاس کرنا چاہئے۔ فعل قبیح کی دو قسمیں ہیں: (۱) قبیح لعینه (۲) قبیح لغیره۔ فقبیح لعینہ: یہ ہے کہ قطع نظر اوصاف لازمہ اور عوارض مجاورہ کے جس کی ذات قبیح ہو پھر اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں: (۱) قبیح لعینہ غیر قابل سقوط جیسے کفر وشرک، زنا وغیرہ (۲) قبیح لعینہ قابل سقوط۔ جیسے اکل میتہ کی حرمت و قبح کا سقوط حالت مخمصہ میں۔ (۲) قبیح لغیرہ: جس کی ذات قبیح نہ ہو بلکہ وصف خارج کی وجہ سے اس میں قبح آیا ہو۔ پھر اس کی بھی دو قسمیں ہیں: (۱) قبیح لغیرہ الحق بالتصحیح عیہ، جیسے غصب جو کہ حرام ہے کہ اس میں غیر کا حق وابستہ ہے لیکن یہ واسطہ مصدرہ ہے اس لئے غصب قبیح لعینہ کے ساتھ ملحق ہے۔ (۲) قبیح لغیرہ غیر احق بالتصیح لعینہ: جیسے صوم یوم عید۔ کہ صوم فی نفسہ حسن ہے مگر ضیافت اللہ سے اعراض کی وجہ سے یوم عید میں صوم قبیح ہے اور جیسے بیع بوقت ندا قبیح ہے کہ فوات جمعہ کی طرف مفضی ہے ورنہ فی نفسہ بیع مباح ہے ارشاد ہے أحل الله البيع وحرم الرباء۔
His statement: And thus the divisions of evil. That is, just as the good act has divisions, so too does the evil act have divisions that have been mentioned in summary; here below examples are given. The detail of the remaining means should be analogized to the means of good. Evil act has two types: (1) Intrinsically evil (qabih li-aynihi) (2) Extrinsically evil (qabih li-ghayrihi). Intrinsically evil: it is that whose essence is evil disregarding necessary attributes and accompanying accidents. Then it has two subtypes: (1) Intrinsically evil that cannot be removed, like disbelief, polytheism, adultery, etc. (2) Intrinsically evil that can be removed, like the prohibition and evil of eating carrion that is removed in a state of desperation. (2) Extrinsically evil: that whose essence is not evil but evil enters into it due to an external attribute. Then it also has two types: (1) Extrinsically evil that is attached to what is intrinsically evil due to a right from another, like usurpation (ghasb) which is prohibited because it involves another's right; but this means is from the source, so usurpation is annexed to intrinsically evil. (2) Extrinsically evil that is not attached to what is intrinsically evil: such as fasting on the day of Eid; fasting in itself is good but due to turning away from the feast of Allah, fasting on the day of Eid is evil; and such as selling at the time of the call (to Friday prayer) is evil because it leads to missing Friday prayer; otherwise in itself selling is permissible. The guidance states: Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary on the divisions of evil (qabih) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author explains that just as good (husn) has types, so does evil. He divides evil into two main categories: intrinsically evil (qabih li-aynihi) and extrinsically evil (qabih li-ghayrihi). Intrinsically evil is further subdivided into that which cannot be removed (e.g., kufr, shirk, zina) and that which can be removed due to necessity (e.g., eating carrion when starving). Extrinsically evil is also subdivided into that which is attached to the intrinsically evil due to violation of another's right (e.g., ghusb, which is annexed to intrinsically evil because it involves a right of another), and that which is not so attached (e.g., fasting on Eid, which is good in itself but becomes evil due to the occasion; or selling during the Friday call to prayer, which leads to missing the prayer, though selling in itself is halal). The author cites the Quranic verse 'Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury' to show that selling in itself is permissible. This classification is foundational for understanding how acts acquire their legal rulings in Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
قبيح لعينه (qabih li-aynihi): Evil by virtue of its own essence, regardless of external factors.
قبيح لغيره (qabih li-ghayrihi): Evil due to an external attribute or circumstance, not by its own essence.
قابل للسقوط (qabil li al-suqut): Capable of being removed or overridden, as in the case of darura (necessity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of intrinsically evil (qabih li-aynihi) that can be removed under necessity?
A) Kufr (disbelief)
B) Zina (adultery)
C) Eating carrion when starving
D) Usurpation (ghasb)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the classification of an act as qabih li-aynihi or qabih li-ghayrihi determines both the source of its prohibition and the possibility of its removal under necessity.

The Hanafi Definition of Hukm
Definition of a key usul term with objections and critiques

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hukm, identify its essential elements, and apply it to distinguish between different types of divine address.

Core Idea
Hukm is Allah's address requiring or permitting an action of a responsible person—not every divine utterance.

In Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh, the term 'ḥukm' is defined with precision. This lesson unpacks the classical definition from the matn, explores objections about prophetic and master's commands, and examines Taftazānī's critique of a variant phrasing. By understanding this definition, you will be able to classify divine addresses correctly and avoid conflating informative verses with legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Isolate the definition
Extract the exact definition given in the matn: 'It is the address of Allah related to the act of the mukallaf by way of requirement or option.' Note the key components: khāṭib (Allah), muḍāf ilayh (the mukallaf's act), and the nature of the address (iqtidā' or takhyīr).
The Arabic reads: خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بفعل المكلف اقتضاء أو تخييرا.
2
Analyze the qualifications
Break down each part: 'address of Allah' excludes speech of angels, jinn, or humans; 'related to the act of the mukallaf' excludes informative verses about creation or attributes; 'requirement or option' distinguishes commands/prohibitions from permissibility.
The commentator explains that 'khitāb' here means 'directed speech' (al-kalām al-muwajjah).
3
Understand the objection and response
The objection: The Prophet's commands or a master's commands are also called ḥukm and are obligatory. The response: Their obligation ultimately derives from Allah's command; thus they are included in the definition indirectly.
The verse 'Whoever obeys the Messenger has obeyed Allah' (Q.4:80) is cited.
4
Evaluate Taftazānī's critique
Taftazānī criticizes those who define ḥukm as 'related to the acts of the responsible people' (plural). He argues that this would imply a ruling must apply to all mukallafīn collectively, which is not the case; each individual act has its own ruling.
This highlights the importance of wording in legal definitions.

الباب الثانى فى الحكم وهو عندنا خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بفعل المكلف اقتضاء او تخييراً فنحو و الله خلقكم وما تعملون ليس منه ترجمہ :۔ باب دوم حکم میں ہے اور حکم ہمارے نزدیک اللہ تعالیٰ کا وہ خطاب ہے جو فعل مکلف سے بطور اقتضاء وتخیر متعلق ہوپس و الله خلقكم و ما تعملون " جیسی آیات حکم سے نہیں ہیں۔ تشریح : ۔ مقدمہ میں معلوم ہو چکا ہے کہ یہ کتاب ایک مقدمہ، تین مقالات اور ایک خاتمہ پر مشتمل ہے۔ مقالہ اولی ، کلام میں اور مقالہ ثانیہ، احکام کے بیان میں تھا اور مقالہ ثانیہ چار ابواب پر مشتمل تھا، باب اول حکم کے بیان میں جسکی شرح گذری۔ اب یہاں مقالہ ثانیہ کے چار ابواب میں سے باب دوم کا ذکر ہے جس میں حکم کی بحث ہے اس لئے مصنف نے کہا۔ قوله وهو عند نا خطاب الله الخ اس عبارت سے ماتن نے حکم کی تعریف بیان کی ہے کہ ۔ حکم ہم معاشر اہلسنت کے نزدیک اللہ تعالیٰ کا وہ خطاب ہے جو مکلف ( عاقل بالغ ) کے افعال سے حتماً واباحی متعلق ہو۔ خطاب لغت میں " توجیہ الکلام نحو الغير لا فہام کو کہتے ہیں یعنی دوسروں کو سمجھانے کے لئے کلام کو متوجہ کرنا۔ مگر اس جگہ خطاب مصدر بول کر مفعول مراد لیا گیا ہے اس لئے " الکلام الموجہ" کے معنی میں ہے۔ چنانچہ مصنف حاشیہ میں رقمطراز ہیں۔ الخطاب لغة توجيه الكلام نحو الغير للافهام ثم نقل الى الكلام الموجه كذا ذكر السيد قدس سره فوائد قیود : - خطاب کی اضافت اللہ کی طرف کر کے غیر اللہ مثلا ملئکہ اور جن وانس کے خطاب کو حد حکم سے خارج کرنا ہے کہ "لا حکم الا للہ ثابت ہے۔ اعتراض:۔ خطاب رسول امتی کے حق میں، خطاب مولی وسید ان کے غلام باندی کے حق میں حکم کہلاتا ہے چنانچہ اس لئے اس کی بجا آوری امتی پر اور غلام باندی پر عند الشرع بھی لازم ہے پس حکم کی تعریف میں غیر اللہ کا خطاب داخل ہو گیا اور تعریف دخول غیر سے مانع نہ رہی۔ جواب : حکم رسول یا حکم سید و آقا کی اطاعت کا وجوب در حقیقت اللہ تعالیٰ ہی کے حکم سے ثابت ہے۔ یا آقا کی اطاعت کا وجوب غلام کے حق میں حکم رسول ہے اور حکم رسول حکم الہی ہے ارشاد باری تعالیٰ ہے من اطاع الرسول فقد اطاع الله - حاصل یہ کہ آقا کی اطاعت کا وجوب حکم رسول سے ثابت ہے اور حکم رسول کی اطاعت کا وجوب حکم الہی سے ثابت ہے اس لئے رسول کا حکم امتی کو خواہ سید کا حکم غلام کو در حقیقت اللہ ہی کا حکم ہے۔ اپنے المتعلق بفعل المکلف سے ان خطاب کو نکالنا ہے جو خطاب اللہ تو ہے لیکن حکم پر مشتمل نہیں ہے جیسے وہ آیات مبارکہ جو قصص و امثال اور ذات وصفات باری تعالیٰ کے متعلق ہیں۔ فعل المکلف میں فعل فعل جوارح اور فعل قلب دونوں کو عام ہے۔ یادر ہے کہ حکم کی یہی تعریف صدر الشریعہ، امام غزالی اور علامہ ابن حاجب سے بھی منقول ہے مگر ان کی تعریف میں قدرے لفظی فرق ہے چنانچہ ان لوگوں نے فعل المکلف" کے بجائے بافعال المکلفین " کہا ہے یعنی فعل کی جگہ افعال اور مکلف کے بجائے مکلفین جمع استعمال کیا ہے جب کہ اکثر نے واحد استعمال کیا ہے۔ تفتازانی کا تعقب:۔ امام غزالی وصدر الشریعہ وغیرھا جن علمائے اصول نے حکم کی تعریف بافعال المکلفین سے کیا ہے علامہ تفتازانی نے ان پر تعقب کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے کہ ان کے قول لمکلفین کو اگر اس کے ظاہر معنی مراد پرمحمول کیا جائے تو یہ تعریف احکام میں سے کسی شئی کو شامل لمکلفین" کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ جملہ مکلفین کے جمیع افعال ا نہ ہوگی کیونکہ معنی ظاہر مراد لینے کی تقدیر پر افعال سے جو خطاب متعلق ہے وہ حکم ہے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں اس لئے کہ کسی بھی حکم پر یہ صادق نہیں آتا
The Second Chapter: On the Legal Ruling (Hukm). According to us, it is the address of Allah the Exalted related to the act of the responsible person (mukallaf) by way of requirement or option. Thus verses like 'And Allah created you and what you do' are not from it. Translation: The second chapter concerns hukm, and hukm according to us is the address of Allah related to the act of the mukallaf by way of requirement or option. Thus verses like 'And Allah created you and what you do' are not hukm. Elaboration: It has been known in the introduction that this book consists of an introduction, three discourses, and a conclusion. The first discourse was on speech, the second was on rulings, and the second discourse comprises four chapters. The first chapter was on hukm, its commentary passed. Now here is mention of the second chapter among the four chapters of the second discourse, which discusses hukm. Therefore the author said: His statement 'And according to us it is the address of Allah...' With this expression, the author of the matn defines hukm: Hukm, according to us the Ahl al-Sunnah, is the address of Allah related necessarily or permissively to the actions of the mukallaf (sane, adult). Khitab linguistically means directing speech towards another for understanding. But here, khitab is used as a verbal noun meaning the directed speech. Thus the commentator writes in the marginal notes: 'Khitab linguistically is directing speech towards another for understanding, then it was transferred to mean the directed speech, as mentioned by al-Sayyid (may his secret be sanctified).' Benefits of the qualifications: Adding the address to Allah excludes the address of other than Allah, such as angels and jinn and humans, from the definition of hukm, because 'there is no hukm except for Allah' is established. Objection: The address of the Messenger for the ummati, and the address of the master and lord for his slave, are called hukm. So their compliance is obligatory for the ummati and the slave according to the Shariah. Thus the address of other than Allah enters the definition of hukm, and the definition is not prevented from inclusion. Response: The obligation of obeying the hukm of the Messenger or the master is in reality established by the hukm of Allah. Or the obligation of obeying the master for the slave is the hukm of the Messenger, and the hukm of the Messenger is the hukm of Allah. Allah said: 'Whoever obeys the Messenger has obeyed Allah.' The conclusion is that the Messenger's hukm for the ummati or the master's hukm for the slave is in reality the hukm of Allah. 'Related to the act of the mukallaf' excludes that address which is from Allah but does not contain a ruling, such as the blessed verses concerning stories, parables, and the essence and attributes of Allah. 'Act of the mukallaf' includes acts of the limbs and acts of the heart. Note: This same definition of hukm is transmitted from Sadr al-Shariah, Imam al-Ghazali, and Allamah Ibn al-Hajib, but there is a slight verbal difference in their definitions: they used 'b-af'al al-mukallafeen' (by the acts of the responsible people) instead of 'fi'l al-mukallaf' (act of the responsible person), i.e., they used plural 'af'al' and 'mukallafeen' while the majority used singular. Taftazani's critique: Taftazani criticized those ulema of usul like Imam al-Ghazali and Sadr al-Shariah who defined hukm with 'b-af'al al-mukallafeen'. He said that if their statement is interpreted according to its apparent meaning, then this definition would not include any ruling because the address related to the acts of all mukallafeen is hukm, but that is not the case.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the technical term 'hukm' (legal ruling) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author of the matn defines hukm as 'the address of Allah the Exalted related to the act of the mukallaf by way of requirement (iqtida') or option (takhyir).' This means that Allah's speech (the Qur'an or Sunnah) that either commands, prohibits, or gives a choice concerning the actions of a legally responsible person (mukallaf) is what constitutes a hukm. Verses that are purely informational, such as 'And Allah created you and what you do,' are not considered hukm in this technical sense because they do not impose a requirement or give an option. The commentator then explains each part: 'khitab' (address) is defined linguistically and then technically as 'the directed speech.' The qualification 'of Allah' excludes the address of angels, jinn, or humans. An objection is raised that the commands of the Prophet and of a master are also called hukm, but the response is that their authority ultimately derives from Allah's command, so they are included in Allah's address indirectly. The phrase 'related to the act of the mukallaf' excludes Allah's speech about stories or attributes. 'Mukallaf' means a sane, adult person. The commentator notes that Sadr al-Shariah, Ghazali, and Ibn al-Hajib defined hukm similarly but used the plural 'af'al al-mukallafeen' (actions of the responsible people). Taftazani critiqued this plural version, arguing that if taken literally, it would imply that a ruling must apply to the collective actions of all responsible persons, which is not true; rather, each individual act has its own ruling.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-ḥukm): The address of Allah related to the act of the responsible person by way of requirement or option.
الخطاب (al-khiṭāb): The directed speech (al-kalām al-muwajjah) for understanding.
المكلف (al-mukallaf): A sane, adult person who is addressed by the Law.
الاقتضاء (al-iqtiḍā): A demand (requirement) from the address, such as a command or prohibition.
التخيير (al-takhyīr): Giving an option, such as permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, which of the following is considered a hukm?
A) A verse narrating the story of the prophets
B) A verse commanding prayer
C) A verse describing the creation of the heavens
D) A verse mentioning the attributes of Allah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm restricts it to Allah's address that imposes a requirement or grants an option regarding the acts of a responsible person, excluding pure reports and indirect addresses.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Hukm: Taftazani's Critique and Refinement
Refines the definition of hukm by addressing Taftazani's objection to plural wording and explains the five categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hukm, identify the function of each qualification, and explain how Taftazani's objection to the plural wording is resolved through genus-to-genus interpretation.

Core Idea
Hukm is divine address concerning action; plural wording does not imply totality but genus relation.

In this lesson, we delve into the precise definition of hukm (divine ruling) as formulated by Hanafi usul scholars. The definition is carefully crafted with several qualifications to exclude non-legal addresses. A notable point of discussion is the use of plural wording ('actions of the responsible persons') by some authorities, which Taftazani critiqued. We will see how the Hanafi tradition responds, preserving the definition's validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and its exclusions
Note the full definition: 'the divine address related to the action of the responsible person by way of requirement or permission.' Consider each qualification: address attributed to Allah (خِطاب) excludes non-divine sources; 'related to the action of the responsible person' excludes non-legal narratives; 'requirement or permission' sets the scope of rulings.
This definition is from Sadr al-Sharia, Ghazali, and Ibn Hajib with slight wording variations.
2
Examine the objection regarding non-divine address
Consider the objection: if only Allah's address is hukm, then the Prophet's commands and a master's orders would not be hukm. The response: their authority is derived from Allah (Quran 4:80). Thus, they are essentially divine and included.
This is a key point: ultimate authority rests with Allah, so indirect commands are subsumed.
3
Analyze Taftazani's critique of the plural wording
Taftazani objects that the phrase 'with the actions of the responsible persons' (بافعال المکلفین), if taken literally, would require a ruling to relate to all actions of all responsible persons, which is false. Understand why this is a problem for the definition.
This critique targets the wording used by Ghazali and others.
4
Apply the genus-to-genus interpretation
The resolution is that the plural indicates a genus-to-genus relation, not totality. Use the example 'Zaid is a rider of horses' – Zaid rides some horses, not all. Similarly, the genus of divine address relates to the genus of actions; the specific ruling applies to an individual instance.
Sayyid Muttafaq provided this clarification, showing the plural is not problematic.
5
Extract the five categories from 'requirement or option'
The passage concludes by mapping the five rulings: definitive demand for action = wujub; non-definitive = mandub; definitive demand for abandonment = haram; non-definitive = karahah; option = mubah. This shows how the definition encompasses the entire fivefold classification.
This step confirms the practicality of the definition.

فوائد قيود : - خطاب کی اضافت اللہ کی طرف کر کے غیر اللہ مثلا ملئکہ اور جن وانس کے خطاب کو حد حکم سے خارج کرنا ہے کہ "لا حکم الا للہ ثابت ہے۔
اعتراض:۔ خطاب رسول امتی کے حق میں، خطاب مولی وسید ان کے غلام باندی کے حق میں حکم کہلاتا ہے چنانچہ اس لئے اس کی بجا آوری امتی پر اور غلام باندی پر عند الشرع بھی لازم ہے پس حکم کی تعریف میں غیر اللہ کا خطاب داخل ہو گیا اور تعریف دخول غیر سے مانع نہ رہی۔

پس مراد، افعال سے بفعل ما ہے یعنی مکلف کے کسی فعل سے جو بھی خطاب متعلق ہو حکم ہے۔ اسکی کامل توضیح سید متفق قدس سرہ نے کی ہے کہ انکا قول "بافعال المکلفین زید مرکب الخیل کے قبیل سے ہے
حالانکہ زید بیک وقت ایک ہی فرس پر سوار ہوسکتا ہے لیکن، زید بر کب الخیل" کہنا صحیح ۔ اسی طرح افعال المکلفین ' کہنا درست ہے گرچہ حکم پر ایک ہی فعل کا اطلاق ہے اور ایسا بھی نہیں کہ یہاں جمع بولکر واحد مراد لیا گیا ہے بلکہ یہاں یہ مفہوم ہے کہ زید کا رکوب اس مجموعہ خیل کے جنس سے متعلق ہے مجموعہ کمار کے جنس سے نہیں مثلاً ۔ ایسے ہی انکے قول "بافعال المتکلفین " کامعنی ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے خطاب کا جنس مکلف کے جنس فعل سے تعلق حکم کہلاتا ہے یہ معنی نہیں ہیکہ جمیع مکلفین کے جمیع افعال سے تعلق کا نام حکم ہے اس لئے کہ آخر الذکر مفہوم ظاہر البطلان ہے
الغرض حکم کی تعریف ہر مکلف کے فعل سے متعلق خطاب کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہے بلکہ اس خطاب کو شامل ہے جو خطاب متعلق ہو ایسے فعل سے جو مکلف کے ساتھ مختص ہے پس اس تاویل سے حضورسید عالم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ساتھ مختص افعال و خواص اور شہادت حضرت خزیمہ جیسے فعل سے اعتراض نہ پڑیگا کہ حکم کی تعریف جامع نہیں ہے!
قوله " اقتضاء او تخییراً الخ ماتن نے اپنے قول اقتضاء او خیر اسے تعریف حکم کے تمہ کے ساتھ اسکے اقسام خمسہ کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے نیز تعریف حکم پر چند وجوہ سے اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے اسکے جواب کی طرف اشارہ ہے معنی یہ ہے کہ ہر خطاب حکم نہیں ہوگا بلکہ وہ خطاب الہی جو فعل عبد کے ساتھ بطور طلب یا بطور اباحت متعلق ہو وہ حکم ہوگا۔
یا در ہے کہ طلب و اباحت احکام خمسہ مشہورہ کو عام ہے۔ اس لئے کہ خطاب یا تو طلب سے متعلق ہوگا یا اباحت سے متعلق ہوگا۔ برشق ثانی مباح ہوگا اور بر تقدیر اول (یعنی خطاب طلب سے متعلق ہوگا) وہ طلب فعل سے متعلق ہوگا یا طلب ترک فعل سے متعلق ہوگا بہر دو نقد بر طلب حتمی ہوگا یا طلب غیر حتمی ہوگا اگر طلب فعل حتمی ہے تو وہ و جوب ہے اور اگر طلب ترک فعل حتمی ہے تو حرام ہے اور اگر طلب فعل غیر حتمی ہے تو مندب اور ترک فعل غیر حتمی ہے تو کراہت ۔
Benefits of restrictions: - Adding the address to Allah excludes the address of others like angels and jinn from the definition of hukm, because "there is no ruling except from Allah" is established. Objection: The address of the Messenger to his community and the address of a master to his slave is called hukm. Therefore its fulfillment is incumbent upon the community and slave according to the Sharia. So the address of other than Allah enters the definition of hukm and the definition fails to exclude others. Response: The obligation to obey the ruling of the Messenger or the master is in reality established by Allah's command. The obligation to obey the master for the slave is a ruling of the Messenger, and the ruling of the Messenger is a divine ruling. Allah says: "Whoever obeys the Messenger has obeyed Allah." So the Messenger's ruling over the community and the master's ruling over the slave are in reality Allah's ruling. The phrase 'related to the action of the responsible person' excludes those addresses that are from Allah but do not contain a ruling, such as verses about stories, parables, attributes of Allah. 'Action of the responsible person' includes actions of the limbs and actions of the heart. Note that this definition of hukm is transmitted from Sadr al-Sharia, Imam Ghazali, and Allama Ibn Hajib, but there is a slight verbal difference: they used 'with the actions of the responsible persons (plural)' instead of 'action of the responsible person (singular)', using plural for both 'action' and 'responsible person', while most used the singular. Taftazani's objection: Imam Ghazali, Sadr al-Sharia, and other usul scholars who defined hukm with 'actions of the responsible persons', Allama Taftazani objected to them, saying that if their statement 'actions of the responsible persons' is taken in its apparent meaning, this definition would not include any of the rulings because the apparent meaning of 'actions of the responsible persons' would be the totality of actions of all responsible persons, but no ruling is related to all actions of all responsible persons. So the intended meaning is 'some action', i.e., any action of the responsible person to which the address is related is a ruling. Sayyid Muttafaq (may his secret be sanctified) gave a complete explanation: their statement 'with the actions of the responsible persons' is like 'Zaid is a rider of horses' even though Zaid can only ride one horse at a time, but it is correct to say 'Zaid is a rider of horses'. Similarly, saying 'actions of the responsible persons' is correct even though the ruling applies to a single action. It is not that here plural is used but singular is intended; rather, the meaning is that Zaid's riding is related to the genus of horses, not to the genus of donkeys. Similarly, their statement 'with the actions of the responsible persons' means that the genus of Allah's address related to the genus of the action of the responsible person is called hukm. It does not mean that the relation to all actions of all responsible persons is called hukm, because the latter meaning is obviously false. In short, the definition of hukm is not restricted to the address related to the action of each responsible person individually, but includes the address related to an action that is specific to a responsible person. Thus, with this interpretation, the objection regarding acts specific to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the testimony of Hadhrat Khuzayma (like an action specific to a person) does not arise that the definition is not comprehensive. His statement 'requirement or option etc.': The matn author indicates with his statement 'requirement or option' the five categories of hukm, and also indicates the response to several objections on the definition. The meaning is that not every address is a ruling, but that divine address which is related to the action of the servant in the manner of demand or permissibility is a ruling. Demand and permissibility encompass the well-known five rulings. Because the address is either related to demand or to permissibility. In the second case, it will be permissible (mubah). In the first case (the address is related to demand), that demand is either for action or for abandonment. In both cases, the demand is either definitive or non-definitive. If the demand for action is definitive, it is obligation (wujub); if for abandonment definitively, it is prohibition (haram); if for action non-definitively, it is recommended (mandub); and if for abandonment non-definitively, it is disliked (karahah).
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of hukm (divine ruling) from the matn of Muslim al-Thubut. It begins by explaining the qualifications in the definition: first, the address is attributed to Allah to exclude non-divine sources; second, the address must be related to the action of the responsible person (mukallaf) to exclude non-legal narratives. The commentator anticipates an objection: if Allah's address alone is considered, then the rulings of the Prophet and a master would be excluded, but they are valid in Sharia. The response is that their authority is ultimately derived from Allah: obeying the Prophet is obeying Allah (Quran 4:80), and obeying the master is a command of the Prophet, which is itself Allah's command. Thus, they are included within the definition because they are essentially divine. Next, the phrase 'related to the action of the responsible person' excludes verses that do not contain legal commands, such as stories or theological descriptions. The passage then notes a variation in wording: some scholars (like Sanad al-Sharia, Ghazali, Ibn Hajib) define hukm as 'the address related to the actions of the responsible persons' (plural), while others use the singular. Taftazani criticizes the plural wording, arguing that if taken literally, it would imply that a ruling must relate to all actions of all responsible persons, which is false. The solution is that the plural indicates genus-to-genus relation, not totality. The example 'Zaid is a rider of horses' illustrates that one can attribute a genus action even if only one instance occurs. Thus, the definition means that the genus of divine address relates to the genus of actions of responsible persons, and that specific manifestation is called hukm. This interpretation resolves objections regarding acts specific to the Prophet (like extra prayers) or individual cases like the testimony of Khuzayma, which are still included because they relate to the action of a responsible person. Finally, the passage introduces the qualification 'demand or option' from the matn, indicating that a ruling is either a demand (for action or abandonment) or a permission (ibaha). The demand can be definitive (wujub or haram) or non-definitive (mandub or karahah). This yields the famous five categories of hukm: wujub, haram, mandub, karahah, and ibaha. The commentator thus confirms the definition and defends it against objections.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): Divine address related to the action of a responsible person, involving demand or permission
خطاب (khitab): Address from Allah (or indirectly from Him) that conveys a ruling
فعل المكلف (fi'l al-mukallaf): Action of the legally responsible person, both physical and mental
اقتضاء (iqtida'): Demand for action or abandonment, either definitive or non-definitive

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does Taftazani's objection to the definition 'address related to the actions of the responsible persons' (بافعال المکلفین) get resolved?
A) The plural is used to indicate all actions of all responsible persons at once.
B) The plural is interpreted to mean 'some action' and the relation is genus-to-genus, not individual totality.
C) The definition is rejected and a new one is proposed.
D) Taftazani's objection is incorrect because the ruling applies to every single action of every person.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm is precise: divine address related to action with demand or permission, and the plural wording is reconciled via genus interpretation.

Definition of Hukm and Its Five Categories
Definition of hukm with five-category division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hukm according to the Hanafi school, explain its scope using the 'genus of actions' clarification, and list the five categories with their distinguishing criteria.

Core Idea
Hukm is Allah's address related to the mukallaf's act with demand or option, yielding five categories: wajib, haram, mandub, makruh, and mubah.

This passage presents the foundational Hanafi definition of hukm (shar'i ruling). The author clarifies that hukm is specifically Allah's address that relates to the action of the legally responsible person (mukallaf) in terms of demand (iqtida') or option (takhyir). By understanding that the address relates to the genus of actions rather than every individual act, potential objections are resolved. The definition then naturally divides into the five known categories through a logical subdivision of demand and option.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of hukm
Identify the definition: hukm is Allah's address (khitab) that relates to the action of the mukallaf. Note the nuance: the address relates to an action (fi'l ma), not all actions collectively.
The definition restricts hukm to addresses that carry a demand or option, excluding mere informative statements.
2
Understand the 'genus of actions' clarification
The analogy 'Zaid is a horse rider' shows that the predicate relates to the genus of horses, not every horse. Similarly, Allah's address relates to the genus of actions of the mukallaf, not every individual action. This prevents the objection that the definition would require a relation to all actions of all mukallaf.
The author uses this to include special cases (Prophet's specific acts, Khuzayma's testimony) because they are still actions of a mukallaf.
3
Identify the two main branches: demand and option
The matn's phrase 'demand or option' indicates the two overarching categories. If the address is by way of option (takhyir), it yields mubah. If by way of demand (iqtida'), it further divides.
Takhyir means the person is free to do or leave the action.
4
Subdivide demand into action and abandonment
Demand (iqtida') is either a demand to perform an action (talab al-fi'l) or a demand to abandon (talab al-tark). This is the next logical split.
5
Subdivide each into determined and non-determined
Each demand can be determined (hatmi) – required without concession – or non-determined (ghayr hatmi) – encouraged but not binding. Determined demand to act = wajib, determined demand to abandon = haram; non-determined demand to act = mandub, non-determined demand to abandon = makruh. Combined with mubah, we get five categories.
This classification is the standard Hanafi taxonomy of hukm taklifi.

That it is such an address that is related to all actions of the obligated persons. So the meaning is from actions is 'by an action' meaning whatever address is related to any action of the obligated person is a ruling. Its complete explanation was given by Sayyid Mutafaq (may his secret be sanctified) that his saying 'by the actions of the obligated persons' is like 'Zaid is a horse rider' even though Zaid can ride only one horse at a time, but saying 'Zaid is a horse rider' is correct. Similarly, saying 'actions of the obligated persons' is correct even though the ruling applies to one action. And it is not that here the plural is used meaning the singular, rather here the meaning is that Zaid's riding pertains to the genus of the totality of horses, not to the genus of the totality of mules, for example. Similarly, his saying 'by the actions of the obligated persons' means that the genus of Allah's address being related to the genus of the action of the obligated person is called a ruling. It does not mean that the name of the ruling is the relation to all actions of all obligated persons, because the latter meaning is clearly false. In short, the definition of ruling is not restricted to the address related to the action of every obligated person, rather it includes that address which is related to an action that is specific to the obligated person. Thus, by this interpretation, no objection will arise regarding actions and characteristics specific to the Master of the Worlds (peace be upon him) and actions like the testimony of Hadrat Khuzayma, that the definition of ruling is not comprehensive. His statement 'demand or option, etc.' The Matn author, by his statement 'demand or option', pointed to the five categories along with the preamble of the definition of ruling, and also hinted at the answer to several objections that occur on the definition of ruling. The meaning is that not every address is a ruling, but that divine address which is related to the action of the servant by way of demand or option is a ruling. Or it is that demand and option are general to the well-known five rulings. Because the address will either be related to demand or to option. On the second supposition it will be permissible, and on the first supposition (i.e., the address is related to demand) it will be related to the demand of an action or the demand of abandoning an action. In both cases, it will be either a determined demand or a non-determined demand. If the demand of an action is determined, then it is obligation; if the demand of abandoning an action is determined, then it is prohibition; if the demand of an action is non-determined, then it is recommended; and if the demand of abandoning an action is non-determined, then it is disliked.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the definition of hukm (ruling) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by clarifying that hukm is Allah's address relating to the actions of the mukallaf (obligated person), but this does not mean a blanket relation to all actions; rather, it means the address is connected to the genus of actions of the genus of obligated persons. He provides an analogy: saying 'Zaid is a horse rider' is correct even if Zaid only rides one horse, because the predicate relates to the genus of horses. Similarly, Allah's address relates to the genus of actions. He then responds to a potential objection that this definition would exclude actions specific to the Prophet (SAW) like his special characteristics, or the testimony of Khuzayma — but these are included because the definition covers actions specific to a particular mukallaf. The author then explains the five categories of hukm by analyzing the matn's phrase 'demand or option'. The address either demands something (طلب) or leaves an option (اباحة). Demand further divides into demand to do (فعل) or demand to leave (ترك), and each can be determined (حتمی) or non-determined (غير حتمی). This yields the five: wajib (determined demand to do), haram (determined demand to leave), mandub (non-determined demand to do), makruh (non-determined demand to leave), and mubah (option). This is the standard Hanafi classification.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): الخطاب الإلهي المتعلق بفعل المكلف من حيث هو مكلف
اقتضاء (iqtida'): طلب الفعل أو الترك
تخییر (takhyir): التخيير بين الفعل والترك (الإباحة)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Hukm is precisely Allah's address related to the mukallaf's act with demand or option, logically dividing into the five categories of taklifi rulings: wajib, haram, mandub, makruh, and mubah.

The Condition of Haythiyya in the Definition of Hukm
Addressing objections about including non-taklifi acts in hukm definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of haythiyya (perspective of obligation) to refine the definition of hukm and defend against objections regarding non-taklifi acts.

Core Idea
A valid definition of hukm must be restricted by 'from the perspective of obligation' to exclude non-legislative addresses.

For usul definitions, precision is paramount. The Hanafi definition of hukm as 'Allah's address related to the action of the obligated person' faced objections: first, that it inadvertently includes descriptive verses about actions; second, that acts of ibaha (permission) lack obligation. This lesson unpacks how the implicit condition of haythiyya (being from the perspective of obligation) resolves both objections, and how taklif extends even to seemingly non-demanding rulings through belief and preferential demand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection about creation verses
The first objection claims that verses like 'And Allah created you and what you do' (37:96) are addresses about actions, thus they would be included in the definition of hukm, making it non-mani' (not exclusive).
This objection targets the scope of the definition.
2
Recall the Hanafi definition of hukm
The definition is: Khiṭāb Allāh al-mutaʿalliq bi-fiʿl al-mukallaf. But implicitly it includes 'min ḥaythu huwa mukallaf' (from the perspective that he is obligated).
The haythiyya condition is often assumed but not always stated.
3
Apply the haythiyya restriction
Verses about creation relate to actions from the perspective of divine power, not from the perspective of obligation. Thus they are excluded from the definition, preserving its exclusivity.
The same logic applies to all informational (ikhbarī) verses.
4
Evaluate Taftazani's objection and the response
Taftazani questioned whether acts of ibaha, nadb, and karahah involve taklif. The response: taklif is realized in two ways—(1) belief in the correctness of the ruling is obligatory for all acts, and (2) for nadb/karahah, there is a preferential demand (talab tarjihi) with reward/punishment, which is also taklif.
Thus the haythiyya condition remains valid for all five rulings.

اعتراض : اللہ عز شانہ کا ارشاد والله خلقکم و ماتعملون ایسے ہی خالق کل شئی وغیرھا آیات مبارکہ اللہ کا خطاب ہیں اور بندوں کے افعال سے بھی متعلق ہیں اس لئے اس قسم کی آیتیں حد حکم میں داخل ہو گئیں لہذا احکم کی تعریف دخول غیر سے مانع نہیں رہی۔ جواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ ہر حد میں حیثیت کی قید معتبر ہوتی ہے گرچہ حیثیت کی تصریح اس میں نہ ہو پس حکم کی تعریف میں حیثیت معتبر ہے چنانچہ پوری عبارت اس طرح ہے۔ خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بفعل المكلف من حيث هو مكلف الخ لہذ احکم کی تعریف پر مانعیت سے اعتراض نہ پڑے گا کیونکہ پیش کردہ آیات میں خطاب کا تعلق اس حیثیت سے نہیں ہے کہ وہ فعل عبد ہے۔ مگر حکم کی تعریف میں حیثیت کی قید اعتبار کرنے پر دو وجوہ ہے اعتراض کیا گیا ہے۔ وجہ اول :۔ علامہ تفتازانی نے شرح مختصر کی شرح میں کہا ہے کہ بندہ کے فعل اباحت وندب اور کراہت کے ساتھ خطاب متعلق ہونے میں حیثیت تکلیف کا اعتبار محل نظر ہے۔ جواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ حکم الہی کی اطاعت دو طریقے سے ہوتی ہے۔ حکم الہی کی اطاعت کی ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ اس حکم کے بارے میں اس کے حق ہونے کا اعتقاد رکھا جائے۔ اطاعت کی دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ حکم کے مقتضاء پر عمل کیا جائے۔ پس حکم اباحت میں اگر چہ طلب بشرط مشیت مکلف مشروط ہے کہ عمل مباح میں تکلیف کا تصور نہیں ہوتا تاہم عمل مباح میں اباحت کا اعتقاد بہر حال واجب ہے لہذا حکم اباحت میں باعتبار اعتقاد حقیت تکلیف متحقق ہے یہی حال ندب و کراہت کا بھی ہے چنانچہ فل مندوب میں ندب ہونے کا اعتقاد اور فعل مکروہ میں کراہت کا اعتقاد واجب ہے ۔ بلکہ ان دونوں میں دوسرے اعتبار سے بھی تکلیف متحقق ہے وہ اس طرح کہ ان دونوں (مندوب و مکروہ) میں طلب ترجیحی کے ساتھ تکلیف ہے کہ اول میں مندوب کی بجا آوری پر ثواب دیا جائے گا اور دوم میں مکروہ کے ارتکاب پر عقاب کیا جائے گا۔ وجہ دوم : حکم کی تعریف میں حیثیت مذکورہ کے اعتبار کرنے پر دوسرا اعتراض سید محقق نے کیا ہے۔ کہ الله عز شانہ کا ارشاد "انكم وما تعبدون من دون الله حصب جهنم الآية وعید ہے ؟
Objection: Allah's statement 'And Allah created you and what you do' and similarly 'Creator of all things' and other blessed verses are Allah's addresses and are also related to the actions of servants. Therefore, such verses enter the definition of ruling. Hence the definition of ruling is not prevented from including other things. Response: It is that in every definition, the condition of consideration (haythiyya) is considered even if it is not explicitly mentioned. So in the definition of ruling, consideration is valid. Thus the full expression is: 'Allah's address related to the action of the obligated person from the perspective that he is obligated' etc. Therefore, there will be no objection of non-prevention on the definition of ruling because in the presented verses, the address is not related from the perspective that it is the action of the servant. However, on considering the condition of consideration in the definition of ruling, objections have been made on two grounds. First objection: Allama Taftazani said in his commentary on Mukhtasar that in the address being related to the servant's action of permission, recommendation, and dislike, the consideration of obligation (haythiyyat al-taklif) is questionable. Response: It is that obedience to the divine ruling is of two ways. One form of obedience to the divine ruling is that belief in its being correct is held regarding that ruling. The second form of obedience is acting according to the requirement of the ruling. So in the ruling of permission, although the demand is conditioned by the will of the obligated person in that the concept of obligation does not occur in the permissible act, nevertheless, belief in its being permissible is obligatory in any case. Therefore, in the ruling of permission, obligation is realized in terms of belief in correctness. The same is the case with recommendation and dislike. Thus, for the recommended, belief in its being recommended is obligatory, and for the disliked act, belief in its being disliked is obligatory. Rather, in both, obligation is also realized from another perspective: that in both (recommended and disliked) there is obligation with a preferred demand (talab tarjihi), in that performing the recommended will be rewarded and committing the disliked will be punished. Second objection: The second objection on considering the mentioned consideration in the definition of ruling is made by Sayyid Muhaqqiq. That Allah's statement 'You and what you worship besides Allah are fuel of Hell' is a threat?
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage deals with objections to the definition of hukm and their answers. The first objection is that verses like 'Allah created you and what you do' (Surah al-Saffat:96) describe Allah's creation of actions but are not demands or options, yet they mention actions of servants. If the definition of hukm is 'address related to actions of mukallaf', such verses would be included, making the definition too broad (dakhul ghayr). The answer: The definition implicitly includes a restriction (qayd) of consideration (haythiyya): it is 'address related to the action of the mukallaf from the perspective that he is a mukallaf' (i.e., from the perspective of obligation). In the cited verses, the action is described as created by Allah, not from the perspective of obligation. So they are not included. Then two objections arise regarding the validity of this restriction. First, Taftazani objects that for acts of ibaha (permission), nadb (recommendation), and karahah (dislike), the consideration of taklif (obligation) is questionable because these do not impose a demand. The author responds that taklif is realized through two forms of obedience: (1) belief in the correctness of the hukm (e.g., believing that a mubah act is indeed permitted) is obligatory; (2) for mandub and makruh, there is a preferential demand (talab tarjihi) which entails reward or punishment, thus involving obligation. Therefore, the condition of haythiyya is valid. The second objection from Sayyid Muhaqqiq concerns a verse about idol worshipers being fuel for hell (Surah al-Anbiya:98) — this seems to be a threat related to actions, but the text breaks off. The intended response likely follows similar reasoning.

Key Terms
حیثیت (haythiyya): الاعتبار أو القيد الذي يخصص الموضوع (من حيث هو مكلف)
تکلیف (taklif): ما فيه كلفة أو مشقة، وهو خطاب الله المتعلق بفعل المكلف اقتضاءً أو تخییراً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to Taftazani's objection that acts of ibaha, nadb, and karahah lack the quality of taklif?
A) He says they are not part of hukm.
B) He argues that taklif consists only of reward and punishment.
C) He explains that taklif is realized through belief in the ruling and preferential demand.
D) He modifies the definition of hukm.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm requires the condition of haythiyya (perspective of obligation) to exclude non-legislative addresses and to affirm that even mubah/nadb/karahah involve taklif through belief and preferential demand.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Defending the Definition of Hukm Against Two Objections
Two objections and their responses to the definition of hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate two objections to the Hanafi definition of hukm and explain how the addition of 'demand or choice' resolves them.

Core Idea
A hukm is an address from the perspective of obligation; reportive verses and verses lacking demand/choice are excluded.

The Hanafi definition of hukm is precise: it is Allah's address related to the action of the responsible person, but only insofar as he is responsible (من حيث هو مكلف). This lesson examines two objections that challenge whether this definition prevents other verses from entering. Through careful analysis of the responses, we see how the definition holds and is refined by including 'demand or choice' to cover all categories.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Definition
Recall the definition: 'خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بفعل المكلف من حيث هو مكلف' (the address of Allah related to the action of the responsible person insofar as he is responsible). Note the key qualifier 'insofar as he is responsible'—this introduces the concept of perspective (haythiyya).
This definition is from the Hanafi school; Mutakallimin define hukm differently.
2
First Objection and Response
Identify the first objection: verses like 'والله خلقكم وما تعملون' are addresses about actions, so they would enter the definition. The response: every definition considers a specific perspective; these verses do not address actions from the perspective of obligation ( taklif ) but as reports. Thus they are excluded.
The response uses the concept of haythiyya (perspective) to maintain preventiveness.
3
Second Objection and Response
Identify the second objection: the verse 'إنكم وما تعبدون من دون الله حصب جهنم' is a threat attached to an action as such, so it should be a hukm, but by consensus it is not. The response: this verse implicitly demands abandonment of worshipping false gods, so it contains an implicit demand (iqtida' damini), making it a hukm.
The response shows that implicit demand is sufficient for a verse to be a hukm.
4
Final Refinement: Demand or Choice
Understand the refinement by Ma'een: adding 'اقتضاء أو تخير' (demand or choice) to the definition. This covers permissibility, recommendation, and disapproval (which involve obligation in belief or preferential demand) and excludes purely reportive verses (like creation verses) that lack both demand and choice.
This refinement makes the definition universally applicable and immune to the objections.
