The Three Roles of Descriptions in Wad'i Rulings
Definition and classification of wad'i rulings into sabab, mani', shart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify wad'i rulings into cause (sabab), preventer (mani'), and condition (shart) based on the description's role, and distinguish temporal from conceptual causes.

Core Idea
A wad'i ruling links a description to a hukm as a cause, preventer, or condition — the same description can play different roles.

In this passage from Muslim al-Thubut, we move from the first kind of legislative address (khatab taklifi) to the second kind (khatab wad'i). The author classifies wad'i rulings into three categories depending on whether the description acts as a cause, preventer, or condition. Understanding this classification is essential for grasping how Shari‘ah attributes affect legal obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the first sentence that lists 'cause' (sabab), 'preventer' (mani'), and 'condition' (shart). Each is a different wad'i ruling about a description of an act or object.
These categories are mutually exclusive in a given context but a description may shift roles.
2
Distinguish temporal vs. conceptual cause
The cause (sabab) is divided into two subtypes: temporal (like the declining sun) and conceptual (like intoxication). Temporal causes are time-based; conceptual causes are intrinsic properties that trigger a ruling.
'Intoxication' itself is not a time but a quality that leads to prohibition.
3
Distinguish types of preventer
The preventer (mani') can block either the ruling directly (e.g., fatherhood prevents retaliation) or the cause of the ruling (e.g., debt prevents zakat from being due). Identify which scenario fits each.
A preventer does not negate the cause; it suspends its effect.
4
Distinguish types of condition
A condition (shart) is required for the ruling itself (e.g., ability to deliver for a valid sale) or for the cause to be effective (e.g., purification for prayer). Recognize the difference.
A condition does not cause the ruling but enables the cause to operate.
5
Map each example to its category
For each example given in the passage (decline of sun, intoxication, fatherhood, debt, ability to deliver, purification), assign the correct wad'i role and subcategory.
Confirm your assignments by re-reading the Arabic phrases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Text of Muslim al-Thubut: 'Then legislative address of the second kind (khatab al-wad') has types: among them is the ruling that a description is a cause (sababiyya), and it is by induction either temporal like the decline of the sun for the obligation of prayer, or conceptual like intoxication for prohibition; among them is the ruling that it is a preventer (mani') either of the ruling like fatherhood in retaliation, or of the cause like debt in zakat; among them is the ruling that it is a condition (shart) for the ruling like ability to deliver in sale, or for the cause like purification in prayer, and its cause is the glorification of the Most High. Memorize this!' Translation: Then the second type of legislative address has several divisions. One division is the ruling that a description is a cause, and by induction it is either temporal, like the decline of the sun for the obligation of prayer, or conceptual, like intoxication for prohibition. Another division is the ruling that a description is a preventer; then the description either prevents the ruling, like fatherhood in retaliation, or prevents the cause, like debt in zakat. Another division is the ruling that a description is a condition for the ruling or for the cause, like ability to deliver the sold item for the validity of sale, and like purification in prayer; and its cause is the glorification of Allah. Memorize this! Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of khatab al-wad' (legislative address of the second kind), also known as wad'i rulings. The matn of Muslim al-Thubut divides wad'i rulings into three categories based on the role of a description (wasf): cause (sabab), preventer (mani'), and condition (shart). The cause is further divided into temporal (like the declining sun causing prayer obligation) and conceptual (like intoxication causing prohibition). The preventer can block either the ruling itself (like fatherhood prevents retaliation) or the cause of the ruling (like debt prevents zakat from being due). The condition can be for the ruling (like ability to deliver is a condition for a valid sale) or for the cause (like purification is a condition for prayer's cause being the command to pray). The commentator notes that this follows the discussion of taklifi rulings and clarifies that wad'i rulings are subsumed under taklifi rulings because hukm includes both. This classification is fundamental in Hanafi usul for understanding how attributes affect legal obligations.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): A cause that directly triggers a ruling; divided into temporal (waqtiyya) and conceptual (ma'nawiyya).
مانع (mani'): A preventer that blocks either the ruling itself or the cause of the ruling.
شرط (shart): A condition that is required for the validity of a ruling or for the effectiveness of a cause.

Wad'i rulings categorize descriptions as causes, preventers, or conditions, each with subtypes, forming the backbone of how rules attach to actions.

Understanding خطاب الوضع: The Declaratory Address
Defines declaratory address and its components

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define خطاب الوضع and distinguish it from خطاب التكليفي by identifying its key features (no explicit implication/choice, indicates a request, establishes relationships).

Core Idea
خطاب الوضع is not a command but a sign — it marks the cause, condition, pillar, or preventer of a directive ruling.

In Hanafi usul, divine address is divided into two fundamental types: declaratory and directive. While directive address directly commands, prohibits, or gives choice, declaratory address sets the stage by establishing the relationships upon which directive rulings depend. This lesson unpacks the definition of خطاب الوضع, clarifying how it functions as a sign of a request rather than the request itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify definition components
Read the definition: 'خطاب الوضع هو خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بافعال المكلفين وضعاً من غير اقتضاء وتخيير صريحاً بل على وجه يدل على تعلق الطلب ويكون علامة عليه'. Identify what is included and what is excluded.
Note the exclusion of explicit implication (اقتضاء صريحي) and explicit choice (تخيير صريحي).
2
Understand the exclusion
Why are explicit implication and explicit choice excluded? Because declaratory address does not directly command or give choice; it only indicates a directive ruling.
Think of it as a signpost pointing to a command, not the command itself.
3
Link to directive rulings
The definition says the address 'indicates the attachment of a request and is a sign of it'. Explain how a cause (e.g., sun's decline) is a sign of the obligation of prayer.
The cause is not the obligation but a marker that the obligation is triggered.
4
List the categories
The passage mentions that declaratory address establishes relationships like cause (سبب), condition (شرط), pillar (ركن), and preventer (مانع). State each and give a fiqh example.
Example: purification is a condition for prayer; impurity is a preventer.
5
Apply to an example
Take the statement 'Recitation is a pillar of prayer'. Explain how this is declaratory address and what directive ruling it points to.
It points to the obligation to recite in prayer, but the statement itself is not a command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقتضاء اقتضاء صریحی ، واقتضاء منی سے عام ہے یا پھر حد حکم میں وضعاً کی قید کا اضافہ کر لیا جائے بہر صورت احکام وضعیہ حکم میں داخل رہینگے ، اس لئے مصنف نے احکام وضعیہ کی تعریف نہ کر کے صرف اسکی تقسیم کی طرف اشارہ کرتے ہوئے کہا ثم خطاب الوضع اصناف الخ۔ قوله "ثم خطاب الوضع اصناف" اس عبارت سے ماتن نے خطاب وضع کی قسموں کو بیان کیا ہے مگر پہلے خطاب وضع کی تعریف ذکر کی جاتی ہے تب تقسیم کا ذکر ہوگا۔ خطاب وضع کی تعریف:۔ یہ کی گئی ہے۔ "خطاب الوضع هو خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بافعال المكلفين وضعاً من غير اقتضاء وتخيير صريحاً بل على وجه يدل على تعلق الطلب ويكون علامة عليه" یعنی خطاب وضعی ، اللہ تعالیٰ کا وہ خطاب ہے جو افعال مکلفین سے بطور وضع متعلق ہو، اقتضاء صریحی یا تغییر صریحی کے طور پر نہ متعلق ہو بلکہ وہ خطاب ایسے طریق پر متعلق ہو جو طلب کے تعلق پر دلالت کرے اور طلب کے لئے علامت بنجائے ۔ بلفظ دیگر خطاب وضع وہ احکام وضعیہ ہوتے ہیں جن کو شارع نے ایک شئی کے ساتھ دوسری شئی کے تعلق کو بیان کرنے کے لئے وضع فرمایا ہو کہ شئی اول شئی ثانی کے لئے مثلا سبب ہے یا شرط ہے یار کن ہے یا مانع ہے وغیرہ جیسے یہ خطاب کہ دلوک وجوب صلوۃ کا سبب ہے ، طہارت صحت نماز کے لئے شرط ہے قرآت نماز کا ایک رکن ہے اور نجاست، نماز سے مانع ہے غرض یہ کہ خطاب وضعی ایک حکم اضافی کا نام ہے جس میں خطاب تکلیفی کی اضافت معتبر ہوتی ہے اس کی چند قسمیں ہیں۔
The implication of an explicit implication is general, or the restriction of 'positionally' is added to the limit of the ruling. In any case, the declaratory rulings remain included in the ruling. Therefore, the author did not define the declaratory rulings but only pointed to their division by saying: 'Then the declaratory address [has] types.' His statement: 'Then the declaratory address [has] types.' By this expression, the author has stated the types of declaratory address, but first the definition of declaratory address is mentioned, then the division will be mentioned. The definition of declaratory address is given: 'The declaratory address is the address of Allah the Exalted that relates to the actions of the legally responsible persons in a positional manner, not by way of explicit implication or explicit choice, but in a manner that indicates the attachment of a request and is a sign of it.' That is, declaratory address is the address of Allah that relates to the actions of the legally responsible persons in a positional manner, not by way of explicit implication or explicit choice, but it relates in a manner that indicates the attachment of a request and becomes a sign for the request. In other words, declaratory address consists of those declaratory rulings that the Legislator has placed to express the relationship of one thing to another, such that the first thing is, for example, a cause, condition, pillar, or preventer, etc. For example, the address that the declining of the sun is a cause for the obligation of prayer, purification is a condition for the validity of prayer, recitation is a pillar of prayer, and impurity is a preventer of prayer. In short, declaratory address is the name of an additional ruling in which the relation of the directive address is considered, and it has several types.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage defines the second major category of divine address in Hanafi usul: خطاب الوضع (declaratory address) as opposed to خطاب التكليفي (directive address). The author explains that declaratory rulings (أحكام وضعية) are not directly commands or prohibitions but rather establish relationships between acts and legal consequences—such as causes, conditions, pillars, and preventers. The definition stresses that declaratory address does not contain explicit implication (اقتضاء صريحي) or explicit choice (تخيير صريحي); rather, it serves as a sign or indicator of a directive ruling. For example, the verse 'Establish prayer at the decline of the sun' (دلوك الشمس) is declaratory in that it sets the decline as a cause for the obligation, not as a command itself. The passage also lists the main categories: cause, condition, pillar, and preventer, which will be elaborated in subsequent sections.

Key Terms
خطاب الوضع (khiṭāb al-waḍ‘): The address of Allah that relates to the actions of the legally responsible persons in a positional manner, indicating a relationship (cause, condition, etc.) without direct command or prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It directly commands or prohibits actions.
B) It establishes a relationship (cause, condition, pillar, preventer) that indicates a directive ruling.
C) It is always explicit and clear.
D) It only applies to acts of worship.

Key Takeaway
خطاب الوضع is the framework of relationships (cause, condition, pillar, preventer) that supports directive rulings, without being a command itself.

Sabab: Temporal and Conceptual Causes
Defines and classifies causes in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sabab (cause) in Hanafi usul, distinguish between sabab waqti and sabab ma'nawi, and identify the Quranic and Sunnah evidence for each type.

Core Idea
A cause is a well-defined attribute indicated by divine law as the means for a ruling.

Usul al-fiqh begins with declaring how rulings are linked to their causes. This passage introduces the first type of declaratory address: that a description is a cause. It defines 'sabab' and, through induction, divides it into two categories: temporal causes tied to time and conceptual causes tied to meaning. Understanding this distinction is essential for deriving rulings from their effective causes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of declaratory address
The passage explains the first type of declaratory address (خطاب وضع): that a description is ruled to be a cause for a legal ruling.
This is foundational to understanding how rulings are linked to their causes.
2
Define 'sabab' (cause) in Hanafi terminology
A cause is a well-defined attribute (وصف منضبط) that the divine law (سمع) indicates as the means for establishing a ruling.
The attribute must be clearly apparent and divinely indicated.
3
Recognize the two subtypes by induction
The passage states that by induction (استقراء) causes are confined to two: temporal (وقتیہ) and conceptual (معنویہ).
This classification is specific to Hanafi usul.
4
Examine the example of temporal cause
The declining of the sun (دلوک الشمس) is a temporal cause for the obligation of Zuhr prayer, supported by Quran 17:78.
Time is the locus (معترف) of the ruling.
5
Examine the example of conceptual cause
Intoxication (اسکار) is a conceptual cause for the prohibition of intoxicants, supported by a hadith from Sahih Muslim.
Conceptual causes are not tied to time but to a meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله منها الحكم على الوصف بالسببية وهى بالاستقراء الخ اس عبارت سے خطاب وضع کی پہلی قسم کو بیان کیا ہے پھر قسم کی قسم کو مع مثال ذکر کیا ہے تفصیل درج ذیل ہے۔ تقسيم وضع : (۱) پہلی قسم " الحكم على الوصف بالسببية“ ہے یعنی کسی شئی کے لئے ایک ایسا وصف ثابت ہو جس پر حکم لگایا جائے کہ وہ وصف اس شئی پر حکم لگائے جانے کا سبب ہے اور سبب اصطلاح میں ایسے وصف منضبط کا نام ہے کہ حکم شرعی کے ثبوت کے لئے جن کے معرف ہونے پر سمع دال ہو ۔ پھر بطور استقرار وہ دو قسموں میں منحصر ہے ۔ ایک سییہ وقتیہ دوسری سب یہ معنویة وقتیہ وقت کی طرف منسوب ہے گویا شارع کی تعریف اور انکے بیان سے ”وقت حکم شرع کا معترف ہے اس لئے اسکو وقعیہ کہتے ہیں جیسے دلوک شمس صلوۃ ظہر کے وجوب کے لئے سب وقعہ ہے چنانچہ اللہ عز شانہ کا ارشاد ہے اقم الصلوۃ لدلوک الشمس اور معنویہ معنی کی طرف منسوب ہے جو وقعیہ کے بالمقال بولا گیا ہے پس معنویہ سے ایسا سبب مراد ہے جو غیر واقعیہ ہے جیسے اسکار حکم تحریم کے لئے سبب معنوی ہے چنانچہ پیغمبر اسلام میں اللہ نے ارشاد فرمایا ہے کل منکر حرام ( رواہ مسلم)
His statement: 'From them is the ruling on the description as causality, and it is by induction etc.' This expression explains the first type of declaratory address, and then the subtype is mentioned with an example. The detail is as follows: Division of the positional: (1) The first type is 'the ruling on the description as causality', meaning that a description is affirmed for something such that it is ruled that this description is a cause for the ruling on that thing. And 'cause' in terminology is the name of a well-defined description that the divine law indicates as a means of the establishment of a legal ruling. Then, by induction, it is confined to two types: one is temporal cause (sabab waqti) and the other is conceptual cause (sabab ma'nawi). Temporal is attributed to time, meaning that time is the locus of the legal ruling, so it is called 'waqti' (temporal). For example, the declining of the sun is a temporal cause for the obligation of the Zuhr prayer, as Allah, whose glory is great, says: 'Establish prayer at the declining of the sun' (17:78). And conceptual is attributed to meaning, as opposed to temporal. So 'conceptual cause' refers to a cause that is not temporal, such as intoxication being a conceptual cause for the ruling of prohibition, as the Messenger of Allah said: 'Every intoxicant is forbidden' (narrated by Muslim).
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage explains the first type of declaratory address: الحكم على الوصف بالسببية (ruling that a description is a cause). A cause (سبب) is defined terminologically as a clearly apparent attribute (وصف منضبط) that the divine law (سمع) indicates as the means for establishing a legal ruling. By induction (استقراء), causes are divided into two: temporal (سبب وقتیہ) and conceptual (سبب معنویہ). Temporal causes are linked to time, which is the locus (معترف) of the ruling; the example given is the declining of the sun (دلوک الشمس) as a cause for the obligation of Zuhr prayer, citing the Quranic verse. Conceptual causes are not tied to time but to a meaning; the example is intoxication (اسکار) as a cause for the prohibition of intoxicants, citing the hadith 'كل مسكر حرام' (though the text has 'كل منكر حرام', which is likely a scribal error). Note that the hadith is from Muslim, indicating a Sahih source. This classification helps in understanding how rulings are linked to their causes in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): A well-defined attribute (وصف منضبط) that the divine law indicates as the means for establishing a legal ruling.
سبب وقتیہ (sabab waqtiyya): A cause that is based on time, such as the declining of the sun being the cause for the obligation of Zuhr prayer.
سبب معنویہ (sabab ma'nawiyya): A cause based on a meaning, not time, such as intoxication being the cause for prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a conceptual cause (سبب معنویہ)?
A) The declining of the sun for Zuhr prayer
B) Intoxication for the prohibition of intoxicants
C) The dawn for Fajr prayer
D) The moon sighting for Ramadan fasting

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a cause (sabab) is a well-defined attribute indicated by revelation, and it is either temporal (linked to time) or conceptual (linked to meaning).

The Preventer (Māni‘): Blocking the Ruling or the Cause
Explains the second type of hukm wad‘ī: māni‘ with two subtypes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between māni‘ li’l-ḥukm and māni‘ li’l-sabab using Hanafi fiqh examples.

Core Idea
A preventer either blocks the ruling or nullifies its cause.

This lesson explores the second type of hukm wad‘ī: the ruling that a description is a preventer (māni‘). The Hanafi jurists divide preventers into two categories: those that block the ruling itself (māni‘ li’l-ḥukm) and those that nullify the cause (māni‘ li’l-sabab). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying many fiqh rules.

Guided Path
1
Define māni‘
Start by defining the term māni‘ in Hanafi usul: a description that prevents either the ruling or its cause from taking effect.
Māni‘ is a type of hukm wad‘ī.
2
Differentiate the two subtypes
Learn that māni‘ li’l-ḥukm blocks the ruling while the cause remains; māni‘ li’l-sabab negates the cause itself.
The two subtypes have different mechanisms and effects.
3
Analyze fatherhood in qisas
Examine the example: fatherhood prevents the ruling of qisas even though the cause (intentional murder) exists. This illustrates māni‘ li’l-ḥukm.
The father is not executed for killing his son.
4
Analyze debt in zakat
Examine the example: debt prevents the nisab from being free of basic needs, thus negating the cause of zakat. This is māni‘ li’l-sabab.
Zakat is not obligatory if nisab is offset by debt.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Try to identify a similar scenario in Hanafi fiqh where a description acts as a preventer and classify it.
For instance, safar (travel) as a preventer of certain obligations? But careful: safar is a sabab for concessions, not a māni‘. Use a standard one like 'being a father' is a māni‘ in qisas.

قوله - ومنها الحكم بكونه مانعاً اما للحكم كالابوة فى الخ درج بالا عبارت میں ماتن نے نطاب وضع کی دوسری قسم کو بیان کیا ہے۔ (۲) دوسری قسم الحکم بکون الوصف مانعا “ ہے یعنی کسی شی ء کے لئے ایک ایسا وصف ثابت ہو جو وصف کہ شئی کے حکم یا سبب حکم کو مانع ہو پس اس اعتبار سے خطاب وضع کی اس قسم کی بھی دو قسمیں ہوتی ہیں۔ ایک تم کون الوصف مانعا للحكم " ہے یعنی وصف صرف علم کو مانع ہوگا ، مانع سب نہ ہوگا بلکہ سیب موجود قسم ہو گا لیکن اس سبب پر حکم مسبب مرتب نہ ہوگا کہ ایسا مانع موجود ہے جو تر تب حکم کو منع کر رہا ہے جیسے بوت (باپ ہونا کسی کا مسئلہ قصاص میں ایک ایسا وصف ہے جو مانع حکم قصاص ہے چنانچہ باپ نے جب اپنے بیٹے کو قتل کر دیا تو قصاص میں باپ کو قتل کرنے کا حکم نہیں دیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ وصف ابوت حکم قصاص کے مانع ہے باوجود یکہ حکم قصاص کا سبب ( قتل عمد ظلما ) موجود ہے۔ دوسری قسم کون الوصف، مانعا للسبب " ہے یعنی وصف سب حکم کو مانع ہو اسطرح کہ اس وصف کے ہوتے ہوئے سبب کی سبیت باقی نہ رہے جیسے دین مسئلہ حکم زکوۃ میں اس لئے کہ شارع نے اس نصاب کو وجوب زکوۃ کا سبب قرار دیا ہے جو نصاب کہ حوائج اصلیہ سے خالی ہو اور اداء دین بھی حوائج اصلیہ میں سے ہے اس لیئے دین کے ہوتے ہوئے گویا وہ نصاب جو سبب وجوب زکوۃا ہے پایا نہیں گیا کیونکہ نصاب حوائج اصلیہ سے فارغ نہیں ہے الغرض وصف دین ، العقاد مب ( نصاب ) ہی سے مانع ہوا اسلئے زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔
His statement: 'And from them is the ruling of it being a preventer, either for the ruling, like fatherhood in [qisas] etc.' In the above phrase, the author has explained the second type of declaratory address. (2) The second type is 'the ruling that the description is a preventer', meaning that a description is affirmed for something such that it prevents the ruling of that thing or the cause of the ruling. Accordingly, this type of declaratory address also has two types. First: the description being a preventer of the ruling (مانع للحكم), meaning the description will prevent only the ruling, not the cause; rather, the cause is present, but the ruling is not applied because there is a preventer that blocks the ruling from occurring. For example, fatherhood in the matter of qisas is a description that prevents the ruling of qisas. If a father kills his son, the father will not be subject to qisas because the description of fatherhood prevents the ruling of qisas, even though the cause (intentional unjust murder) exists. Second: the description being a preventer of the cause (مانع للسبب), meaning the description prevents the cause of the ruling such that the causality of the cause does not remain. For example, debt in the matter of zakat, because the Legislator has made the nisab that is free from basic needs the cause for the obligation of zakat. Since debt is also one of the basic needs, when debt exists, that nisab which is the cause for the obligation of zakat is not found, because the nisab is not free from basic needs. In short, the description of debt prevents the nisab itself, so zakat is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage discusses the second main type of declaratory address: الحكم بكون الوصف مانعا (ruling that a description is a preventer). A preventer is an attribute that either blocks the ruling (مانع للحكم) or blocks the cause itself (مانع للسبب). The first subtype, مانع للحكم, is illustrated with fatherhood (الابوة) in the law of qisas (retributive justice). Even though the cause for qisas exists (intentional murder of the son), the father is exempt from qisas because fatherhood is a preventer of the ruling. This ruling is well-established in Hanafi fiqh: a father is not executed for killing his child. The second subtype, مانع للسبب, is illustrated with debt in zakat. The cause for zakat is possession of nisab beyond basic needs. Debt, being a basic need, prevents the nisab from reaching the threshold; thus, the cause is negated, and zakat is not obligatory. This example shows how a preventer can undermine the very foundation of the ruling. The passage demonstrates the precision of Hanafi usul in categorizing the ways a description can obstruct a legal effect.

Key Terms
مانع (māni‘): A description that prevents either the ruling itself or the cause of the ruling.
مانع للحكم (māni‘ li’l-ḥukm): A preventer that blocks the ruling from being applied even though its cause is present.
مانع للسبب (māni‘ li’l-sabab): A preventer that nullifies the cause itself, so the cause is not considered valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of debt and zakat, what type of preventer is debt?
A) مَانِع لِلْحُكْم (preventer of the ruling)
B) مَانِع لِلسَّبَب (preventer of the cause)
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a preventer (māni‘) can block either the ruling itself (as fatherhood blocks qisas) or the cause of the ruling (as debt negates the nisab for zakat).

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Distinguishing Mani' Hukm from Mani' Sabab
Resolves objection about two subtypes of mani'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a preventer of the ruling (mani' hukm) and a preventer of the cause (mani' sabab) and apply this distinction to examples from Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A preventer can block the ruling directly while the cause remains, or block the cause itself, indirectly preventing the ruling.

In Hanafi usul, the second division of declaratory speech (al-khitab al-wad'i) includes two subtypes of preventer (mani'). The division states that one subtype prevents the ruling directly (mani' hukm) and the other prevents the cause (mani' sabab). An objection arises: the examples of fatherhood preventing qisas and debt preventing zakat both seem to prevent the ruling directly, so what is the difference? This lesson resolves that objection by analyzing the cause in each case, showing that in the debt example the cause itself is absent, making it a preventer of the cause.

Guided Path
1
State the two subtypes of preventer
Identify the two subtypes: preventer of the ruling (mani' hukm) and preventer of the cause (mani' sabab). Understand that in both cases the ruling does not apply, but the mechanism differs.
Mani' hukm blocks the ruling despite the cause being present; mani' sabab blocks the cause, so the ruling never arises.
2
Recognize the objection
The objector notes that in the fatherhood example, the ruling (qisas) is prevented; in the debt example, the ruling (zakat) is also prevented. So both seem to be mani' hukm. Understand why this superficial similarity creates confusion.
The objection assumes that if the ruling is absent, the preventer must act on the ruling. It fails to check whether the cause is present.
3
Analyze the fatherhood example as mani' hukm
The cause of qisas is intentional unjust killing. When a father kills his son, the cause (killing) exists. But the ruling (obligation of qisas) is blocked by fatherhood. So the fatherhood prevents the ruling directly while the cause remains. This is mani' hukm.
The key point: the cause is present, but the ruling is removed. The prevention is on the ruling itself.
4
Analyze the debt example as mani' sabab
The cause of zakat is ownership of nisab free from basic needs. When the owner has debt, the nisab is not free from basic needs because debt repayment is a basic need. Thus the cause does not exist. The debt prevents the existence of the cause. Therefore, the prevention of the ruling is indirect – it is through prevention of the cause. This is mani' sabab.
In this case, the cause is absent, so the ruling is never triggered. The preventer acts on the cause, not the ruling.
5
Summarize the distinction
The distinction hinges on whether the cause remains present. In mani' hukm, the cause exists but the ruling is directly blocked. In mani' sabab, the cause itself is blocked, so the ruling is indirectly prevented. This distinction is essential for correct usul analysis.
Always check the status of the cause: if it exists, the preventer is on the ruling; if it is eliminated, the preventer is on the cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشکال : ۔ خطاب وضع کی دوسری قسم کی دونوں قسموں کے بیان سے ایک قومی انکال لازم آتا ہے وہ یہ کہ وصف ابوت جس طرح حکم قصاص کو مانع ہے اسی طرح وصف دین بھی حکم وجوب زکوۃ کو مانع ہے تو دونوں قسموں میں کوئی فرق نہیں رہا کہ بہر دو صورت وصف مانع حکم ہی ہے جبکہ مقام تقسیم میں کہا گیا ہے کہ صرف اول مانع حکم ہے اور دوم مانع سبب ہے مگر دو مثالوں سے مانع حکم ہی سمجھ میں آتا ہے۔
جواب : کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ وصف ابوت مانع حکم کی مثال ہے اور وصف دین مانع سبب کی مثال ہے اور دونوں میں بین فرق ہے چونکہ مثال اول میں قصاص کا سبب وہ ظلما قتل عمد ہے اور یہ سبب صورت مذکورہ میں حقیقتاً موجود بھی ہے مگر وجو د سبب کے باوجود وصف ابوت نے حکم قصاص کو منع کر دیا، اس کے برخلاف دوسری مثال میں وجوب زکوۃ کا جو سبب ہے کہ نصاب کا حوائج اصلیہ سے خالی ہونا تو یہ سب دین کی وجہ سے موجود نہیں ہے۔ غرض دین نے سب کو سبب ہونے ہی سے منع کر دیا گویا سبب ہی نہیں پایا گیا گو کہ اس صورت میں بھی حکم ممنوع ہے تاہم منع حکم بالذات و بلا واسطہ نہیں ہے بلکہ منع سبب کے واسطہ سے منع حکم ثابت ہے جبکہ اول میں منع حکم بالذات و بلا واسطہ ثابت ہے کیونکہ سبب ممنوع نہیں ہے بلکہ موجود ہے دونوں قسموں اور اسکی مثالوں میں یہی خطا امتیاز ہے۔
توضیح دوم : - مزید توضیح اس طرح بھی کر سکتے ہیں کہ مثال دوم میں دین کی وجہ سے سبب وجوب زکوۃ یعنی نصاب زائل ہو گیا جب کہ مثال اول میں ابوت کی وجہ سے سبب قصاص یعنی ظلما قتل عمد زائل نہیں ہوا بلکہ باقی ہے البتہ اسکا حکم یعنی " وجوب قصاص قرابت وابوت کے سبب زائل ہو گیا غرض ابوت والی مثال میں صرف حکم کا رفع ہے مگر سبب باقی ہے اور دین والی مثال میں سبب اور حکم دونوں کا رفع ہے ہاں منع حکم اولا و بالذات نہیں ہے بلکہ ثانیا اور بالعرض ہے اولاً وبالذات صرف وجود سبب کا رفع ہے اس کے برعکس مثال اول میں وجود حکم کا رفع اولاً وبالذات ہوتا ہے سبب کا نہیں۔ چنانچہ شارع نے قتل کو قصاص کا سبب قرار دیا ہے اپنے ارشاد النفس بالنفس والعین بالعین (الآية ) سے اور اس میں کوئی شبہ نہیں کہ باپ نے اپنے بیٹا کو جب ظلما قتل کر دیا تو سب قصاص خارج میں متفق ہو گیا گو اس کا حکم یعنی وجوب قصاص ، ابوت کے سبب زائل ہو گیا ، اور مثال ثانی میں شارع نے نصاب فارغ عن الحوائج الاصلیہ کو وجوب زکوۃ کا سبب قرار دیا ہے اور جب دین مالک نصاب کے ذمہ میں ثابت ہے تو نصاب حوائج اصلیہ سے فارغ نہ ہوا کہ اداء دین جملہ حوائج میں سے ہے پس دین نے اولاً و بالذات انعقا د سبب ہی کو منع کر دیا ہے اس لئے سبب کے وجود و عدم کے اعتبار سے اس پر حکم مرتب ہوتا ہے۔
Objection: From the explanation of the two types of the second division of declaratory speech, an implication necessarily arises: that the attribute of fatherhood prevents the ruling of qisas, and similarly the attribute of debt prevents the ruling of the obligation of zakat. So there is no difference between the two types; in both cases the attribute prevents the ruling, whereas in the place of division it was said that only the first is a preventer of the ruling and the second is a preventer of the cause. But from the two examples, only a preventer of the ruling is understood.
Answer: The summary is that the attribute of fatherhood is an example of a preventer of the ruling, and the attribute of debt is an example of a preventer of the cause, and there is a clear difference between them. In the first example, the cause of qisas is intentional unjust killing, and this cause is actually present in the mentioned situation, but despite the existence of the cause, the attribute of fatherhood prevented the ruling of qisas. In contrast, in the second example, the cause of the obligation of zakat is that the nisab is free from basic needs. This cause is not present due to debt. In short, debt prevented the cause itself from being a cause, as if the cause did not exist at all. Even though in this case the ruling is also prevented, however the prevention of the ruling is not direct and without mediation, rather the prevention of the ruling is established through the prevention of the cause. While in the first, the prevention of the ruling is direct and without mediation because the cause is not prevented but exists. This is the distinction between the two types and their examples.
Second Clarification: Further clarification can be given that in the second example, due to debt, the cause of the obligation of zakat, i.e., the nisab, is eliminated. Whereas in the first example, the cause of qisas, i.e., intentional unjust killing, is not eliminated due to fatherhood but remains; however its ruling, i.e., the obligation of qisas, is eliminated due to kinship. So in the fatherhood example, only the ruling is removed, but the cause remains. In the debt example, both the cause and the ruling are removed. However, the prevention of the ruling is not primary and direct, but secondary and incidental. The primary and direct removal is only of the existence of the cause. Contrary to this, in the first example, the removal of the existence of the ruling is primary and direct, not the cause. Thus, the Lawgiver established killing as the cause of qisas by His saying 'The soul for the soul, the eye for the eye' (verse), and there is no doubt that when a father kills his son unjustly, the cause of qisas exists externally, although its ruling, i.e., the obligation of qisas, is eliminated due to fatherhood. In the second example, the Lawgiver established the nisab free from basic needs as the cause of the obligation of zakat. When the nisab owner has a debt upon him, the nisab is not free from basic needs because repaying the debt is among basic needs. Thus, debt primarily and directly prevented the occurrence of the cause itself. Therefore, the ruling depends on the existence or non-existence of the cause.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage resolves an objection about the two subtypes of the second type of declaratory speech (al-khitab al-wad'i): the preventer (mani'). The division states that one subtype prevents the ruling (mani' hukm) and the other prevents the cause (mani' sabab). The objection is that both examples (fatherhood preventing qisas, debt preventing zakat) seem to prevent the ruling directly. The commentator clarifies that in the fatherhood example, the cause (intentional murder) exists, but the ruling (qisas) is prevented; thus it is a preventer of the ruling. In the debt example, the cause itself (nisab free from basic needs) does not exist because debt is a basic need; therefore the preventer acts on the cause, not the ruling directly. The second clarification reinforces this: in the debt case, both cause and ruling are absent, but the primary prevention is of the cause; in the fatherhood case, only the ruling is absent. The passage uses rational reasoning (talil) to uphold the division.

Key Terms
مانع حکم (mani' hukm): A preventer that directly blocks the ruling while the cause remains present.
مانع سبب (mani' sabab): A preventer that blocks the cause itself, indirectly preventing the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of a father killing his son, why is the attribute of fatherhood considered a preventer of the ruling (mani' hukm)?
A) Because the cause of qisas is not present.
B) Because the ruling of qisas is directly prevented despite the cause being present.
C) Because both the cause and the ruling are prevented.
D) Because the father is not legally responsible.

Key Takeaway
A preventer can either block the ruling directly while the cause remains (mani' hukm) or block the cause itself, indirectly preventing the ruling (mani' sabab); always check the existence of the cause.

The Condition (Shart) as a Declaratory Ruling
Defines the third type of hukm wad'i: shart and its two subtypes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shart li'l-hukm and shart li'l-sabab, and apply the Hanafi usul definition of shart to given examples.

Core Idea
A condition is a description whose absence prevents the ruling—but it may prevent the ruling directly or indirectly via the cause.

In Hanafi usul, the declaratory ruling (hukm wad'i) includes three types: sabab, mani', and shart. This lesson unpacks the third type, shart, and its two subtypes. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly tracing how conditions affect rulings and their causes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of shart
The passage defines shart as a description that is in the position of a condition; its absence prevents the ruling or the cause. Note that the condition itself is a declaratory ruling, not a ruling of obligation.
Shart is categorized under hukm wad'i, not hukm taklifi.
2
Distinguish the two subtypes
First subtype: shart li'l-hukm (condition for the ruling) directly affects the ruling's validity. Example: seller's ability to deliver is a condition for the validity of the sale. Second subtype: shart li'l-sabab (condition for the cause) affects the cause, which then affects the ruling indirectly.
The second subtype is unique to Hanafi usul and reflects a deeper causal chain.
3
Analyze the example of purification for prayer
The passage uses purification (tahara) for prayer. Prayer is the cause of exalting Allah. Purification is a condition for the cause (exaltation), not just for the ruling (validity of prayer). Without purification, exaltation is inconceivable, so the cause fails.
This shows that the condition can be attached to the cause rather than the ruling directly.
4
Apply the definition to new cases
Consider other examples: A condition like 'witnesses' for a valid marriage—is it a condition for the ruling or for the cause? In Hanafi fiqh, witnesses are a condition for the validity of marriage (shart li'l-hukm). Contrast with purification which is shart li'l-sabab.
Practice identifying which subtype applies based on the causal chain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولم ومنها الحكم بكونه شرطاً للحكم كا لقدرة على التسليم الخ
درج بالا عبارت میں خطاب وضع کی تیسری اور آخری قسم کو بیان کیا ہے۔
(۳) تیسری قسم " الحکم بکون الوصف شرطاً " ہے یعنی کسی شئی کے لئے ایک ایسا وصف ثابت ہو کہ وہ وصف اس شئی پر حکم لگانے کے لیے شرط کی منزل میں ہو بایں طور کہ شرط کا عدم مانع حکم ہو، اس قسم کی بھی دو قسمیں ہیں۔
پہلی قسم ۔ کون الوصف شرحا للحکم یعنی وصف صحت حکم کے لئے شرط ہو جیسے صحت بیچ کے لئے بائع کو مبیع کی سپردگی کی قدرت ہونا شرط ہے اس مثال میں صحت بیع حکم ہے اور بائع کو مبیع پر سپردگی کی قدرت ہونا وصف ہے جو انعقاد بیع کے لئے شرط ہے ورنہ وصف ( یعنی شرط قدرت ) حکم بیع کو معدوم کر دے گا
اور دوسری قسم کون الوصف شرطا للسبب ہے یعنی وصف سبب کے لئے شرط ہو بایں طور کہ وصف کا عدم سبب کی سبت سے مانع ہو نہ کہ صرف حکم کو منع کرے جیسے طہارت نماز کے لئے چنانچہ نماز میں طہارت شرط ہے وہ محض اس لئے کہ نماز تعظیم باری تعالیٰ کا سبب ہے غرض طہارت محض نماز (مسبب) کیلئے شرط نہیں بلکہ تعظیم (سب) باری تعالیٰ کے لئے شرط ہے کیونکہ بغیر طہارت تعظیم متصور نہیں ہوتی۔
اس مثال میں طہارت ایسا وصف ہے جو شرط کی منزل میں ہے اور صحت صلوۃ حکم ہے مگر طہارت صحت صلوۃ کے لئے صرف شرط نہیں بلکہ صلوٰۃ کا جو سبب ہے یعنی تعظیم باری تعالیٰ اس کے لئے بھی شرط ہے اس مفہوم کو ماتن نے اپنے قول کو نہ شرطا للسبب كالطهارة في الصلوة وسبها تعظیم البارى تعالیٰ سے تعبیر کیا ہے۔
وهم : حکم وضعی کی تقسیم کے مقام میں یہ وھم ہو سکتا ہے کہ حکم وضعی کو تین قسموں سبب ، مانع ،
His saying: 'And among them is the ruling that a description is a condition for the ruling, like the ability to deliver, etc.'
In the above passage, the third and last division of declaratory speech is explained.
(3) The third division is 'the ruling that a description is a condition', i.e., that a description is established for something such that that description is in the position of a condition for placing the ruling on that thing, in the sense that the absence of the condition is a preventer of the ruling. This division also has two types.
The first type: The description is a condition for the ruling, i.e., the description is a condition for the validity of the ruling. For example, for the validity of a sale, the seller's ability to deliver the sold item is a condition. In this example, the validity of the sale is the ruling, and the seller's ability to deliver the sold item is the description that is a condition for the contract of sale. Otherwise, the description (i.e., the condition of ability) would nullify the ruling of the sale.
The second type: The description is a condition for the cause, i.e., the description is a condition for the cause, in the sense that the absence of the description prevents the cause, not merely prevents the ruling. Like purification for prayer. Indeed, in prayer, purification is a condition, solely because prayer is the cause of exalting Allah Almighty. In short, purification is not merely a condition for prayer (the effect), but rather it is a condition for exalting (the cause) Allah Almighty, because without purification, exaltation is inconceivable.
In this example, purification is a description that is in the position of a condition, and the validity of prayer is the ruling, but purification is not merely a condition for the validity of prayer; rather, it is also a condition for the cause of prayer, i.e., exalting Allah Almighty. The author (matn) expressed this meaning in his statement: 'rather a condition for the cause, like purification in prayer and its cause is exalting Allah Almighty'.
An illusion: In the place of dividing declaratory rulings, this illusion may occur: that declaratory rulings are three types: cause, preventer,
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage explains the third and final type of declaratory speech (al-khitab al-wad'i): the condition (shart). The commentator expands on the matn's definition. The third type is 'the ruling that a description is a condition'. This means that for a given thing, a description is established that acts as a condition for applying the ruling to that thing. The absence of that condition prevents the ruling. This type is further divided into two subtypes. The first subtype is when the description is a condition for the ruling itself, like the seller's ability to deliver being a condition for the validity of the sale. If the seller cannot deliver, the sale is not valid. The second subtype is when the description is a condition for the cause, not just the ruling. For example, purification (tahara) is a condition for prayer. Prayer is the cause of exalting Allah. Purification is a condition for the cause (exaltation) because without purification, exaltation is not possible. Thus, purification is a condition for the cause, not merely for the effect (prayer). The author used the example of purification in prayer and its cause being exaltation. The passage ends with a note about a possible illusion regarding the three types: cause, preventer, and condition.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A description that is in the position of a condition; its absence prevents the ruling or the cause.
شرط للسبب (shart li'l-sabab): A condition that is required for the cause to be effective, e.g., purification for the cause of prayer (exaltation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Passages example of purification for prayer, why is purification considered a condition for the cause rather than just for the ruling?
A) Because purification is not required for the validity of prayer.
B) Because prayer is the cause of exalting Allah, and purification is a condition for that exaltation.
C) Because purification directly causes the prayer to be valid.
D) Because purification is a condition for the contract of sale.

Key Takeaway
The shart in Hanafi usul has two subtypes: one directly for the ruling and one for the underlying cause, which is essential for correctly analyzing conditions in fiqh rulings.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Shart in Hanafi Usul: Two Subdivisions and Refutation of a Fourth Type
Definition and defense of shart as a wad'i ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two subdivisions of shart (condition) in Hanafi wad'i rulings and explain why true cause (illah haqiqiyyah) does not form a separate fourth type.

Core Idea
Shart is either for the ruling itself or for its cause; true cause is a sabab in reality.

This passage from the commentary on Musallam al-Thubut defines the third wad'i ruling — a condition (shart). The author presents two subdivisions: a condition for the ruling (e.g., ability to deliver for sale) and a condition for the cause (e.g., purity for prayer). Then, an objection is raised: why not include true cause (illah haqiqiyyah) as a fourth type? The answer clarifies the Hanafi distinction between sabab and illah, showing that all causes used in qiyas are actually identifiers (sabab), not true efficient causes. This preserves the threefold division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third type of wad'i ruling
The passage calls it 'the ruling that a description is a condition' (al-hukm bi-kawn al-wasfi shartan). Recognize that shart is a wad'i ruling that makes the existence of another ruling or cause dependent on it.
Shart is defined by its absence preventing the ruling, not by its presence causing it (that is sabab).
2
Distinguish the two subdivisions of shart
First: shart li al-hukm (condition for the ruling itself) – e.g., seller's ability to deliver conditions the validity of sale. Second: shart li al-sabab (condition for the cause) – e.g., purity is a condition for the cause of prayer (glorification). Identify the examples given and the reasoning.
In the second, the absence of purity prevents the cause (glorification) from being valid, thereby also preventing the ruling.
3
Understand the objection of a fourth type
Someone might argue that true cause (illah haqiqiyyah) is a separate wad'i ruling because it has real effect, unlike sabab which is only an identifier. This would break the threefold division (sabab, maniʿ, shart).
The objector assumes illah haqiqiyyah is not included in sabab.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentator defines sabab as the identifier/manifestation of a ruling, and illah as that which has real effect. But in Shariʿah, real effect is solely Allah's. Therefore, what is called 'illah in qiyas is actually a sabab (a manifest sign), not a true cause. Hence, it falls under sabab, not a new type.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle: causes in Shariʿah are not efficient causes but signs.
5
Confirm the threefold division
Since apparent causes are included in sabab, the three types (sabab, maniʿ, shart) are exhaustive. The author's limitation (hagr) is valid.
This refutation shields the Hanafi classification from the objection.

Source Text

درج بالا عبارت میں خطاب وضع کی تیسری اور آخری قسم کو بیان کیا ہے۔
(۳) تیسری قسم " الحکم بکون الوصف شرطاً " ہے یعنی کسی شئی کے لئے ایک ایسا وصف ثابت ہو کہ وہ وصف اس شئی پر حکم لگانے کے لیے شرط کی منزل میں ہو بایں طور کہ شرط کا عدم مانع حکم ہو، اس قسم کی بھی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ پہلی قسم ۔ کون الوصف شرحا للحکم یعنی وصف صحت حکم کے لئے شرط ہو جیسے صحت بیچ کے لئے بائع کو مبیع کی سپردگی کی قدرت ہونا شرط ہے اس مثال میں صحت بیع حکم ہے اور بائع کو مبیع پر سپردگی کی قدرت ہونا وصف ہے جو انعقاد بیع کے لئے شرط ہے ورنہ وصف ( یعنی شرط قدرت ) حکم بیع کو معدوم کر دیے گا اور دوسری قسم کون الوصف شرطا للسبب ہے یعنی وصف سبب کے لئے شرط ہو بایں طور کہ وصف کا عدم سبب کی سبت سے مانع ہو نہ کہ صرف حکم کو منع کرے جیسے طہارت نماز کے لئے چنانچہ نماز میں طہارت شرط ہے وہ محض اس لئے کہ نماز تعظیم باری تعالیٰ کا سبب ہے غرض طہارت محض نماز (مسبب) کیلئے شرط نہیں بلکہ تعظیم (سب) باری تعالیٰ کے لئے شرط ہے کیونکہ بغیر طہارت تعظیم متصور نہیں ہوتی۔
اس مثال میں طہارت ایسا وصف ہے جو شرط کی منزل میں ہے اور صحت صلوۃ حکم ہے مگر طہارت صحت صلوۃ کے لئے صرف شرط نہیں بلکہ صلوٰۃ کا جو سبب ہے یعنی تعظیم باری تعالیٰ اس کے لئے بھی شرط ہے اس مفہوم کو ماتن نے اپنے قول کو نہ شرطا للسبب كالطهارة في الصلوة وسبها تعظیم البارى تعالیٰ سے تعبیر کیا ہے۔
وهم : حکم وضعی کی تقسیم کے مقام میں یہ وھم ہو سکتا ہے کہ حکم وضعی کو تین قسموں سبب ، مانع ، اور شرط میں منحصر کرنا صحیح نہیں کیونکہ حکم وضعی کی چوتھی قسم ملت حقیقیہ بھی پائی جاتی ہے جس کو بھٹی کے وجود میں بڑا دخل ہے اور علت حقیقیہ چونکہ سب کا غیر ہوتی ہے اس لئے علت حقیقہ سبب میں داخل نہیں ہو سکتی پس حکم وضعی کی چار قسمیں ہونی چاہئے ۔
جواب : ازالہ دھم سے پیشتر سبب وعلت کا معنی جاننا ضروری ہے اس لئے پہلے دونوں کی تعریف ذکر کی جاتی ہے۔
سبب : حکم شرعی کے معرف و مظہر کا نام اصطلاح میں سبب ہے یعنی وجود سبب کے وقت مسبب کے وجود کی معرفت ہوتی ہے اور سبب کے عدم سے مسبب کا عدم سمجھا جاتا ہے۔ علت : اسکو کہتے ہیں جس کو وجود معلول میں تاثیر ہو اس حیثیت سے کہ اگر علت نہ ہو تو فی الواقع معلول کا وجود متنع رہے گا۔
سبب وعلت کا معنی جاننے کے بعد یہ جاننا چاہئے کہ تمام اشیاء میں در حقیقت تاثیر صرف اور صرف اللہ سبحانہ تعالیٰ کی ہے اس کے باوجود اللہ نے عالم کو عالم اسباب و علل قرار دیا ہے کہ مسببات اپنے اسباب کے ساتھ اور احکام اپنے عمل کے ساتھ مربوط و منسلک رہتے ہیں۔
لہذا علت اسکار مثلاً نسبت کرتے ہوئے تحریم کی طرف اور اسی طرح تمام علل جو باب قیاس میں معتبر ہیں وہ در حقیقت ملل حقیقیہ نہیں ہیں بلکہ وہ معرفات بالحقیقہ یعنی حکم شرعی کے مظہر ہیں۔ حاصل جواب وہم یہ ہے کہ حکم وضعی میں علت حقیقیہ داخل نہیں ہے اور جو بظاہر علت معلوم ہوتی ہے وہ حقیقت میں علت نہیں ہے بلکہ مظہر ہے جو سبب ہی میں داخل ہے جب حکم وضعی کی قسموں میں ایک قسم کو سبب قرار دے دیا گیا تو علت ظاہرہ سبب ہی میں داخل ہوگئی لہذا اخطاب وضع کی قسموں کو تین میں منحصر کرنا صحیح ہے غرض حصر مصنف فاسد نہ ہوا ۔۱۲

His statement: 'And among them is the ruling that it is a condition for the ruling, like the ability to deliver, etc.' The above sentence explains the third and last type of wad'i (stipulative) address. (3) The third type is 'the ruling that a description is a condition', meaning that for something a description is established such that this description is in the status of a condition for applying the ruling to that thing, in the sense that the absence of the condition prevents the ruling. This type also has two divisions. First division: the description being a condition for the ruling, i.e., the description is a condition for the validity of the ruling, like the seller's ability to deliver the sold item being a condition for the validity of the sale. In this example, the validity of the sale is the ruling, and the seller's ability to deliver the sold item is the description which is a condition for the contract of sale; otherwise, the description (i.e., the condition of ability) would nullify the ruling of sale. The second division: the description being a condition for the cause, i.e., the description is a condition for the cause, in the sense that the absence of the description prevents the cause itself, not merely the ruling, like purity (taharah) for prayer. For indeed, purity is a condition in prayer, not merely because prayer is a cause for glorification of Allah Almighty; rather, purity is not merely a condition for the prayer (the effect) but for the glorification (the cause) of Allah Almighty, because without purity, glorification is inconceivable. In this example, purity is a description that is in the status of a condition, and the validity of prayer is the ruling, but purity is not merely a condition for the validity of prayer, but also for the cause of prayer, i.e., the glorification of Allah; this meaning the author expressed by his statement: 'Like purity in prayer and its cause is glorification of Allah Almighty.' Objection: In the context of dividing wad'i rulings, it may be imagined that confining wad'i rulings to three types — cause, preventer, and condition — is not correct, because there is also a fourth type of wad'i ruling: the true cause, which has a great effect on the existence of things, and since the true cause is other than a cause (sabab), it cannot be included in the cause. Therefore, wad'i rulings should be four types. Answer: Before removing the doubt, it is necessary to know the meaning of cause (sabab) and true cause (illah). Therefore, the definitions of both are mentioned first. Sabab: In terminology, it is the identifier and manifestation of a Shari'ah ruling, meaning that at the time of the sabab's existence, the existence of the effect (musabbab) is known, and from the absence of the sabab, the absence of the effect is understood. Illah: It is that which has an effect on the existence of the effect in the sense that if the illah were not present, the existence of the effect would actually be prevented. After understanding the meaning of sabab and illah, it should be known that in all things, real effect is solely from Allah, the Glorified and Exalted. Nevertheless, Allah has made the world a world of causes and effects, such that effects are connected and linked to their causes, and rulings to their acts. Therefore, when we attribute effect to the illah, like the prohibition, and similarly all the illahs that are considered in the chapter of qiyas are not true causes (illah haqiqiyyah) in reality, but rather they are true identifiers, i.e., manifestations of the Shari'ah ruling. The gist of the answer to the objection is that true cause is not included in wad'i rulings, and what appears to be a cause is not a cause in reality but a manifestation, which is included in the sabab. Since one of the types of wad'i rulings has been designated as sabab, the apparent cause becomes included in the sabab. Therefore, confining the types of wad'i address to three is correct; thus, the author's limitation is not flawed. So praise be to Allah and gratitude, and blessings upon the best of mankind, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the third type of wad'i (stipulative) ruling: the ruling that a description is a condition. The commentator explains that this type has two subdivisions: (1) the description being a condition for the ruling itself (shart li al-hukm), like the seller's ability to deliver being a condition for the validity of the sale; and (2) the description being a condition for the cause (shart li al-sabab), like ritual purity (taharah) being a condition for prayer because the cause of prayer is glorification of Allah, which requires purity. Then the commentator addresses a potential objection that there should be a fourth type: the true cause (illah haqiqiyyah). The response clarifies the difference between sabab (cause in the sense of identifier/manifestation) and illah (true cause with real effect). In Shari'ah, what is called 'illah in qiyas is actually a sabab (manifestation), not a true cause. True effect belongs only to Allah. Therefore, the apparent illah is included under sabab, so the threefold division (sabab, mani', shart) remains valid. The commentator concludes that the author's limitation (hagr) is correct.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The identifier and manifestation of a Shari'ah ruling; its existence indicates the existence of the effect.
علة (illah): The true cause that has actual effect on the existence of the effect; in Shari'ah, only Allah has true effect.
شرط (shart): A description that is necessary for a ruling or its cause; its absence prevents the ruling or cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason that a true cause (illah haqiqiyyah) does not form a separate fourth type of wad'i ruling?
A) Because it is actually a condition (shart), not a cause.
B) Because it is a preventer (mani') in disguise.
C) Because real causation belongs only to Allah, and what appears as a cause in Shari'ah is actually a sabab (manifestation) included under sabab.
D) Because the author did not include it in his classification, so it is incorrect by default.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi threefold division of wad'i rulings (sabab, mani', shart) is exhaustive; apparent causes are sabab, not a separate type, because true efficient causation belongs to Allah alone.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Sabab vs. Illah: Defending the Three-Fold Division of Hukm Wad'i
Defends three types of hukm wad'i by distinguishing sabab from real illah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sabab and illah haqiqiyyah in Hanafi usul and apply that distinction to defend the three-fold classification of hukm wad'i.

Core Idea
For a mufti, the 'illah of qiyas is merely an indicator (mazhar), not a real cause—so it belongs to sabab.

In this passage, the commentator defends the classical Hanafi position that declaratory rulings (ahkam wad'iyyah) are only three: sabab, shart, and mani'. The opponent argues that the real cause ('illah haqiqiyyah) should be a fourth type because it influences the existence of the effect. The response begins by clearly defining sabab and illah, then shows that any 'illah used in qiyas is actually an indicator (mazhar), not a real cause. Real causality belongs exclusively to Allah. Therefore, the apparent 'illah falls under sabab, and the three-fold division stands intact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The opponent claims that a real cause (illah haqiqiyyah) exists and has influence, so it must be a fourth type of hukm wad'i. Why would this seem plausible? Because in everyday language, causes produce effects.
2
Define sabab terminologically
The author defines sabab as the identifier and indicator (mu'arraf wa mazhar) of a ruling. Its presence makes us know the ruling exists; its absence makes us know the ruling does not exist. It does not create the ruling.
Sabab is a mere indicator, not a producer.
3
Define illah haqiqiyyah
Illah haqiqiyyah is that which, if it were absent, the effect would be impossible. It has real causal influence.
This is the real cause.
4
Understand the theological premise
In reality, all causal power is from Allah alone. He has arranged the world as a web of causes and effects, but the real cause (mu'aththir) is only Allah.
No created thing is a real cause.
5
Reclassify legal 'illah as sabab
The 'illah used in qiyas (e.g., intoxication as the cause of prohibition) is not a real cause but an indicator. Therefore, it fits under the definition of sabab. Hence, no fourth type is needed.
Legal 'illah is a mazhar, subsumed under sabab.

Source Text

جواب : ازالہ وہم سے پیشتر سبب وعلت کا معنی جاننا ضروری ہے اس لئے پہلے دونوں کی تعریف ذکر کی جاتی ہے۔
سبب : حکم شرعی کے معرف و مظہر کا نام اصطلاح میں سبب ہے یعنی وجود سبب کے وقت مسبب کے وجود کی معرفت ہوتی ہے اور سبب کے عدم سے مسبب کا عدم سمجھا جاتا ہے۔
علت : اسکو کہتے ہیں جس کو وجود معلول میں تاثیر ہو اس حیثیت سے کہ اگر علت نہ ہو تو فی الواقع معلول کا وجود ممتنع رہے گا۔
سبب وعلت کا معنی جاننے کے بعد یہ جاننا چاہئے کہ تمام اشیاء میں در حقیقت تاثیر صرف اور صرف اللہ سبحانہ تعالیٰ کی ہے اس کے باوجود اللہ نے عالم کو عالم اسباب و علل قرار دیا ہے کہ مسببات اپنے اسباب کے ساتھ اور احکام اپنے عمل کے ساتھ مربوط و منسلک رہتے ہیں۔
لہذا علت اسکار مثلاً نسبت کرتے ہوئے تحریم کی طرف اور اسی طرح تمام علل جو باب قیاس میں معتبر ہیں وہ در حقیقت علل حقیقیہ نہیں ہیں بلکہ وہ معرفات بالحقیقہ یعنی حکم شرعی کے مظہر ہیں۔ حاصل جواب وہم یہ ہے کہ حکم وضعی میں علت حقیقیہ داخل نہیں ہے اور جو بظاہر علت معلوم ہوتی ہے وہ حقیقت میں علت نہیں ہے بلکہ مظہر ہے جو سبب ہی میں داخل ہے جب حکم وضعی کی قسموں میں ایک قسم کو سبب قرار دے دیا گیا تو علت ظاہرہ سبب ہی میں داخل ہوگئی لہذا اخطاب وضع کی قسموں کو تین میں منحصر کرنا صحیح ہے غرض حصر مصنف فاسد نہ ہوا ۔
And confining it to condition is not correct, because the fourth type of declaratory ruling, the real cause, also exists, which has great influence in the existence of the effect. And since the real cause is other than everything, therefore the real cause cannot enter into the cause (sabab). So the declaratory ruling should have four types. Answer: Before removing the doubt, it is necessary to know the meaning of sabab and illah. Therefore, the definition of both is mentioned first. Sabab: In terminology, sabab is the name for the identifier and indicator of a legal ruling. That is, at the time of the existence of the sabab, there is knowledge of the existence of the musabbab (effect), and from the absence of the sabab, the absence of the musabbab is understood. Illah: It is called that which has effect in the existence of the effect (ma'lul) in the sense that if the illah were not there, the existence of the effect would actually be impossible. After knowing the meaning of sabab and illah, it should be known that in all things, in reality, effect belongs solely to Allah Almighty. Despite that, Allah has made the world a world of causes and effects, such that effects are connected and linked with their causes, and rulings with their actions. Therefore, the illah in qiyas, for example, relating prohibition, and similarly all illahs that are valid in the chapter of qiyas, in reality they are not real causes, but rather they are identifiers (mu'arrafat) in reality, i.e., indicators of the legal ruling. The summary of the answer to the doubt is that the real cause is not included in the declaratory ruling, and whatever appears as an illah is in reality not an illah but rather an indicator, which is included in sabab. When one type of declaratory ruling was designated as sabab, the apparent illah entered into the sabab. Therefore, confining the types of declaratory rulings to three is correct. In short, the author's limitation is not invalid.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection against the author's (of Muslim al-Thubut) classification of declaratory rulings (ahkam wad'iyyah) into three types: sabab, shart, and mani'. The objector claims that a fourth type, the real cause ('illah haqiqiyyah), should be added because it has a distinct effect on the existence of the ruling's object. The author's response begins by defining sabab and illah. Sabab is defined as an identifier (mu'arraf) and indicator (mazhar) of a ruling: its presence indicates the presence of the effect, and its absence indicates the absence of the effect. Illah is defined as that which has real causal influence (ta'thir) such that without it, the effect would necessarily be non-existent. However, the author clarifies that in Islamic theology, all true causal influence belongs to Allah alone. What appears as 'illah in legal reasoning (qiyas) is not a real cause but rather an indicator (mazhar) that signals the ruling. Therefore, these apparent causes are actually subsumed under sabab. Thus, the real cause is not part of the categories of hukm wad'i, and the three-fold division—sabab, shart, mani'—remains correct. The author's use of 'illah here distinguishes between the real ontological cause and the legal indicator that the Hanafis call 'illah in qiyas.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): An identifier (mu'arraf) and indicator (mazhar) of a legal ruling; its presence signals the presence of the effect (musabbab) and its absence signals the absence of the effect.
علت (illah): That which has real causal influence (ta'thir) on the existence of the effect; if it were absent, the effect would be impossible. In legal context, this real cause is not within the categories of hukm wad'i; what is called 'illah in qiyas is actually a mazhar (indicator).
حکم وضعی (hukm wad'i): A declaratory ruling that posits something as a cause, condition, or preventer of another ruling. The author restricts it to three types: sabab, shart, and mani'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the real cause ('illah haqiqiyyah) not included in the categories of hukm wad'i?
A) Because it has no effect on rulings.
B) Because real causality belongs only to Allah, so it cannot be a legal category.
C) Because it is subsumed under shart.
D) Because it is not defined in the text.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi three-fold division of hukm wad'i (sabab, shart, mani') is preserved by recognizing that any 'illah used in qiyas is merely an indicator (mazhar) and thus a sabab, not a real cause.
